284	per-(kind, key) state-change suppression and per-kind repeat cadence.
285
286	`SMTP2GO_API_KEY` is injected via systemd `EnvironmentFile=/etc/mwan/secrets.env`
287	rather than templated into `config.toml`. This secret-handling contract is also
288	documented in [docs/ansible/secrets.md](../ansible/secrets.md).
289
290	In-flight plan and full routing detail: see
291	[docs/plans/mwan-email-routing.plan.md](../plans/mwan-email-routing.plan.md).
292
293	## Tracing
294
295	MWAN scripts emit structured JSON logs to `/var/log/mwan-debug.log` when
296	`mwan_debug_logging: true`. Each log line includes a `traceId` so events
297	across `systemd-networkd`, `networkd-dispatcher`,
298	[update-routes.sh](../../mwan/scripts/update-routes.sh),
299	[update-npt.sh](../../mwan/scripts/update-npt.sh), and `health-check` can be
300	correlated.
301
302	Trace ID sources:
303
304	- `mwan-trace-boot.service` writes `/run/mwan-trace-id` and
305	  `/var/lib/mwan/trace-id` at boot.
306	- The deploy playbook writes the same files at the start of deploy.
307
308	Quick check on MWAN:
309
310	```bash
311	cat /run/mwan-trace-id
312	tail -n 200 /var/log/mwan-debug.log
313	```
314
315	## Operational quick reference
316
317	On MWAN:
318
319	```bash
320	ssh root@mwan.home.goodkind.io
321	wpa_cli status
322	systemctl status wpa_supplicant-mwan systemd-networkd networkd-dispatcher \
323	  nftables mwan-health cloudflared
324	mwan health-check --status
325	/usr/local/bin/mwan-debug
326	```
327
328	IPv6 sanity checks:
329
330	```bash
331	ip -6 route show table 100
332	ip -6 route show table 200
333	ip -6 rule show
334	nft -a list chain ip6 nat postrouting
335	nft -a list chain ip6 nat prerouting
336	```
337
338	For troubleshooting AT&T 802.1X, Webpass DHCP, virtio-serial wedges,
339	OPNsense REST behaviour, and the upgrade-snapshot pitfalls, see
340	[docs/opnsense/operational-notes.md](../opnsense/operational-notes.md).

1	# MWAN Go standards
2
3	Standards for Go code under [mwan/go/](../../mwan/go/). Violations block merge.
4	See [docs/mwan/overview.md](overview.md) for the runtime architecture and
5	[docs/mwan/script-style.md](script-style.md) for shell and OPNsense conventions.
6
7	## Monolith contract
8
9	All Go infrastructure code lives in one binary built from
10	[mwan/go/cmd/mwan/](../../mwan/go/cmd/mwan/). The linux/amd64 build is `mwan` on targets and `mwan-linux` in
11	[mwan/go/bin/](../../mwan/go/bin/) on the local host. The freebsd/amd64 build is `mwan-opnsense` and runs only on OPNsense,
12	where it auto-dispatches into the `opnsense` daemon based on `argv[0]`.
13
14	Subcommands (as defined in [mwan/go/cmd/mwan/main.go](../../mwan/go/cmd/mwan/main.go)):
15
16	- `mwan agent` runs the gRPC agent (vsock + TCP) inside the MWAN VM. Source:
17	  [mwan/go/internal/agent/](../../mwan/go/internal/agent/).
18	- `mwan watchdog` runs the connectivity and rollback daemon. Source:
19	  [mwan/go/internal/watchdog/](../../mwan/go/internal/watchdog/).
20	  `mwan watchdog failover` is the BGP-aware failover variant.
21	- `mwan ifmgr` runs the per-host interface manager. Role is read from
22	  `[ifmgr].role` in `/etc/mwan/config.toml`. Source:
23	  [mwan/go/internal/ifmgr/](../../mwan/go/internal/ifmgr/).
24	- `mwan health-check` is a one-shot probe. Source:
25	  [mwan/go/internal/healthcheck/](../../mwan/go/internal/healthcheck/).
26	- `mwan opnsense` is the FreeBSD config daemon (config.xml mutation over
27	  virtio serial). Reached via the explicit subcommand or by invoking the
28	  binary as `mwan-opnsense`. Source:
29	  [mwan/go/internal/opnsense/](../../mwan/go/internal/opnsense/).
30	- `mwan opnsense version` probes the OPNsense daemon through a configured
31	  gRPC target.
32	- `mwan opnsense host serve` runs the Proxmox host-side Unix socket bridge to
33	  the OPNsense VM's `mwanrpc` chardev.
34
35	There are no separate Go binaries. New tools become subcommands of this
36	monolith.
37
38	Shared code lives under
39	[mwan/go/internal/config/](../../mwan/go/internal/config/),
40	[mwan/go/internal/email/](../../mwan/go/internal/email/),
41	[mwan/go/internal/logging/](../../mwan/go/internal/logging/),
42	[mwan/go/internal/ops/](../../mwan/go/internal/ops/),
43	[mwan/go/internal/bgp/](../../mwan/go/internal/bgp/),
44	[mwan/go/internal/alert/](../../mwan/go/internal/alert/),
45	[mwan/go/internal/tracing/](../../mwan/go/internal/tracing/),
46	[mwan/go/internal/mwn1/](../../mwan/go/internal/mwn1/), and
47	[mwan/go/internal/rollback/](../../mwan/go/internal/rollback/).
48
49	## Code standards
50
51	- **Single TOML config.** All subcommands read `/etc/mwan/config.toml`. No
52	  env-var-based config loading. Env vars override secrets only
53	  (`SMTP2GO_API_KEY`, `PVE_TOKEN_SECRET`).
54	- **No globals.** Config is passed explicitly through function arguments. No
55	  package-level `var` for config, state, or singletons.
56	- **DRY.** No duplicated structs, no bridge or adapter types that mirror another
57	  struct field-by-field. If two things need the same data, they share one type.
58	- **Small files.** No file over 500 lines. If a file exceeds this, split by
59	  responsibility.
60	- **Separated concerns.** Config loading, business logic, I/O, and CLI parsing
61	  live in separate files. No function that parses flags and runs business logic
62	  at the same time.
63	- **One email sender.** One `EmailSender` type, parameterized at construction.
64	  No per-subcommand email implementations.
65	- **One logger factory.** One `newLogger()` function parameterized by
66	  subcommand name, log paths, and an optional email handler. No per-subcommand
67	  logger setup files.
68	- **No hardcoded values.** IPs, paths, timeouts, email addresses, and hostnames
69	  come from TOML config. Validation errors loudly when a required field is
70	  missing.
71	- **Comments explain why, not what.** Do not add comments that restate the
72	  code. Do not add `// Foo does X` when the function name already says X.
73	- **Secrets in Ansible Vault.** TOML templates use `{{ vault_* }}` Jinja2
74	  variables. Never commit plaintext secrets. The `.j2` suffix signals a
75	  template. Full vault contract in [docs/ansible/secrets.md](../ansible/secrets.md).
76	- **Linting enforced.** `make lint` (golangci-lint) must pass. Config in
77	  [mwan/go/.golangci.yml](../../mwan/go/.golangci.yml).
78	## Build rules
79
80	Every implementation agent or person making changes must:
81
82	- **Start from evidence.** Read the relevant source before changing code.
83	- **Respect the boundary.** Generic layers stay generic. Provider-specific or
84	  platform-specific behaviour lives behind the provider boundary. Preserve
85	  exact user-visible values unless an external boundary requires escaping or
86	  translation.
87	- **Implement real behaviour.** Wire features into the real runtime path, not
88	  only into tests or fallback code. Prefer one source of truth over
89	  compatibility crutches. Reconcile related state immediately when the
90	  user-facing contract says values should stay in sync.
91	- **No shortcuts.** No baseline edits to hide lint findings. No `//nolint`
92	  without explicit operator authorisation. No synthetic references, dummy
93	  logs, or marker-method calls to satisfy reachability tools. No no-op closers
94	  or empty lifecycle methods. No compile-only or log-only tests presented as
95	  behavioural coverage.
96	- **Tight types.** Avoid `any`, `interface{}`, and loose maps unless required
97	  at a real external boundary. Convert untyped input to concrete types as
98	  early as possible.
99	- **Useful tests.** Test the real contract. Add regression coverage for the
100	  failure mode that motivated the change. Avoid tests that only prove
101	  compilation, only log output, or assert implementation trivia.
102	- **Verify before reporting.** Run the project's real gates: `make check`,
103	  `make test`, `make build-linux`, `make build-mwan-opnsense`. State exactly
104	  what was run and whether it passed. If a gate could not be run, state why.
105	- **Report honestly.** State what changed, the verification commands, and any
106	  residual risks. Do not claim files, symbols, commits, or behaviour that
107	  was not verified.
108

[tool: Read] {"file_path":"/Users/agoodkind/Sites/configs.wt-ifmgr-scaffold/docs/mwan/script-style.md"}
[tool output]
1	# MWAN and OPNsense script style
2
3	Working rules for shell scripts and Ansible templates under
4	[mwan/scripts/](../../mwan/scripts/),
5	[ansible/playbooks/](../../ansible/playbooks/), and the OPNsense daemon
6	deployment. Live host topology lives in [docs/infra/mwan-layout.md](../infra/mwan-layout.md)
7	and [docs/infra/opnsense.md](../infra/opnsense.md). Go code rules live in
8	[docs/mwan/go-standards.md](go-standards.md).
9
10	## SSH and host access
11
12	Use jump hosts explicitly when the environment requires it (for example, when
13	the controller cannot reach a testbed IPv6 directly). Disable strict host key
14	checking only for automation or diagnostics:
15
16	```bash
17	ssh -o StrictHostKeyChecking=no -o UserKnownHostsFile=/dev/null ...
18	```
19
20	Prefer non-disruptive actions on the MWAN VM. Avoid
21	`systemctl restart systemd-networkd` unless necessary.
22
23	## Deterministic convergence (no races)
24
25	- Scripts and services must be idempotent and tolerate partial boot ordering.
26	- Any script that mutates shared kernel state must be serialized with a lock:
27	  use `flock` against a lock file in `/run/...` for `ip rule`, `ip route`, and
28	  `nft` writers.
29	- When a service can run before prerequisites are ready, gate it with an
30	  `ExecStartPre` wait script and add `Restart=on-failure` with retries.
31
32	## Jinja and templating strategy
33
34	- Do not keep a `.j2` file if it contains no Jinja (no `{{`, no `{%`, no
35	  `{#}`). Use a normal extension and deploy with `ansible.builtin.copy`.
36	- If a shell script, hook, or service only uses templating to inject
37	  variables, prefer one templated env file (for example `/etc/mwan/mwan.env`)
38	  and make the script static. Source the env via `. /etc/mwan/mwan.env`. For
39	  systemd units, prefer `EnvironmentFile=/etc/mwan/mwan.env`.
40
41	## WAN state terminology
42
43	Use **healthy / unhealthy / unknown** for WAN health. Do not use **up / down**
44	for health, because that conflicts with `ip link` state semantics.
45
46	## Logging and JSON
47
48	- Prefer structured JSON logs to `/var/log/mwan-debug.log`.
49	- Use `jq -cn` for JSON generation; avoid `printf`-built JSON.
50	- Avoid embedded Python for JSON generation or parsing.
51	- Include `traceId` in logs when available (`MWAN_TRACE_ID`).
52
53	## Parsing and tooling preferences
54
55	- Prefer machine-readable outputs:
56	  - `ip -j ... | jq` over `ip ... | awk/sed`.
57	  - `networkctl ... --json=short | jq` over text parsing.
58	  - `ipcalc-ng --all-info -j ... | jq` over bespoke IPv6 math.
59	  - `nft -j` for inspection where feasible.
60	- Avoid long pipe trains like `... | grep ... | tail -1 | awk ... | awk ...`.
61	  Prefer a single-pass `awk` program (track `last=...` and print in `END`) or
62	  capture output to local variables.
63	- Keep scripts portable across Debian base utilities (avoid GNU-only flags
64	  unless already assumed or installed).
65
66	## jq usage
67
68	- Use `jq` for selection, extraction, and light reshaping.
69	- Avoid algorithmic formatting in `jq` (for example, converting a byte array
70	  into an IPv6 literal). Move that to a small shell helper.
71
72	## ipcalc-ng helper patterns
73
74	If you find yourself repeating `ipcalc-ng ... | jq -r '.NETWORK'`, factor it
75	into a helper such as `ipcalc_field <cidr> <jq_field>` and
76	`ipcalc6_field <cidr> <jq_field>`. Keep long command substitutions readable
77	with multi-line `$( ... )`.
78
79	## Shell style and safety
80
81	- Use `set -euo pipefail` for scripts that mutate state.
82	- Use `|| true` only at expected failure points (best-effort probes or
83	  cleanup).
84	- Source constant paths directly (`. /etc/mwan/mwan.env`) to keep shellcheck
85	  happy; avoid unused `ENV_FILE` variables.
86	- Keep lines reasonably short; wrap long `{ ... }` blocks with newlines after
87	  `{`.
88	- For every MWAN script or hook, include a top comment block describing what
89	  it does (symptoms plus technical effect) and where it sits in the dependency
90	  graph.
91
92	## Console auto-login
93
94	- Physical console access (keyboard plus VGA, or serial) auto-logs in as root
95	  without a password.
96	- SSH access requires normal authentication (password or key).
97	- Configuration uses systemd getty service overrides:
98	  - `getty@tty1`: `--autologin root --noclear %I $TERM`.
99	  - `serial-getty@ttyS0`: `--autologin root --keep-baud 115200,57600,38400,9600 - ${TERM}`.
100	- Idempotent deployment: Ansible handles directory creation; systemd reloads on
101	  reboot.
102
103	## nftables and runtime rules
104
105	Assume an `nftables` reload flushes runtime rules. Any dynamic runtime rule
106	programming (for example NPT) must be re-applied via:
107
108	- `networkd-dispatcher` hooks, and
109	- a boot or deploy safety-net systemd unit.
110
111	## Documentation constraints
112
113	- Do not add new docs unless asked.
114	- When updating existing docs, avoid giant pasted code blocks; prefer short
115	  excerpts and direct pointers to files.
116	- When you encounter and fix issues, document them in
117	  [docs/opnsense/operational-notes.md](../opnsense/operational-notes.md) using
118	  the established format.
119

[tool: Read] {"file_path":"/Users/agoodkind/Sites/configs.wt-ifmgr-scaffold/docs/mwan/dscp-wan-pinning.md"}
[tool output]
1	# Pinning a device or app to one WAN via DSCP
2
3	Status: design plus manual PoC. Not deployed. Captured 2026-06-15.
4
5	## Why this exists
6
7	Hulu shows a "location changed" notification when its flows load-balance across
8	WANs, because each WAN egresses a different ISP IP (AT&T `104.57.226.x`, Webpass
9	`136.25.91.x`, Monkeybrains `158.247.70.x`) and Hulu reads the account as hopping
10	networks. The first fix was destination-IP pinning via the `att_pinned_v4/v6`
11	nftables sets (see [overview.md](overview.md) and
12	`ansible/inventory/group_vars/mwan_servers.yml`). A live capture on 2026-06-15
13	showed that approach loses to Hulu's CDN: Hulu sprays video segments across
14	Akamai, Fastly, and CloudFront `/24`s (and v6 `/64`s) faster than the 6h refresh
15	can track, so new rotated IPs keep leaking to the load-balanced WAN.
16
17	The durable fix is to stop classifying by destination and instead carry a
18	classification signal from OPNsense (which sees the device and the DNS) across
19	the routed hop to mwan, then pin on that signal. DSCP is the one piece of
20	metadata that survives a plain routed hop.
21
22	## What mwan can and cannot see (verified live)
23
24	Checked against `/proc/net/nf_conntrack` and `conntrack -L` on the mwan VM:
25
26	- IPv4: mwan sees `src=10.250.250.2` for every LAN flow. OPNsense source-NATs all
27	  IPv4 LAN clients to its `10.250.250.2` edge before handing traffic to mwan
28	  (consistent with the masquerade rule matching only `ip saddr 10.250.250.0/29`
29	  in `mwan/config/nftables.conf.j2`). So mwan cannot tell v4 devices apart by
30	  source, and a v4 source pin at mwan would pin all LAN v4 traffic.
31	- IPv6: mwan sees the real client `/128` (e.g. `3d06:bad:b01:2:9121:f8:be06:8f4a`)
32	  because the internal `3d06:bad:b01::/60` is routed end to end with no NAT. A v6
33	  source pin at mwan works, though SLAAC privacy addresses rotate, so pin a
34	  device `/64` (its own VLAN) rather than a single `/128`.
35
36	This split is why OPNsense-side tagging is required for v4: OPNsense is the only
37	node that sees the real `10.250.2.x` client.
38
39	## How to set DSCP on OPNsense (verified in source)
40
41	OPNsense can only SET DSCP through legacy scrub/normalization rules:
42
43	- `opnsense-core-25.7/src/etc/inc/filter.inc:534` emits `set-tos <value>` from
44	  `$config['filter']['scrub']['rule']`. Live on 26.1.9 the same line is
45	  `filter.inc:555`, and the GUI field is `firewall_scrub_edit.php:580`
46	  ("TOS / DSCP").
47	- Allowed values come from `get_tos_values()` (filter.inc:781-807): named
48	  (`lowdelay`, `ef`, ...), `af11`-`af43`, `cs0`-`cs7`, and raw hex `0x00`-`0xFF`.
49	- The MVC firewall filter-rule `tos` field (`Filter.xml`, `TosField.php`) and the
50	  Traffic Shaper `dscp` field are MATCH-only, not set. There is no ipfw
51	  `setdscp`. So scrub `set-tos` is the only set primitive.
52
53	Scrub runs before OPNsense's outbound NAT, so a scrub rule can match the real
54	v4/v6 client source, stamp a codepoint, and the bits ride through the NAT to
55	mwan.
56
57	## Automation reach (verified in source)
58
59	- The `opnsense-go` REST client cannot do this: its `Filter` struct has no
60	  `tos`/`dscp` field (`opnsense-go/pkg/firewall/filter.go:21-39`), and it
61	  implements no traffic-shaper or scrub resource.
62	- The configs stack does not use that REST client. It drives OPNsense through the
63	  `mwan-opnsense` gRPC daemon over virtio-serial, which mutates `config.xml` via
64	  `XPathSet`/`XPathGet`/`XPathDelete` plus `Exec`
65	  (`mwan/go/internal/opnsense/rpc_typed.go:71-170`, `docs/mwan/overview.md`).
66	  Scrub rules live at `config.xml` `filter/scrub/rule`, so that daemon can
67	  program the tag with `XPathSet` and a filter reload. It currently only touches
68	  BGP, gateways, and upgrades, so this would be a new use of an existing
69	  mechanism.
70
71	## Design
72
73	Chosen codepoint: CS1 (DSCP 8, ToS byte `0x20`), a scavenger-class value nothing
74	else here uses. nft accepts `ip dscp cs1`; OPNsense scrub stores `set-tos` as
75	`cs1`.
76
77	### OPNsense half (scrub set-tos)
78
79	One Normalization rule per family (or one rule with an alias holding both
80	addresses): match the streaming device source, set TOS/DSCP to `cs1`. Config
81	shape under `config.xml` `filter/scrub/rule`:
82
83	```
84	interface = lan
85	proto     = any
86	src       = <streaming-device-ip-or-alias>
87	dst       = any
88	set-tos   = cs1
89	descr     = Tag streaming device for AT&T pin
90	```
91
92	### mwan half (nft ip dscp)
93
94	In `mwan/config/nftables.conf.j2`, `table inet mangle` / `chain prerouting`,
95	right after the existing `@att_pinned` rules (currently lines 207-208) and before
96	the v6 numgen load-balancer and the `ct state established,related` restore:
97
98	```
99	# Pin DSCP-tagged app traffic (set by OPNsense scrub set-tos) to AT&T (mark 1).
100	ip dscp cs1 meta mark set 1
101	ip6 dscp cs1 meta mark set 1
102	```
103
104	This works for both families because the inet mangle chain (priority mangle)
105	runs before the IPv4 numgen load-balancer in `table ip nat` (priority dstnat),
106	so the mark is set before the `meta mark 0` guard there skips it. The existing
107	postrouting `ct mark set meta mark` and the prerouting `ct state
108	established,related meta mark set ct mark` carry the mark across the rest of the
109	flow, identical to how `att_pinned` behaves today.
110
111	## GUI-guided PoC (manual, about 10 minutes, no code deploy)
112
113	This proves the path end to end before any Ansible or daemon work.
114
115	1. Identify the streaming device LAN addresses. On the mwan VM during playback,
116	   the device's v6 appears as the conntrack source for Hulu flows (for example
117	   `3d06:bad:b01:2:9121:f8:be06:8f4a`); its v4 is its DHCP lease on OPNsense.
118	2. OPNsense, optional alias: Firewall > Aliases > Add, type Host(s), name
119	   `streaming_device`, add the device v4 and v6. Apply.
120	3. OPNsense scrub rule: Firewall > Settings > Normalization > Add.
121	   - Interface: the LAN the device is on.
122	   - Protocol: any.
123	   - Source: `streaming_device` (or the device IP). Leave invert off.
124	   - Destination: any.
125	   - TOS / DSCP: `cs1`.
126	   - Description: `Tag streaming device for AT&T pin`.
127	   - Save, then Apply changes.
128	4. mwan, live nft rules (PoC only, reverted on next nft reload):
129	   ```
130	   nft add rule inet mangle prerouting ip dscp cs1 ct state new meta mark set 1
131	   nft add rule inet mangle prerouting ip6 dscp cs1 ct state new meta mark set 1
132	   ```
133	   These append to the chain. `ct state new` marks fresh flows; established flows
134	   are restored from ct mark by the existing rule, so append order is safe for a
135	   PoC. The permanent placement is after the `@att_pinned` rules as shown above.
136	5. Restart Hulu on the device (so flows are new), then watch egress on the mwan
137	   VM. A simple watcher over `conntrack -L` filtered to Hulu destinations should
138	   show `mark=1` regardless of which CDN IP Hulu rotates to, since the pin now
139	   keys on DSCP, not destination.
140
141	If it works, promote it: add the two nft lines to `nftables.conf.j2`, and either
142	keep the scrub rule in OPNsense config or program it from `mwan-opnsense` via
143	`XPathSet` into `filter/scrub/rule`.
144
145	## Verification
146
147	- Confirm the tag survives to mwan: on the mwan VM, `conntrack -L` Hulu flows
148	  show `mark=1`; before the change they split between `mark=1` and `mark=2`.
149	- Confirm the device egresses AT&T: its public IP as seen by an IP-echo service
150	  while streaming should be in the AT&T `104.57.226.x` range.
151	- Confirm no collateral: only the tagged device should change WAN; other LAN
152	  traffic still load-balances.
153
154	## Caveats
155
156	- It is config.xml, not the REST API. Automating it means the `mwan-opnsense`
157	  XPath path, which has not yet been used for firewall rules; verify the daemon
158	  can insert a rule subtree, not just scalar values, before relying on it.
159	- Verify nothing else re-normalizes ToS to 0 between OPNsense and mwan (a quick
160	  live capture settles this).
161	- Pick a codepoint not otherwise in use. CS1 (`0x20`) is the assumed free value
162	  here; confirm no Traffic Shaper or other consumer keys on it.
163	- This pins the whole device, which is the intended "blunt" behavior. For
164	  app-only granularity on a shared device, OPNsense would still need a per-app
165	  classifier, which inherits the same shared-CDN problem.
166

1	# Infrastructure overview
2
3	This directory is the point-in-time infrastructure snapshot for `goodkind.io`.
4	Treat every IP address, route, bridge, and service state here as potentially
5	stale, because these files are not a live feed.
6
7	Use this directory for current state and inventory-shaped facts. Use

47	## AT&T ONT access
48
49	The AT&T ONT is a Realtek-based GPON SFP ("ONT-on-a-stick", firmware
50	`V1.0-220923`) presented to MWAN as a Layer-2 device on the untagged
51	parent `enatt0`. MWAN reaches its management plane at `192.168.1.1` over
52	that link.
53
54	- Credentials: stock vendor defaults for this Humax SFP unit. Not stored in the repo. Operator memory or the Humax operator doc.
55	- SSH: dropbear 0.48, requires legacy KEX, host key, and cipher.
56	- Telnet: also open on port 23.
57
58	SSH command (from MWAN, replace `<user>` and supply the password interactively):
59
60	```bash
61	ssh -o StrictHostKeyChecking=no -o UserKnownHostsFile=/dev/null \
62	  -o KexAlgorithms=+diffie-hellman-group1-sha1 \
63	  -o HostKeyAlgorithms=+ssh-rsa \
64	  -o Ciphers=+3des-cbc \
65	  <user>@192.168.1.1
66	```
67
68	Useful binaries on the ONT: `ShowStatus`, `pondetect`, `checkomci`,
69	`omci_app`, `omcicli`, `oamcli`. Useful `/proc` entries: `/proc/omci`,
70	`/proc/fiber_debug`, `/proc/fiber_mode`, `/proc/internet_flag`. The
71	device has a small connection limit and wedges its SSH/telnet daemons
72	when hit rapidly; keep to one connection at a time and `reboot` over
73	SSH if both daemons stop responding while TCP accepts succeed.
74
75	## AT&T 802.1X chain on MWAN
76
77	The MWAN VM holds AT&T's certificates and runs `wpa_supplicant` directly,
78	with the ONT acting only as a Layer-2 EAPOL forwarder. The bring-up chain:
79
80	1. `wpa_supplicant-mwan.service` runs the supplicant against the parent
81	   `enatt0` interface using certs at
82	   `/etc/wpa_supplicant/{ca_cert,client_cert,private_key}.pem`.
83	2. On reaching the AUTHENTICATED state, `wpa-cli-action.service` writes
84	   `/run/wpa_supplicant-mwan.authenticated`.
85	3. `wpa-authenticated.path` watches that file and starts
86	   `wpa-authenticated.service`, which then starts
87	   `bringup-att-vlan.service`.
88	4. `bringup-att-vlan.sh` polls `wpa_cli status` until AUTHENTICATED, then
89	   runs `networkctl renew enatt0.3242` to trigger DHCPv4 + DHCPv6-PD on
90	   the VLAN sub-interface.
91	5. DHCPv4 yields the AT&T public address. DHCPv6-PD yields the AT&T
92	   delegated `/60` used by `update-npt.sh`.
93
94	Failure modes:
95
96	- **`wpa-authenticated.path` in `failed (unit-start-limit-hit)`**: the
97	  path triggered `bringup-att-vlan` too many times in a row at boot.
98	  Clear with `systemctl reset-failed wpa-authenticated.path` then
99	  `systemctl start wpa-authenticated.path`.
100	- **TLS handshake completes but AT&T returns `EAP-Failure`**: AT&T's
101	  RADIUS rejected our cert identity. The supplicant port may stay
102	  `Authorized` from the initial boot auth, but DHCP gets no replies
103	  because the RADIUS session is invalid. Reboot the ONT
104	  (`reboot` over SSH at `192.168.1.1`) to clear AT&T's session state;
105	  the ONT comes back in ~30s and re-presents EAPOL, triggering a fresh
106	  RADIUS session.
107	- **`Supplicant PAE state=AUTHENTICATING` with `wpa_state=COMPLETED`**:
108	  re-authentication failing in the background. Same recovery as above.
109
110	Diagnostic commands on MWAN:
111
112	```bash
113	ls -la /run/wpa_supplicant-mwan.authenticated
114	ls -la /etc/wpa_supplicant/*.pem
115	sudo wpa_cli -i enatt0 status
116	journalctl -u wpa_supplicant-mwan --no-pager --since "1 hour ago"
117	journalctl -u bringup-att-vlan --no-pager --since "1 hour ago"
118	networkctl status enatt0.3242
119	```
120	| `enmbrains0` | Monkeybrains | `158.247.70.6/26` (public) | SLAAC `2607:f598:d3e0:131::/64` (no PD) | 5000 (tertiary) | RA restored. DHCPv6-PD not delegated (provider-side). NAT66 masquerade fallback active. IPv4 upgraded from CG-NAT to public. |

83	## Testbed-only infrastructure
84
85	ISP LXCs 200/201/202, suburban-side safe IPv6 sysctl defaults, and suburban
86	masquerade rules (`vmbr1` to `vmbr0`/`wg0`) only exist on the testbed. The
87	bridge shape stays in OpenTofu, the safe early-boot sysctl defaults stay in
88	[ansible/playbooks/deploy-testbed.yml](../../ansible/playbooks/deploy-testbed.yml),
89	and the live per-bridge Router Advertisement policy is reconciled continuously by
90	`mwan-ifmgr` from the suburban host config rendered by the Proxmox host tasks.
91
92	## Suburban gotchas
93
94	These are suburban-specific facts that differ from vault and cost time when
95	unknown.
96
97	- **Cloud-init drive storage.** `local-lvm` is disabled on suburban; only
98	  `local-zfs` is active. Guest `initialization.datastore_id` must be `local-zfs`,
99	  or a cloud-init drive regen fails with `storage 'local-lvm' is not available`.
100	- **`args` ownership.** VMs with a virtio-serial or vsock device (VM 950, VM 101)
101	  carry their `args` set by Ansible as `root@pam`, because the Proxmox API rejects
102	  `args` writes from a token. OpenTofu must not manage `kvm_arguments` for those
103	  VMs (`lifecycle.ignore_changes = [kvm_arguments]`), or a plan tries to null the
104	  field and the apply fails with `VM is locked`. See
105	  [docs/opnsense/operational-notes.md](../opnsense/operational-notes.md) Rule 8.
106	- **Management return path.** VM 950 management has no policy route, mirroring
107	  prod, so on-link replies to peers on the `204::` services LAN return directly.
108	  A management policy table carrying only a default route shadows the connected
109	  route and triangles on-link replies through the gateway, which breaks
110	  reachability.
111	- **Reachability probing.** The testbed OPNsense blocks ICMP echo to LAN hosts
112	  but allows TCP, so measure reachability with TCP or SSH, not `ping6`, or a
113	  healthy host reads as down.
114	- **Watchdog host config address.** `mwan-watchdog-testbed` on the suburban host
115	  must target VM 950's current management address (`204::950`) in
116	  `/etc/mwan/config.toml`. A stale address degrades its VM health probe to the
117	  TCP and PVE fallback channels (the vsock channel still works because it is
118	  CID-based), and a wedged snapshot plus a tight retry loop can hold the VM lock.
119	  The config is rendered by `deploy-proxmox --limit suburban`.
120
### Assistant (2026-07-06 21:03)
[tool: Read] {"file_path":"/Users/agoodkind/Sites/configs.wt-ifmgr-scaffold/docs/infra/network.md"}
[tool output]
1	# Networking and DHCP diagnosis
2
3	IPv6 connectivity is P0. Treat IPv6 issues as critical priority and diagnose the
4	IPv6 stack first, then IPv4. See [docs/infra/overview.md](overview.md) for the
5	current live network state and [docs/infra/access.md](access.md) for SSH paths
6	between hosts.
7
8	## Configuration preferences
9
10	- Prefer IPv6 literals over IPv4 in configuration files and bindings:
11	  `[::1]` rather than `127.0.0.1`, `[::]` rather than `0.0.0.0`.
12	- When verifying connectivity (SSH, curl, etc.), test the IPv6 address first.
13
14	## DHCPv6 reservation matching in KEA
15
16	### Root cause: DUID instability
17
18	Containers and VMs sometimes get a different IPv6 address than the
19	MAC-based reservation specifies. The usual cause is that the client's DUID
20	changes.
21
22	systemd-networkd generates DUIDs that can change:
23
24	- `DUIDType=vendor` (default) is derived from `/etc/machine-id` and changes when
25	  the container is recreated.
26	- `DUIDType=link-layer` is derived from the MAC and is stable if the MAC is
27	  pinned.
28	- `DUIDType=uuid` is derived from the product UUID and may change.
29
30	Two related problems compound the DUID issue:
31
32	- When DUID changes, KEA creates new leases but the old ones remain active and
33	  conflict with the new ones.
34	- Without `host-reservation-identifiers` matching the actual identifier used in
35	  reservations, KEA never prioritises MAC-based matching.
36
37	### KEA configuration principles
38
39	Three knobs control reservation matching.
40
41	`mac-sources` tells KEA how to extract a MAC address from DHCPv6 packets:
42
43	- `"duid"` extracts the MAC from a DUID-LL (format `00:03:00:01:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX`).
44	- `"ipv6-link-local"` extracts the MAC from the EUI-64 link-local address.
45	- `"client-link-addr-option"` uses option 79 if provided by a relay agent.
46
47	`host-reservation-identifiers` controls which identifier types KEA checks and
48	in what order. The reservation's identifier must be in this list, otherwise it
49	will not match.
50
51	Per-reservation identifier types:
52
53	- `duid` matches the DUID directly and requires a stable DUID.
54	- `hw-address` matches the MAC and requires that MAC extraction works.
55
56	Decision tree:
57
58	1. Is the DUID stable for a given MAC?
59	   - DUID-LL: use `duid` in the reservation,
60	     `host-reservation-identifiers: ["duid", "hw-address"]`.
61	   - DUID changes: use `hw-address` in the reservation and make sure
62	     `mac-sources` can extract the MAC.
63	2. Can the MAC be extracted at all?
64	   - DUID-LL (`00:03:00:01:...`): `mac-sources: ["duid"]` works.
65	   - DUID-EN (`00:02:...`): `mac-sources: ["duid"]` does not work. Use
66	     `["ipv6-link-local"]` or `["client-link-addr-option"]`.
67	   - Other formats: typically need `["ipv6-link-local"]` or a relay agent.
68
69	### Required systemd-networkd configuration
70
71	```ini
72	[DHCPv6]
73	DUIDType=link-layer
74	```
75
76	This produces a DUID-LL of `00:03:00:01:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX` where the last six
77	bytes are the MAC. DUID-LL is stable as long as the MAC is pinned. If the MAC
78	changes, the DUID changes.
79
80	## Diagnosis workflow
81
82	### 1. Inspect container or VM state
83
84	```bash
85	ssh root@<host> "ip -6 addr show eth0"
86	ssh root@<host> "networkctl status eth0 | grep -i duid"
87	ssh root@<host> "ip link show eth0 | grep -i link/ether"
88	```
89
90	### 2. Inspect KEA leases
91
92	```bash
93	ssh <kea-host> "sudo cat /var/db/kea/kea-leases6.csv | grep -i '<mac>'"
94	```
95
96	The [kea/Rakefile](../../kea/Rakefile) provides higher-level helpers, for
97	example `rake lease:get6_by_ip[<ip>]` and
98	`rake lease:cleanup6_by_mac[<mac>]`.
99
100	### 3. Identify DUID instability
101
102	Look for multiple different DUIDs for the same MAC:
103
104	- DUID-EN format `00:02:00:00:XX:XX:...` is machine-id based and unstable.
105	- DUID-LL format `00:03:00:01:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX` is MAC based and stable.
106
107	### 4. Inspect KEA configuration
108
109	```bash
110	grep -A 2 "host-reservation-identifiers" /path/to/kea-dhcp6.conf
111	grep "mac-sources" /path/to/kea-dhcp6.conf
112	```
113
114	### 5. Clean up stale leases
115
116	By MAC, when DUID has changed:
117
118	```bash
119	cd /path/to/bind-kea
120	rake lease:cleanup6_by_mac[<mac>,<subnet_id>]
121	```
122
123	By DUID, when you have a specific DUID:
124
125	```bash
126	rake lease:cleanup6_conflicts[<duid>,<subnet_id>]
127	```
128
129	By IP, when the wrong IP is known:
130
131	```bash
132	rake lease:delete6_by_ip[<ip>]
133	```
134
135	### 6. Renew DHCP on the client
136
137	```bash
138	ssh root@<host> "systemctl restart systemd-networkd"
139	# or
140	ssh root@<host> "networkctl renew eth0"
141	```
142
143	### 7. Verify the reservation is honoured
144
145	```bash
146	ssh root@<host> "ip -6 addr show eth0 | grep 'scope global'"
147	ssh <kea-host> "sudo cat /var/db/kea/kea-leases6.csv | grep '<expected-ip>'"
148	```
149
150	## Common issues
151
152	### Container gets a different IP each time
153
154	1. Check DUID stability:
155
156	   ```bash
157	   ssh root@<host> "networkctl status eth0 | grep -i 'DUID:'"
158	   ssh <kea-host> "cat /var/db/kea/kea-leases6.csv | grep '<mac>' \
159	     | awk -F',' '{print $2}' | sort -u"
160	   ```
161
162	2. Identify the DUID format:
163	   - `00:02:...` is DUID-EN (machine-id based, unstable across recreations).
164	   - `00:03:00:01:...` is DUID-LL (MAC based, stable if the MAC is pinned).
165	   - `00:04:...` is DUID-UUID (may change).
166	3. Determine root cause:
167	   - DUID changes: check `DUIDType` in systemd-networkd config.
168	   - MAC changes: check Proxmox or VM config for MAC pinning.
169	   - Multiple DUIDs exist: stale leases from previous DUID formats.
170	4. Fix at the source: configure `DUIDType=link-layer`, pin the MAC in the
171	   hypervisor config, or clean up the conflicting leases.
172
173	### Reservation exists but is not honoured
174
175	1. Verify the reservation:
176
177	   ```bash
178	   grep -A 5 "reservations" /path/to/kea-dhcp6.conf
179	   grep "host-reservation-identifiers" /path/to/kea-dhcp6.conf
180	   ```
181
182	2. Check the client identifier:
183
184	   ```bash
185	   ssh root@<host> "networkctl status eth0 | grep -i 'DUID:'"
186	   ssh root@<host> "ip link show eth0 | grep -i link/ether"
187	   ```
188
189	3. Check active leases:
190
191	   ```bash
192	   ssh <kea-host> "cat /var/db/kea/kea-leases6.csv | grep '<mac-or-duid>'"
193	   ```
194
195	4. Identify the mismatch:
196	   - Reservation uses `hw-address` but the client sends DUID-EN, so no MAC is
197	     extractable.
198	   - Reservation uses `duid` but the DUID format changed.
199	   - Multiple active leases with different identifiers for the same MAC.
200	   - `host-reservation-identifiers` does not include the identifier type used.
201	5. Fix at the source: update the reservation or `host-reservation-identifiers`,
202	   clean up conflicting leases, or change `mac-sources`.
203
204	### Multiple active leases for the same MAC
205
206	Root cause: the DUID changed over time and created multiple lease entries.
207
208	```bash
209	rake lease:cleanup6_by_mac[<mac>,<subnet_id>]
210	```
211
212	## Last resort: hardcoded DUID
213
214	Only use when the root cause cannot be fixed. If a DUID continues to change
215	despite `DUIDType=link-layer`, you can hardcode it:
216
217	1. Read the current DUID:
218
219	   ```bash
220	   ssh root@<host> "networkctl status eth0 | grep -i 'DUID:'"
221	   ```
222
223	2. Extract the raw DUID without the type prefix. DUID-LL is
224	   `00:03:00:01:bc:24:11:1d:2c:0f` and the raw MAC-based portion is
225	   `bc:24:11:1d:2c:0f`.
226	3. Pin the value in systemd-networkd:
227
228	   ```ini
229	   [DHCPv6]
230	   DUIDType=link-layer
231	   DUIDRawData=bc:24:11:1d:2c:0f
232	   ```
233
234	4. Update the KEA reservation to use the DUID rather than the MAC.
235
236	This is a workaround. The proper fix is to ensure DUID stability through MAC
237	pinning and `DUIDType=link-layer`.
238
239	## IPv6 reachability through MWAN
240
241	### Webpass small-payload ICMPv6 drop
242
243	Webpass silently drops ICMPv6 echo requests with payload `<= 8` bytes, so
244	the BSD `ping6` default (8-byte payload) returns 100% loss even when the
245	path is healthy. Probe IPv6 from FreeBSD or macOS with `ping6 -s 16 ...`
246	instead. Linux `ping6` defaults to a 56-byte payload and is unaffected.
247
248	### MWAN dataplane state for the customer prefix
249
250	Three pieces of state on MWAN must be present for OPNsense LAN traffic to
251	reach the public IPv6 internet:
252
253	- **Webpass PD lease.** `find-pd-prefixes.sh enwebpass0` returns the live
254	  `/56` delegated by Webpass (currently `2604:5500:c271:be00::/56`).
255	- **NPT rules** in `nft list table ip6 nat`. `update-npt.sh` programs them
256	  from the live PD lease. `mwan-update-npt.service` is the boot safety net.
257	- **Internal `/60` return route** in MWAN's main + tables 100/200/300:
258	  `3d06:bad:b01::/60 via fe80::be24:11ff:fe77:500c dev enmwanbr0`.
259	  `update-routes.sh` writes this. Without it, MWAN cannot forward conntrack
260	  replies for any non-shared LAN `/64` back to OPNsense.
261
262	### Source-sweep diagnostic
263
264	When only some IPv6 sources work, sweep across every routable `/64` from
265	OPNsense:
266
267	```bash
268	ssh router 'for src in 3d06:bad:b01::1 3d06:bad:b01:1::1 3d06:bad:b01:2::1 \
269	    3d06:bad:b01:a::1 3d06:bad:b01:10::1 3d06:bad:b01:64::1 \
270	    3d06:bad:b01:fe::2; do
271	        echo "=== source $src ==="
272	        ping6 -c 2 -s 16 -S "$src" 2606:4700:4700::1111
273	done'
274	```
275
276	Interpretation:
277
278	- All sources work: IPv6 path healthy.
279	- All sources fail: WAN side broken (Webpass, NPT, or upstream).
280	- Shared LAN `/64` (`3d06:bad:b01::1`) + transit `/64`
281	  (`3d06:bad:b01:fe::2`) work; everything else fails: MWAN is missing the
282	  internal `/60` return route. The shared `/64` reaches OPNsense without a
283	  route because OPNsense `vtnet0` and MWAN `enmgmt0` are L2 neighbors on
284	  that subnet.
285
286	### Verify and recover the internal /60 return route
287
288	On MWAN:
289
290	```bash
291	ip -6 route show table all | grep '3d06:bad:b01::/60'
292	```
293
294	Expected: one entry in main + one in each of tables 100, 200, 300.
295
296	If empty, recover with `systemctl start mwan-update-routes` to re-run
297	`update-routes.sh`. The script is idempotent.
298
299	The dispatcher hook `routable.d/50-update-routes.sh` fires
300	`update-routes.sh` on any routable transition for `enwebpass0`,
301	`enatt0.3242`, `enmbrains0`, or `enmwanbr0` (the internal link), so any
302	flap of those interfaces reinstalls the route automatically.
303
304	## Pre-commit checklist
305
306	1. Verify `host-reservation-identifiers: ["hw-address"]` (or the matching
307	   identifier list) in KEA config.
308	2. Verify `mac-sources` includes the right extraction method.
309	3. Verify `DUIDType=link-layer` in systemd-networkd config.
310	4. Verify the MAC address is pinned in Proxmox or VM config.
311	5. Check for stale leases before deploying changes.
312	6. Verify reservation matching after deployment.
313

1	# SSH and host access
2
3	How to reach hosts in the homelab and which entry point to prefer. Live IPs for
4	each host belong in [docs/infra/overview.md](overview.md) and
5	[docs/infra/hosts.md](hosts.md), not here.
6
7	## Proxy container access
8
9	The proxy container has two SSH entry points:
10
11	- **Port 22 (SSHPiper)**: public-facing. Routes traffic to other containers by
12	username pattern.
13	- **Port 2222 (OpenSSH)**: admin-facing. Direct access to the proxy container
14	itself.
15
16	### Proxy shortcut
17
18	To reach the proxy container via the public port (SSHPiper), use the
19	`@proxy` suffix when configured, or the matching `~/.ssh/config` alias:
20
21	```bash
22	ssh root@proxy@ssh.home.goodkind.io
23	# Or, with ~/.ssh/config:
24	ssh root@proxy
25	```
26
27	This matches the `^(.+)@proxy` regex in `sshpiperd.yaml` and is routed to
28	`[::1]:2222`.
29
30	## Primary method: SSHPiper routing
31
32	All `*.ssh.home.goodkind.io` DNS resolves to the proxy host, where SSHPiper
33	routes by username:
34
35	```bash
36	ssh adguard@ssh.home.goodkind.io
37	ssh pdns@ssh.home.goodkind.io
38	ssh mwan@ssh.home.goodkind.io
39	```
40
41	Pattern: `ssh <short-hostname>@ssh.home.goodkind.io`. The short hostname is the
42	first label of the full container name (`adguard` from
43	`adguard.home.goodkind.io`).
44
45	## Direct IP access (bypass SSHPiper)
46
47	When SSHPiper is unavailable or for troubleshooting, use IPs directly. Prefer
48	IPv6.
49
50	```bash
51	ssh root@<ipv6-address>
52	```
53
54	### Finding a container or VM IP
55
56	```bash
57	# 1. SSH to the Proxmox host that owns the guest.
58	# 2. Find the guest by name.
59	pct list | grep -i <name>            # LXC containers
60	qm list | grep -i <name>             # QEMU VMs
61
62	# 3. Read its primary IP. Prefer inet6.
63	pct exec <vmid> -- ip addr show eth0
64	qm guest cmd <vmid> network-get-interfaces
65
66	# 4. SSH directly. Prefer IPv6.
67	ssh root@<ipv6-address>
68	```
69
70	## Jump host access (last resort)
71
72	If direct IP access fails, jump through OPNsense, then to the hypervisor, then
73	to the target:
74
75	```bash
76	ssh agoodkind@<opnsense>
77	# from there:
78	ssh root@<proxmox-host>
79	ssh root@<container-ip>
80	```
81
82	## Diagnostics-only SSH options
83
84	Disable strict host key checking for automation or diagnostics only:
85
86	```bash
87	ssh -o StrictHostKeyChecking=no -o UserKnownHostsFile=/dev/null root@<ip>
88	```
89
90	## Direct access to the proxy host
91
92	To reach the proxy host itself (bypassing SSHPiper):
93
94	```bash
95	ssh -p 2222 root@<proxy-ipv6>
96	```
97
98	## SSH user conventions
99
100	- Proxmox hosts: `root` over IPv6.
101	- LXC containers: `root` over IPv6 via SSHPiper or direct.
102	- OPNsense (FreeBSD): `agoodkind`. Use `sudo` for privileged tasks.
103	- Proxy host (port 2222): `root`.
104	- Ansible controller container: has `PROXMOX_API_TOKEN` available.
105
106	## SSH from automation (zsh quoting)
107
108	When passing a command to `ssh host <command>`, quote the entire remote command
109	string in single quotes so that the local shell passes the argument verbatim
110	without glob expansion:
111
112	```bash
113	ssh host 'somecommand --flag=value[index]'
114	```
115
116	For anything more complex than a single command, write the logic to a temp
117	file via `mktemp`, `scp` it to the host, execute it there, and clean up
118	afterward.

1	# Ansible configuration
2
3	Automated deployment and configuration management for goodkind.io infrastructure.
4
5	Playbooks run from the controller via
6	the configs binary or the Rake
7	helpers, both of which pick up `~/.config/ansible/vault.pass`. The canonical
8	deploy invocation lives in [AGENTS.md](../../AGENTS.md). See
9	[docs/ansible/secrets.md](secrets.md) for the vault contract,
10	[docs/ansible/quality.md](quality.md) for style and safety rules, and
11	[docs/ansible/proxmox-api.md](proxmox-api.md) for Proxmox API token setup.
12
13	## Inventory layout
14
15	[ansible/ansible.cfg](../../ansible/ansible.cfg) sets `inventory = inventory`,
16	so Ansible walks the directory and merges every source. The inventory is
17	partitioned by source type, not by host group:
18
19	- [ansible/inventory/hosts](../../ansible/inventory/hosts): static INI file.
20	  Owns the hypervisor parent groups (`vault`, `suburban`) and the testbed
21	  groups for hosts the Proxmox API does not surface. It does not own the
22	  OPNsense SSH targets.
23	- [ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/service_mapping.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/service_mapping.yml):
24	  single source of truth for service hostnames, IPv6 addresses, and optional
25	  `ansible_host` overrides. A custom `service_mapping` inventory plugin (source
26	  at [ansible/plugins/inventory/service_mapping.py](../../ansible/plugins/inventory/service_mapping.py))
27	  reads it and creates one `<service>_servers` group per entry plus an
28	  `all_services` group.
29	- [ansible/inventory/*.proxmox.yml](../../ansible/inventory/):
30	  one `community.proxmox.proxmox` plugin file per hypervisor. Each talks to
31	  its Proxmox API and emits that node's guests as inventory hosts. The plugin
32	  requires filenames ending in `proxmox.yml`, which is why the per-hypervisor
33	  qualifier comes first.
34	- [ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vars.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vars.yml):
35	  shared non-secret defaults.
36	- [ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml):
37	  Ansible Vault-encrypted file holding every secret under a `vault_*` name.
38	  Playbooks and templates reference these names directly.
39	  See [docs/ansible/secrets.md](secrets.md) for the full contract.
40
41	Target-specific variables live in files under
42	[ansible/inventory/group_vars/](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/), named
43	`<group>_servers.yml`. Treat the directory listing as the authoritative
44	inventory of those files; the set changes as services come and go and is not
45	enumerated here.
46
47	## OPNsense inventory ownership
48
49	OPNsense is a special case worth calling out, because it is the easiest place
50	to introduce drift:
51
52	- The `opnsense` and `opnsense_test` entries in
53	  [service_mapping.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/service_mapping.yml)
54	  create the `opnsense_servers` and `opnsense_test_servers` groups via the
55	  `service_mapping` plugin. There is no static `[opnsense_servers]` group in
56	  [inventory/hosts](../../ansible/inventory/hosts).
57	- The plugin sets `ansible_host` from the canonical IPv6 by default. The
58	  `opnsense_test` entry overrides `ansible_host` to its LAN IPv4 because the
59	  testbed IPv6 is not reachable from the controller.
60	- Connection vars (SSH user, ProxyJump, BGP identity, gateway names, etc.) live
61	  in
62	  [ansible/inventory/group_vars/opnsense_servers.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/opnsense_servers.yml)
63	  and
64	  [ansible/inventory/group_vars/opnsense_test_servers.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/opnsense_test_servers.yml).
65
66	[ansible/playbooks/deploy-opnsense.yml](../../ansible/playbooks/deploy-opnsense.yml)
67	runs against `opnsense_servers:opnsense_test_servers` and is branchless on
68	`inventory_hostname`. All connection differences are absorbed by the two
69	group_vars files.
70
71	## Where each task runs
72
73	Three execution paths show up depending on what a task does:
74
75	- **Proxmox HTTP API.** Only the `community.proxmox.proxmox` dynamic inventory
76	  plugin uses the Proxmox HTTP API directly, to list guests. No routine
77	  playbook contacts the Proxmox HTTP API.
78	- **Hypervisor SSH delegation.** Tasks that need to run `pct` or `qm` on a
79	  hypervisor open SSH to that hypervisor and run there.
80	  [ansible/playbooks/deploy-ssh-keys.yml](../../ansible/playbooks/deploy-ssh-keys.yml)
81	  is the canonical example: it uses `delegate_to: "{{ item.host }}"` with `pct
82	  push`, `pct exec`, and `qm` status/start. The task runs on the hypervisor,
83	  not the guest.
84	- **Direct guest SSH.** Tasks that configure something inside a guest open SSH
85	  directly to the guest.
86	  [ansible/playbooks/prep-guests.yml](../../ansible/playbooks/prep-guests.yml)
87	  and most plays inside
88	  [ansible/playbooks/deploy-mwan.yml](../../ansible/playbooks/deploy-mwan.yml)
89	  are direct-guest-SSH; the controller's SSH connection lands on the guest
90	  with no hypervisor in between.
91
92	When reading a playbook, look at `hosts:`, `delegate_to:`, and any `pct` or
93	`qm` commands to tell which path a task takes.
94
95	## Proxmox plugin name collisions
96
97	Each per-hypervisor Proxmox plugin file emits guests using the guest's raw
98	`name` field from Proxmox as the inventory hostname. The
99	`community.proxmox.proxmox` plugin offers no way to override this. If a guest
100	on one hypervisor shares its Proxmox `name` with a guest on another, Ansible
101	merges them into one inventory host, and the second-loaded plugin file wins on
102	conflicting attributes such as `ansible_host`. When this happens, rename one
103	of the guests in Proxmox itself.
104
105	## Secrets management
106
107	All secret values live in Ansible Vault under `vault_*` names. Files that need
108	a vault-stored secret reference the `vault_*` name directly. See
109	[docs/ansible/secrets.md](secrets.md) for the naming rule, allowed env-wrapper
110	exceptions, and the safe key listing command.
111
112	## Setup for new operators
113
114	Store the team vault password at `~/.config/ansible/vault.pass` with mode
115	`600`. Install Ansible collections with
116	`ansible-galaxy collection install -r playbooks/requirements.yml` using
117	[ansible/playbooks/requirements.yml](../../ansible/playbooks/requirements.yml).
118
119	## Running playbooks
120
121	The canonical deploy invocation lives in [AGENTS.md](../../AGENTS.md). Rake
122	helpers wrap the canonical playbooks. See
123	[ansible/Rakefile](../../ansible/Rakefile) for the current set.
124

1	# Ansible quality checks
2
3	Style and safety rules for Ansible playbooks, roles, and templates in this repo.
4	See [docs/ansible/overview.md](overview.md) for inventory layout and
5	[docs/ansible/secrets.md](secrets.md) for the vault contract.
6
7	## Debugging: fix root causes, not symptoms
8
9	When a variable is missing or a validation fails, investigate why before adding
10	defensive code.
11
12	`when:` is for logic branches (deciding between actions), not defensive
13	programming. Adding `| default('')` or `when: var is defined` without
14	understanding why the variable is missing masks the real issue.
15
16	Symptoms that mean you are looking at a root-cause bug, not a missing default:
17
18	- Validation tasks fail for values that should exist.
19	- Variables are unexpectedly empty despite being "set".
20	- Playbooks silently skip tasks that should run.
21
22	Trace the variable source before patching:
23
24	1. Where is it supposed to come from (inventory, `set_fact`, `register`,
25	   hostvars)?
26	2. Is there a naming mismatch? The Proxmox plugin emits `proxmox_type`, not
27	   `proxmox_vmtype`. Dynamic inventories have specific variable names.
28	3. Are play and task ordering correct? Variables set in one play are not
29	   automatically available in another without `hostvars`.
30	4. Is the inventory composition right? See `compose:` in
31	   [ansible/inventory/vault.proxmox.yml](../../ansible/inventory/vault.proxmox.yml).
32
33	```yaml
34	# Bad - bandaid that hides the real problem
35	type: "{{ proxmox_vmtype | default('lxc') }}"
36
37	# Bad - defensive `when` that masks missing data
38	- name: Configure service
39	  ansible.builtin.template:
40	    src: config.j2
41	    dest: /etc/service/config
42	  when: service_config is defined
43
44	# Good - `when` for an actual logic branch (feature flag)
45	- name: Configure IPv6
46	  ansible.builtin.template:
47	    src: ipv6.j2
48	    dest: /etc/network/ipv6
49	  when: enable_ipv6 | bool
50
51	# Good - fix at the source
52	# If proxmox_vmtype is missing, add it to the proxmox.yml compose block:
53	#   compose:
54	#     proxmox_vmtype: proxmox_type
55	```
56
57	Checklist before adding `| default()` or `is defined`:
58
59	1. Where is this variable supposed to come from?
60	2. Is it a naming mismatch?
61	3. Is it missing from inventory composition?
62	4. Is it set in a different play that has not run yet?
63	5. Only add defensive defaults after confirming the source is correct.
64
65	## Default values policy
66
67	Every input value is declared explicitly: in the service's group_vars, in
68	[ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/service_mapping.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/service_mapping.yml),
69	or in OpenTofu. A playbook or template reads it bare and fails at load time when
70	it is missing. Do not use `| default(...)` or `is defined` on an input variable
71	to paper over a missing value or to infer presence. When you need a branch, drive
72	`when:` from an explicit flag, not from whether a variable happens to be set.
73
74	Inferring a value from whether it was set is banned in every form: `| default(...)`,
75	`is defined`, `.get(key, default)` (a default in disguise), any `| length`
76	comparison (an "is this set" or "how big" check in disguise), and
77	`lookup(..., default=...)` (an env-presence default in disguise; the place the
78	declared value stops being deterministic). There is no automatic exception and no
79	escape hatch, and the linter lists every banned line, not one per repeated
80	snippet. The only defensible reason to read a
81	value defensively is a command result from an outside service that is unset more
82	often than not, and that judgment is the author's to make and defend in review.
83	Restructure instead: declare the value, gate a task with the module's own
84	`failed_when` or `changed_when`, or initialize an accumulator with `set_fact`
85	before the loop.
86
87	Enforced by `configs lint`: the deploy command runs it before every deploy, the
88	lint path runs it, and pre-commit runs it on staged files. The check flags every
89	occurrence; it grants no exception, so a genuine outside-service case is the
90	author's call to defend, not the check's to allow.
91
92	The linter parses each Jinja expression with a Go engine and resolves the operand
93	each default or presence construct reads. A few Ansible-Jinja forms the Go engine
94	cannot parse, such as a parenthesized conditional piped into a filter, are routed
95	to a jinja2 reference parser ([scripts/lint_ansible_ast.py](../../scripts/lint_ansible_ast.py)),
96	whose resolved violations are enforced the same as any other. The router runs as a
97	`python3` subprocess, so `configs lint` requires `python3` with the `jinja2`
98	package on PATH. A form neither parser can read is listed for review.
99
100	## Line length
101
102	- Prefer below 80 columns.
103	- Up to 90 columns is acceptable.
104	- 120 columns is the hard limit.
105
106	Break long lines using YAML block scalars (`>-`, `|`) with explicit Jinja2
107	whitespace control (`{{-`, `-}}`), Jinja2 concatenation, named variables, or by
108	splitting conditionals at logical points (`if`, `and`, `or`).
109
110	```yaml
111	# Bad - exceeds 120 columns
112	url: "https://{{ proxmox_api_host }}:8006/api2/json/nodes/{{ target_node }}/lxc/{{ container_result.vmid }}/interfaces"
113
114	# Bad - `>-` collapses the newline to a space, breaking the URL
115	url: >-
116	  "https://{{ proxmox_api_host }}:8006/api2/json/nodes/{{ target_node }}/lxc/
117	  {{- container_result.vmid }}/interfaces"
118
119	# Good - strip trailing whitespace with `-}}` and put `{{-` on the same line
120	url: >-
121	  "https://{{ proxmox_api_host }}:8006/api2/json/nodes/{{ target_node -}}/lxc/{{-
122	  container_result.vmid }}/interfaces"
123	```
124
125	## YAML formatting traps
126
127	### Folded scalars (`>-`) with URLs
128
129	YAML `>-` folds newlines to spaces, which breaks URLs split across lines.
130
131	```yaml
132	# Bad - inserts a space inside the URL
133	url: >-
134	  https://github.com/user/repo/releases/download/
135	  v{{ version }}/file.tar.gz
136
137	# Good - single line
138	url: "https://github.com/user/repo/releases/download/v{{ version }}/file.tar.gz"
139
140	# Good - broken with explicit whitespace control
141	url: >-
142	  "https://{{ host }}/api/nodes/{{ node -}}/lxc/{{-
143	  vmid }}/interfaces"
144	```
145
146	### Quoted strings inside folded scalars
147
148	Quotes inside `>-` become part of the value. `ansible.builtin.uri` will then
149	fail with `unknown url type: "https`.
150
151	```yaml
152	# Bad - quotes are literal characters in the URL
153	url: >-
154	  "https://example.com/path"
155
156	# Good - no embedded quotes
157	url: >-
158	  https://example.com/path
159	```
160
161	### `blockinfile` with systemd `ExecStart`
162
163	`>-` inside a `blockinfile` payload is written to the destination file
164	literally, which breaks systemd units.
165
166	```yaml
167	# Bad - `>-` lands in the unit file
168	block: |
169	  ExecStart=-/sbin/agetty >-
170	    --autologin root tty%I 115200 $TERM
171
172	# Good
173	block: |
174	  ExecStart=-/sbin/agetty --autologin root tty%I 115200 $TERM
175	```
176
177	### YAML operators inside `shell:` blocks
178
179	YAML operators like `>-` are YAML syntax, not shell syntax. They pass through as
180	literal arguments to the command and produce confusing runtime errors (for
181	example, `htpasswd` exiting 2).
182
183	```yaml
184	# Bad - `>-` becomes a literal shell argument
185	- ansible.builtin.shell: |
186	    htpasswd -nb >-
187	      "{{ user }}" >-
188	      "{{ pass }}" >-
189	      /etc/traefik/auth/dashboard-users
190
191	# Good - structured argv via `command`, then copy the output
192	- ansible.builtin.command:
193	    argv: ["htpasswd", "-nbB", "{{ user }}", "{{ pass }}"]
194	  register: htpasswd_out
195	  changed_when: false
196	  no_log: true
197
198	- ansible.builtin.copy:
199	    dest: /etc/traefik/auth/dashboard-users
200	    content: "{{ htpasswd_out.stdout }}\n"
201	    mode: "0600"
202	    no_log: true
203	```
204
205	### systemd-networkd section merging
206
207	systemd-networkd does not merge duplicate sections. Only the first `[Section]`
208	is processed. `blockinfile` that creates a second `[DHCPv6]` silently loses the
209	new keys. Use `lineinfile` with `regexp` and `insertafter` to extend an existing
210	section, or guarantee the section does not exist before using `blockinfile`.
211
212	## Variable safety
213
214	### Undefined references inside the same `set_fact`
215
216	`set_fact` evaluates all keys concurrently, so a later key cannot see an
217	earlier key in the same task.
218
219	```yaml
220	# Bad - var1 is not yet available when var2 evaluates
221	- ansible.builtin.set_fact:
222	    var1: "value"
223	    var2: "{{ var1 }}-suffix"
224
225	# Bad - pipeline facts in one task
226	- ansible.builtin.set_fact:
227	    filtered_ipv6: "{{ ipv6_candidates | reject('match','^fe80:') | list }}"
228	    primary_ip: "{{ filtered_ipv6[0] if (filtered_ipv6 | length > 0) else '' }}"
229
230	# Good - split into sequential tasks
231	- ansible.builtin.set_fact:
232	    var1: "value"
233	- ansible.builtin.set_fact:
234	    var2: "{{ var1 }}-suffix"
235	```
236
237	### Jinja2 `.first` on possibly empty lists
238
239	`.first` on an empty list raises "No first item, sequence was empty". Use
240	indexed access with a length check.
241
242	```yaml
243	# Bad
244	ip: "{{ ip_list | first }}"
245
246	# Good
247	ip: "{{ ip_list[0] if (ip_list | length > 0) else '' }}"
248	```
249
250	## KEA DHCP reservations
251
252	- DHCPv4: `hw-address` and `client-id` are mutually exclusive.
253	- DHCPv6: `hw-address` and `duid` are mutually exclusive.
254
255	Use one identifier per reservation. Prefer `hw-address` when the MAC is pinned.
256
257	## Secrets
258
259	Vault-first. Do not rely on local files on the controller. Store secrets in
260	[ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml)
261	and inject with `content: "{{ vault_var }}"` in `copy` tasks rather than `src:`.
262	Full contract in [docs/ansible/secrets.md](secrets.md).
263
264	## Dynamic list parsing
265
266	`uri` returns multi-line strings for list-like data (Cloudflare IP ranges,
267	etc.). Splitting in YAML breaks if you template the string directly.
268
269	```yaml
270	# Bad - renders as one invalid long string
271	trusted_ips: "{{ response.content.split('\n') }}"
272
273	# Good - a real YAML list
274	trusted_ips: "{{ response.content.splitlines() }}"
275	```
276
277	## Process management
278
279	- For debugging or complex deployments that might race, force sequential
280	  execution with `--forks=1`.
281	- Ensure previous `ansible-playbook` processes are killed before starting a new
282	  run if they might be hung.
283
284	## Linting and verification
285
286	`ansible-lint` is not instant. Wait a few seconds after edits before checking
287	linter output. The linter analyses YAML, Jinja2, and module usage, so freshly
288	edited files may briefly report stale warnings.
289
290	## Pre-commit checklist
291
292	Before committing Ansible changes, verify:
293
294	1. Line length: prefer below 80, acceptable up to 90, hard limit 120.
295	2. No `url:` fields use `>-` with multi-line URLs unless using explicit Jinja2
296	   whitespace control.
297	3. No `url: >-` or `Authorization: >-` values contain surrounding quotes.
298	4. No `shell: |` blocks contain YAML operators like `>-` used as line
299	   continuation.
300	5. No `blockinfile` payload contains literal `>-` in command output.
301	6. No `set_fact` task references a variable defined in the same task.
302	7. No `.first` filter used without an empty-list check.
303	8. No KEA reservation uses mutually exclusive identifiers.
304	9. No `blockinfile` creates a duplicate systemd-networkd section; use
305	   `lineinfile` instead.
306	10. No `| default()` or `is defined` on an input variable. Declare it in
307	    group_vars and read it bare; both are allowed only on command or register
308	    output. `configs lint` enforces this.
309

1	# Ansible Vault Quick Reference
2
3	All secret values live in [ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml), encrypted with Ansible
4	Vault. [ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vars.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vars.yml) stores shared non-secret variables only.
5	List vault key names with
6	the configs binary `keys`. Do not
7	invoke `ansible`, `ansible-vault`, `ansible-playbook`, `ansible-inventory`, or
8	`ansible-console` directly.
9
10	## File locations
11
12	- Vault file: [ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml) (encrypted, committed to git)
13	- Shared vars file: [ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vars.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vars.yml) (plaintext, committed to git)
14	- CLI password: `~/.config/ansible/vault.pass` (not in git, must be 600 permissions)
15
16	## Safe key listing
17
18	```bash
19	go run goodkind.io/configs/cmd/configs keys
20	```
21
22	Prints key paths such as `vault_proxmox_token_secret`. Decrypted values are not
23	printed.
24
25	## Variable contract
26
27	- Secret values in [ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml) use `vault_*` names.
28	- [ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vars.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vars.yml) stores shared non-secret values only.
29	- Files that need a vault-stored secret reference the `vault_*` name directly.
30	- Do not add pure aliases like `api_key: "{{ vault_api_key }}"` to shared or service `group_vars` files.
31	- Env-wrapper variables are allowed only when they encode a real env override with a vault fallback and stay local to the service or play that needs them.
32	- Example: `cloudflare_api_token` in [ansible/inventory/group_vars/proxy_servers.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/proxy_servers.yml) is allowed because it checks `CLOUDFLARE_*` environment variables first and falls back to `vault_cloudflare_api_token`.
33
34	## Troubleshooting
35
36	If decryption fails, verify `~/.config/ansible/vault.pass` exists and contains the
37	correct password. If a playbook reports an undefined `vault_*` variable, verify that
38	the key exists in [ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml) and that the consumer is not still using a removed alias.
39
40	## Lost vault password
41
42	If the vault password is lost, decryption of
43	[ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml)
44	is not possible. Options are to restore the password from the team password manager
45	(1Password), or to re-create all secrets from their original sources and create a new
46	[ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml).
47	Back up the vault password in the team password manager.
48

1	# Proxmox API token setup for Ansible
2
3	## Create the API token
4
5	In the Proxmox web UI, go to Datacenter, then Permissions, then API Tokens.
6	Create a token for `ansible@pam` with token ID `ansible-token`, and disable
7	Privilege Separation so the token inherits the user's permissions directly.
8
9	## Required permissions
10
11	Grant `ansible@pam` the `PVEVMAdmin` role on path `/`. That role covers guest
12	lifecycle operations, config changes, console access, and datastore allocation.
13	If a workflow needs a narrower ACL later, document the missing capability before
14	you tighten it.
15
16	## Where Ansible reads the token secrets
17
18	The per-hypervisor inventory plugins keep the API URL, username, and token ID in
19	plaintext, and they read the token secret directly from
20	[ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml):
21
22	- [ansible/inventory/vault.proxmox.yml](../../ansible/inventory/vault.proxmox.yml) reads `vault_proxmox_token_secret`
23	- [ansible/inventory/suburban.proxmox.yml](../../ansible/inventory/suburban.proxmox.yml) reads `vault_suburban_testbed_pve_token_secret`
24
25	Update those `vault_*` values when a token rotates. Do not move the token
26	secrets into shell startup files just to satisfy inventory.
27
28	## Verification
29
30	Check the ACL list and confirm `ansible@pam` has `PVEVMAdmin` on `/`. Then run a
31	read-only inventory load from [ansible/](../../ansible/) and confirm the
32	Proxmox plugin can list guests without an authentication failure.
33
34	## Troubleshooting
35
36	Permission denied (`403`) errors that mention changing feature flags usually
37	mean `ansible@pam` is missing `VM.Config.Options`. Re-grant `PVEVMAdmin` on `/`
38	and retry.
39
40	Using `root@pam` instead of `ansible@pam` can work for diagnostics, but it is a
41	separate operational path and should not become the documented default.

1	# isp-lxc templates
2
3	Jinja2 templates rendered onto ISP simulator LXCs 200 (Webpass), 201 (AT&T),
4	and 202 (Monkeybrains / mbrains) by the testbed deploy playbook
5	(`deploy-testbed.yml` via `tasks/deploy-testbed-isp-lxc.yml`). Each LXC's
6	capabilities are driven by its entry in `testbed_isp_lxcs`
7	(`ansible/inventory/group_vars/suburban_servers.yml`): `pd_len`, `dynamic_v4`,
8	`ia_na`, `slaac_prefix`, `v4_reservations`.
9
10	## Files
11
12	- `radvd.conf.j2`: radvd configuration. Always advertises the router (default
13	  route) with `AdvManagedFlag on` + `AdvOtherConfigFlag on` so the WAN VM runs
14	  DHCPv6 for IA_NA and PD. When `slaac_prefix` is set, it also advertises that
15	  /64 with `AdvAutonomous on` so the VM autoconfigures a SLAAC global address,
16	  mirroring prod where the ISP RA yields a SLAAC `mngtmpaddr`.
17	- `kea-dhcp6.conf.j2`: DHCPv6. Always delegates a prefix (`pd_len` long). When
18	  `ia_na` is set, it also hands out IA_NA addresses from a pool on the
19	  `slaac_prefix` /64 (full prod-parity dynamic stack).
20	- `kea-dhcp4.conf.j2`: DHCPv4. Rendered and enabled only when `dynamic_v4` is
21	  set (the `kea-dhcp4-server` unit is pre-installed on the LXCs). Serves the
22	  `v4_subnet` pool with optional `v4_reservations` host reservations.
23	- `nftables.conf.j2`, `nftables.conf.tmpl`: firewall and NAT rules for ISP LXCs.
24	- `pd-route.service.j2`, `pd-route.service.tmpl`: systemd unit that installs the
25	  delegated-prefix return route after the DHCP-PD exchange completes.
26	- `sysctl-isp.conf`: kernel tuning applied to ISP LXCs.
27	- `200/`, `201/`, `202/`: rendered per-LXC reference snapshots.
28
29	## Per-ISP IPv6/IPv4 behavior
30
31	Capabilities mirror how prod addresses each WAN:
32
33	- Monkeybrains (202): full dynamic stack. DHCPv4 + DHCPv6 IA_NA + DHCPv6-PD
34	  (`/56`) + SLAAC (on `slaac_prefix`). v4 egress is masquerade.
35	- AT&T (201) and Webpass (200): DHCPv6-PD + RA only (no `slaac_prefix`, no
36	  `dynamic_v4`); the WAN VM holds a static v4. These reach full prod parity in
37	  later phases (att dynamic link plus routed static /29, webpass static /29).

1	# Production OPNsense State
2
3	This file records the current production OPNsense role and topology. It is a
4	state document, not the architectural source of truth for MWAN behavior. For
5	steady-state BGP and operational foot-guns, use
6	[../opnsense/operational-notes.md](../opnsense/operational-notes.md). For the
7	current testbed baseline and import workflow, use
8	[../opnsense/testbed-baseline.md](../opnsense/testbed-baseline.md) and
9	[../opnsense/testbed-config-import.md](../opnsense/testbed-config-import.md). For the
10	out-of-band serial control channel into this router, use the
11	[OPNsense OOB daemon](../opnsense/daemon.md).
12
13	## Role
14
15	Production OPNsense runs as QEMU VM `101` on `vault`. It is the LAN router and
16	services edge, but it is not the WAN edge. All upstream Internet traffic flows
17	through the production MWAN VM, and OPNsense treats that VM as its upstream for
18	both IPv4 and IPv6.
19
20	## Interfaces
21
22	| Interface | Role | IPv4 | IPv6 |
23	| --------- | ---- | ---- | ---- |
24	| `vtnet0` | Management LAN for containers and core services | `10.250.0.1/24` | `3d06:bad:b01::1/64` |
25	| `vtnet1` | Uplink toward the MWAN VM | `10.250.250.2/29` | `3d06:bad:b01:fe::2/64` |
26	| `iavf0` | IoT and UniFi management | `10.250.4.1/24` | `3d06:bad:b01:4::1/64` |
27	| `vlan0100` | Physical devices such as `mini` and `nas` | `10.250.1.1/24` | `3d06:bad:b01:1::1/64` |
28	| `vlan0200` | Home automation segment | `10.250.2.1/24` | `3d06:bad:b01:2::1/64` |
29	| `vlan0300` | Guest and captive-portal segment | `10.250.3.1/24` | None by design |
30	| `wg0` | WireGuard hub | `10.250.10.1/24`, `10.240.10.2/24` | `3d06:bad:b01:10::1/64`, `3d06:bad:b01:a::1/64` |
31	| `nat64` | Tayga NAT64 | `10.250.46.1`, translated toward `10.250.64.1` | `3d06:bad:b01:64::ffff:1/128`, prefix `3d06:bad:b01:6464::/96` |
32
33	## Upstream routing
34
35	The default IPv4 route points at `10.250.250.1` on `vtnet1`. The default IPv6
36	route points at the MWAN-side link-local next hop on `vtnet1`. OPNsense does
37	not hold the WAN uplinks directly, so outbound failover and delegated-prefix
38	handling happen on MWAN, not on OPNsense.
39
40	The internal IPv6 space remains `3d06:bad:b01::/48`. The repo treats that block
41	as the stable internal prefix, and the MWAN VM applies NPT to map internal
42	segments onto provider-delegated space for outbound reachability.
43
44	## Services anchored here
45
46	OPNsense still owns Unbound, DHCP, WireGuard, and the LAN-facing interface
47	address plan.
48
49	Notable current DHCP and DNS state:
50
51	- `mini` is reserved at `10.250.1.2` and `3d06:bad:b01:1::2`.
52	- `nas` is reserved at `3d06:bad:b01:1::3`, and the `nas_host` alias follows
53	  that address.
54	- `home-assistant` is reserved at `10.250.2.3` and `3d06:bad:b01:2::3`.
55	- Unbound forwards upstream queries to NextDNS.
56
57	## WireGuard peers
58
