### Assistant (2026-07-06 21:06)
[tool: Read] {"file_path":"/Users/agoodkind/Sites/configs.wt-ifmgr-scaffold/docs/opnsense/operational-notes.md"}
[tool output]
1	# OPNsense Operational Notes
2
3	These are the non-obvious behaviors and configurations that matter when running
4	OPNsense as a BGP-only edge router. Static WAN gateways do not own the default
5	route. FRR owns the kernel default route.
6
7	If you stand up another OPNsense to replace this one, the steady-state config
8	section is the canonical end target. The operational rules section is the
9	list of foot-guns to avoid.
10
11	---
12
13	## Steady-state OPNsense config
14
15	Validated on prod (`router.home.goodkind.io`).
16
17	### Gateways (System / Gateways / Configuration)
18
19	| Gateway | Disabled | force_down | defaultgw | Notes |
20	|---|---|---|---|---|
21	| NAT64_GW | 0 | **1** | 0 | Enabled but force_down so it does NOT win default selection. Static route to `:6464::/96` still installs because the route lookup ignores `force_down`. Tayga keeps translating. |
22
23	### Static routes (System / Routes / Configuration)
24
25	| Network | Gateway | Why |
26	|---|---|---|
27	| `3d06:bad:b01:6464::/96` | NAT64_GW | NAT64 prefix delegated to Tayga for v6 to v4 translation |
28
29	Only the NAT64 static route belongs here.
30
31	### Outbound NAT (Firewall / NAT / Outbound)
32
33	Mode: **Manual** (or Hybrid; either works as long as the manual rules below exist).
34
35	Explicit manual NAT rules are required because the OPNsense auto-NAT loop only
36	runs when an interface gateway is configured. BGP owns the default route here,
37	so these manual rules provide the outbound NAT contract.
38
39	| # | Interface | Source | Translation | Static port | Purpose |
40	|---|---|---|---|---|---|
41	| 1 | WAN | INTERNAL net (alias) | Interface address | NO | All LAN-side networks NAT to WAN address |
42	| 2 | WAN | THIS FIREWALL | Interface address | NO | OPNsense itself (loopback + interface IPs) NAT when egressing WAN |
43
44	INTERNAL net resolves to all v4 networks of every interface in the INTERNAL
45	group. When you add a new VLAN to INTERNAL, the rule auto-includes it.
46
47	THIS FIREWALL (`(self)` in pf) covers OPNsense-initiated outbound for
48	services that bind to loopback or any LAN-side address.
49
50	Optional rule for IPsec/IKE if used: same source as #1 but dst port 500 with
51	`Static port` checked (auto-NAT generates this; if you do IPsec, replicate it).
52
53	### Default routes (kernel, owned by FRR/zebra)
54
55	```text
56	default            10.250.250.3       UG1          vtnet1   # BGP via VM 113 primary
57	default            3d06:bad:b01:fe::3 UG1          vtnet1   # BGP via VM 113 primary
58	```
59
60	`UG1` flag indicates installed by zebra (FRR). Status in `vtysh -c "show ip[v6] route 0.0.0.0/0"`
61	should be `Status: Installed, Selected` for the BGP entry.
62
63	### FRR / Quagga
64
65	- Plugin: `os-frr` installed
66	- BGP mode enabled
67	- Two neighbors per family:
68	  - `10.250.250.3` and `3d06:bad:b01:fe::3` (VM 113, primary, route-map sets local-pref 200)
69	  - `10.250.250.4` and `3d06:bad:b01:fe::4` (LXC 116, backup, route-map sets local-pref 100)
70
71	---
72
73	## Operational rules (foot-guns)
74
75	### Rule 1: Never enable a v4 or v6 gateway entity at top priority
76
77	Source evidence: `src/etc/inc/system.inc` lines 703-723 + 651-654.
78
79	```php
80	$gateway = $gateways->getDefaultGW($down_gateways, $ipproto);
81	if (empty($gateway['gateway'])) {
82	    continue;       // SKIP because no default gateway candidate
83	}
84	...
85	system_default_route($gateway, $routes);  // route delete + add
86	```
87
88	`system_routing_configure` runs `system_default_route` for each address family
89	**only if** `getDefaultGW` returns a non-empty gateway. `system_default_route`
90	unconditionally calls:
91
92	```shell
93	route delete -inet6 default
94	route add -inet6 default <new_gateway>
95	```
96
97	zebra on FreeBSD does not see `RTM_DELROUTE`, so its BGP-installed default
98	stays `Status: None` while the kernel sits with whatever OPNsense reinstalled
99	(or nothing). Recovery requires `service frr stop && route delete + route start`.
100
101	| Gateway state for family | system_default_route called? | BGP route survives Apply? |
102	|---|---|---|
103	| Any enabled non-down gateway exists | YES | NO (kernel default replaced) |
104	| All gateways for family are deleted/disabled/force_down | NO (early `continue`) | YES |
105
106	So: when no v4 or v6 gateway is selectable as default, future Apply events
107	skip `system_default_route` and leave BGP's kernel default untouched.
108
109	### Rule 2: Auto outbound NAT also requires a gateway
110
111	Source: `src/etc/inc/filter.inc` lines 220-238.
112
113	```php
114	foreach ($fw->getInterfaceMapping() as $intf => $ifcfg) {
115	    if (substr($ifcfg['if'], 0, 4) != 'ovpn' && !empty($ifcfg['gateway'])) {
116	        // generate auto outbound NAT rule
117	    }
118	}
119	```
120
121	When the WAN interface has no configured gateway, this condition is false and
122	OPNsense does not generate auto-NAT for v4 LAN to WAN traffic.
123
124	Replacement: the two manual rules in the steady-state section. They cover
125	the same ground regardless of gateway state.
126
127	### Rule 3: NAT64_GW disabled vs force_down
128
129	| Setting | Effect on `getDefaultGW` | Effect on static route install |
130	|---|---|---|
131	| `disabled=1` | Skipped (good, doesn't grab default) | **Skipped**. `gatewaysIndexedByName(false, ...)` excludes disabled gateways. The `:6464::/96` static route logs `gateway IP could not be found` and is NOT installed. NAT64 breaks. |
132	| `disabled=0` + `force_down=1` | Skipped (good) | **Installed**. `gatewaysIndexedByName` ignores `force_down`. NAT64 keeps working. |
133
134	Use `force_down`, not `disabled`, when you want a gateway to exist for
135	static-route reference but never be selected as default.
136
137	### Rule 4: If you must enable a gateway temporarily
138
139	Restart FRR after to recover BGP defaults:
140
141	```shell
142	ssh agoodkind@3d06:bad:b01::1 "sudo service frr stop && sudo route -n delete -inet default 2>/dev/null; sudo route -n delete -inet6 default 2>/dev/null; sudo service frr start"
143	```
144
145	(Adjust which family to delete based on which gateway you enabled.)
146
147	### Rule 5: GUI Apply consequences are conditional
148
149	For most gateway/route/interface changes, the Apply triggers
150	`system_routing_configure`. The defaults steps run per the rules above.
151	The static-route rebuild always runs (delete + add for every
152	`<staticroutes><route>` entry) but only affects whatever specific networks
153	those routes cover, not the default. So it's safe assuming Rule 1 holds.
154
155	### Rule 6: Duplicate `<if>device</if>` declarations silently drop the loser
156
157	`interfaces_configure` builds `$hardware[$ifcfg['if']] = $if`, keyed by device name. Two interface entries on the same untagged device cause the second to overwrite the first in the map. Iteration order is alphabetical by `<descr>` via `strnatcmp` in `config.inc:340`. The losing interface stays in the GUI config but binds no address to any kernel interface. The testbed substitutions transform strips `opt6` so MANAGEMENT remains the only untagged interface mapped to `vtnet0`.
158
159	### Rule 7: `pkg upgrade -y` must run BEFORE `pkg install`
160
161	The OPNsense install ISO ships one snapshot of the package set. The mirror has moved on by the time you install anything. Running `pkg update -f` then jumping straight to `pkg install os-frr` pulls a libyang2 built against `pcre2-10.47` onto a system that still has `pcre2-10.45`. `vtysh` then fails at startup with `ld-elf.so.1: /usr/local/lib/libpcre2-8.so.0: version PCRE2_10.47 required by libyang2.so.2 not defined`. Insert `pkg upgrade -y` between `pkg update -f` and the first `pkg install`.
162
163	### Rule 8: Proxmox restricts `args` qemu-server field to literal `root@pam`
164
165	Setting the `args` field (used by Tofu's `kvm_arguments`) returns HTTP 500 "only root can set 'args' config" for any API token, regardless of `privsep` or assigned role. The check is hard-coded in Proxmox, not policy-driven. For VMs that need `args` (any VM with a virtio-serial chardev, including the mwan-opnsense VMs): `qm create` manually as root via SSH, then `tofu import` the resulting VM. The pattern is documented in [opentofu/imports.md](../../opentofu/imports.md).
166
167	### Rule 9: Hot-adding a NIC needs `configctl interface reconfigure`
168
169	`qm set <vmid> --netN ...` adds the NIC at the hypervisor level. OPNsense's kernel sees the new `vtnetN` device, but the in-OPNsense interface config does not auto-bind to it. The new device comes up `IFDISABLED` until `configctl interface reconfigure <wan|opt...>` runs on the guest. Run reconfigure for whichever OPNsense interface is supposed to bind to the new device.
170
171	---
172
173	## Recovery snippets
174
175	### BGP default got wiped on v4 + v6
176
177	```shell
178	ssh agoodkind@3d06:bad:b01::1 'sudo service frr stop'
179	ssh agoodkind@3d06:bad:b01::1 'sudo route -n delete -inet default 2>/dev/null'
180	ssh agoodkind@3d06:bad:b01::1 'sudo route -n delete -inet6 default 2>/dev/null'
181	ssh agoodkind@3d06:bad:b01::1 'sudo service frr start'
182	sleep 5
183	ssh agoodkind@3d06:bad:b01::1 'sudo netstat -rn | grep ^default'
184	```
185
186	Should show BGP defaults restored (`UG1` flag).
187
188	### NAT64 stops working
189
190	Check (from any v6-capable host on LAN):
191
192	```shell
193	dig @3d06:bad:b01::64 +short AAAA ipv4.google.com
194	ping6 <synthesized addr from above>
195	```
196
197	If DNS64 returns synth but ping fails, check the `:6464::/96` static route
198	on OPNsense (`netstat -rn -f inet6 | grep 6464`). If missing, check that
199	NAT64_GW is `disabled=0` AND the static route is `disabled=0`.
200
201	### Outbound NAT stops working (LAN clients lose v4 Internet but v6 works)
202
203	Most likely cause: the manual NAT rules are missing. Check Firewall / NAT /
204	Outbound for the two manual rules. Verify with `pfctl -sn | grep ^nat` from
205	OPNsense shell; should see at least one `nat on vtnet1 inet from <internal_net>
206	to any -> (vtnet1:0)` rule.
207

9
10	# Deploy Ansible Playbook
11
12	The vault password file at `~/.config/ansible/vault.pass` is required. Use
13	the configs binary `deploy` to run
14	playbooks. Do not invoke `ansible`, `ansible-vault`, `ansible-playbook`,
15	`ansible-inventory`, or `ansible-console` directly.
16
17	## Canonical Playbooks
18
19	There are five canonical playbooks. Each targets a specific group; environment
20	differences between production and testbed come from group vars, not playbook
21	flags.
22
23	| Playbook | Target group | Owns |
24	| --- | --- | --- |
25	| [ansible/playbooks/deploy-proxmox.yml](../../../ansible/playbooks/deploy-proxmox.yml) | `proxmox_servers` | mwan-ifmgr, mwan-watchdog, cloudflared-oob, package-updater on hypervisors |
26	| [ansible/playbooks/deploy-mwan.yml](../../../ansible/playbooks/deploy-mwan.yml) | `mwan_servers` | MWAN VM, prod VM 113 on vault |
27	| [ansible/playbooks/deploy-mwan-failover.yml](../../../ansible/playbooks/deploy-mwan-failover.yml) | `mwan_failover_servers` or `mwan_failover_test_servers` | MWAN failover LXC |
28	| [ansible/playbooks/deploy-opnsense.yml](../../../ansible/playbooks/deploy-opnsense.yml) | `opnsense_servers` or `opnsense_test_servers` | mwan-opnsense daemon on OPNsense host |
29	| [ansible/playbooks/deploy-testbed.yml](../../../ansible/playbooks/deploy-testbed.yml) | `suburban_servers` | Suburban-only extras, including `qm args`, ISP LXCs, host bridge, and VFIO |
30
31	## Invocation Pattern
32
33	```bash
34	go run goodkind.io/configs/cmd/configs deploy <name> [--limit <host>] [--check] [--diff]
35	```
36
37	`<name>` is the playbook stem, such as `deploy-proxmox` or `deploy-mwan`. The
38	helper resolves it to `playbooks/<name>.yml` under
39	[ansible/](../../../ansible/). A full `.yml` path is also accepted.
40
41	Always include `--limit <host-or-group>` for production runs so one command does
42	not touch both hypervisors at once. Dry-run with `--check --diff` first when in
43	doubt.
44
45	## Examples
46
47	```bash
48	# Configure both Proxmox hypervisors
49	go run goodkind.io/configs/cmd/configs deploy deploy-proxmox
50
51	# Configure only vault
52	go run goodkind.io/configs/cmd/configs deploy deploy-proxmox --limit vault
53
54	# Dry-run the MWAN VM playbook
55	go run goodkind.io/configs/cmd/configs deploy deploy-mwan --check --diff
56
57	# Configure the testbed failover LXC
58	go run goodkind.io/configs/cmd/configs deploy deploy-mwan-failover --limit mwan_failover_test_servers
59
60	# Configure the testbed OPNsense
61	go run goodkind.io/configs/cmd/configs deploy deploy-opnsense --limit opnsense_test_servers
62
63	# Suburban-only testbed extras
64	go run goodkind.io/configs/cmd/configs deploy deploy-testbed --limit suburban
65	```
66
67	## Rake Shortcuts
68
69	The [ansible/Rakefile](../../../ansible/Rakefile) wraps the same invocations:
70
71	```bash
72	rake help
73	rake deploy:proxmox[vault]
74	rake check:mwan
75	rake syntax:all
76	rake inventory
77	```
78
79	## Notes
80
81	- The helper sets `cwd` to [ansible/](../../../ansible/) so `ansible.cfg` and
82	  dynamic inventory resolve. The rake tasks do the same.
83	- The vault password file is `~/.config/ansible/vault.pass`.
84	- For a single deploy of a non-MWAN service, such as proxy, adguard, ddns, or
85	  tack, pass the matching `deploy-<service>` stem to the helper.
86
87	## Debugging Failures
88
89	When a playbook fails, investigate the root cause before adding workarounds:
90
91	1. If a variable is missing, trace where it should come from, such as inventory,
92	   `set_fact`, or `hostvars`.
93	2. If a variable name is wrong, check dynamic inventory names, such as
94	   `proxmox_type` versus `proxmox_vmtype`.
95	3. If validation fails, check whether the validation logic itself is broken.
96	4. If a task is skipped unexpectedly, check whether a `when` condition is too
97	   restrictive.
98
99	Do not add `| default()` or `when: var is defined` without first understanding
100	why the variable is missing.
101
### Assistant (2026-07-06 21:06)
[tool: Read] {"file_path":"/Users/agoodkind/Sites/configs.wt-ifmgr-scaffold/mwan/wpa/README.md"}
[tool output]
1	# AT&T 802.1X Certificates
2
3	Certificates are not stored in this git repository for security reasons.
4
5	They must be manually copied from OPNsense to the mwan VM before `wpa_supplicant` can
6	authenticate. On OPNsense, the certs live under `/conf/opnatt/wpa/`. On the mwan VM,
7	they belong in `/etc/wpa_supplicant/` with `600` permissions. Copy them using `scp`
8	from the OPNsense console via the direct IPv6 address.
9
10	The three required files are the AT&T CA certificate, the client certificate, and the
11	private key. The Ansible playbook checks for their presence and warns if any are missing.
12
### Assistant (2026-07-06 21:06)
[tool: Read] {"file_path":"/Users/agoodkind/Sites/configs.wt-ifmgr-scaffold/.agents/skills/ansible-quality/SKILL.md"}
[tool output]
1	---
2	name: ansible-quality
3	description: >-
4	  Run Ansible playbook quality checks and apply common Ansible fixes in the
5	  configs repo. Use when editing Ansible YAML, reviewing playbooks, or
6	  debugging Ansible failures.
7	disable-model-invocation: true
8	---
9
10	# Ansible Quality Checks
11
12	## Debugging: Fix Root Causes, Not Symptoms
13
14	When a variable is missing or a validation fails, investigate **why** before adding defensive code.
15
16	### Anti-pattern: Bandaid Defaults and Defensive `when`
17
18	- **Rule (enforced)**: Never infer a value from whether it was set, in any form: not `| default(...)`, not `is defined`, not `.get(key, default)` (a default in disguise), not any `| length` comparison (an "is this set" or "how big" check in disguise), and not `lookup(..., default=...)` (an env-presence default in disguise). The linter lists every banned line, not one per repeated snippet. Declare every input value explicitly in the service's group_vars (or `service_mapping.yml` or OpenTofu) and read it bare; a missing value must fail at load time, not silently default. There is no automatic exception, not even for a register or command result. The only defensible defensive read is a command result from an outside service that is unset more often than not, and that is the author's judgment to defend in review. Otherwise restructure: declare the value, gate with the module's own `failed_when`/`changed_when`, or initialize an accumulator with `set_fact`. `when:` is for logic branches between actions, driven by an explicit flag, not defensive programming.
19	- **Enforcement**: `configs lint` flags every occurrence. The deploy command runs it before each deploy, the lint path runs it, and pre-commit runs it on staged files. There is no per-line escape hatch and no allowlist; the check grants no exception, so a genuine outside-service case is the author's call to defend, not the check's to allow.
20	- **Symptoms**:
21	  - Validation tasks failing for values that should exist
22	  - Variables unexpectedly empty despite being "set"
23	  - Playbooks silently skipping tasks that should run
24	- **Root Cause Investigation**:
25	  1. **Trace the variable source**: Is it from inventory, `set_fact`, `register`, or hostvars?
26	  2. **Check variable naming**: Proxmox plugin provides `proxmox_type`, not `proxmox_vmtype`. Dynamic inventories have specific variable names.
27	  3. **Check play/task ordering**: Variables set in one play are not automatically available in another without `hostvars`.
28	  4. **Check inventory composition**: Does the relevant Proxmox plugin file ([ansible/inventory/vault.proxmox.yml](../../../ansible/inventory/vault.proxmox.yml) or [ansible/inventory/suburban.proxmox.yml](../../../ansible/inventory/suburban.proxmox.yml)) compose the variable you expect? For example, `ansible_proxmox_vmid: proxmox_vmid`.
29	- **Example**:
30
31	```yaml
32	# BAD - bandaid that hides the real problem
33	type: "{{ proxmox_vmtype | default('lxc') }}"
34
35	# BAD - defensive when that masks missing data
36	- name: Configure service
37	  ansible.builtin.template:
38	    src: config.j2
39	    dest: /etc/service/config
40	  when: service_config is defined
41
42	# GOOD - when for actual logic branches
43	- name: Configure IPv6
44	  ansible.builtin.template:
45	    src: ipv6.j2
46	    dest: /etc/network/ipv6
47	  when: enable_ipv6 | bool
48
49	# GOOD - fix at the source
50	# If proxmox_vmtype is missing, add it to the per-hypervisor Proxmox
51	# plugin file composition ([ansible/inventory/vault.proxmox.yml](../../../ansible/inventory/vault.proxmox.yml)
52	# or [ansible/inventory/suburban.proxmox.yml](../../../ansible/inventory/suburban.proxmox.yml)):
53	#   compose:
54	#     proxmox_vmtype: proxmox_type
55	```
56
57	- **Checklist before adding `| default()` or `is defined`**:
58	  1. Where is this variable supposed to come from?
59	  2. Is it a naming mismatch, such as `proxmox_type` versus `proxmox_vmtype`?
60	  3. Is it missing from inventory composition?
61	  4. Is it set in a different play that has not run yet?
62	  5. Only add defensive defaults after confirming the source is correct.
63
64	## Line Length Limits
65
66	- **Prefer**: Stay below 80 columns for readability.
67	- **Acceptable**: Up to 90 columns is okay.
68	- **Hard Limit**: 120 columns is the absolute maximum. Use it only when unavoidable.
69	- **Check**: All YAML files should respect these limits.
70	- **Fix**: Break long lines using:
71	  - YAML block scalars (`>-`, `|`) with proper Jinja2 whitespace control (`{{-`, `-}}`).
72	  - Jinja2 string concatenation.
73	  - Variable extraction for repeated long strings.
74
75	```yaml
76	# BAD - exceeds 120 columns
77	url: "https://{{ proxmox_api_host }}:8006/api2/json/nodes/{{ target_node }}/lxc/{{ container_result.vmid }}/interfaces"
78
79	# BAD - `>-` converts newline to space, creating `/lxc/ {{-` with unwanted space
80	url: >-
81	  "https://{{ proxmox_api_host }}:8006/api2/json/nodes/{{ target_node }}/lxc/
82	  {{- container_result.vmid }}/interfaces"
83
84	# GOOD - uses `-}}` to strip trailing whitespace and `{{-` on same line
85	url: >-
86	  "https://{{ proxmox_api_host }}:8006/api2/json/nodes/{{ target_node -}}/lxc/{{-
87	  container_result.vmid }}/interfaces"
88	```
89
90	## YAML Formatting Issues
91
92	### Folded Block Scalars (`>-`) with URLs
93
94	- **Problem**: YAML `>-` folded block scalars replace newlines with spaces, breaking URLs split across lines.
95	- **Check**: Any `url:` field using `>-` with multi-line URLs.
96	- **Fix**:
97	  - For simple URLs, use single-line quoted strings.
98	  - For long URLs that must be broken, use `-}}` on the previous variable to strip trailing whitespace, and place `{{-` on the same line as the preceding text to avoid newline spaces.
99
100	### Quoted Strings Inside Folded Scalars
101
102	- **Problem**: When using `>-`, surrounding the value in quotes makes the quotes part of the string. This can produce errors like `unknown url type: "https` when used with `ansible.builtin.uri`.
103	- **Check**:
104	  - `url: >-` or `Authorization: >-` where the folded block contains a leading `"` or trailing `"`.
105	  - Ansible errors containing `unknown url type: \"https` or a URL that begins with `"https`.
106	- **Fix**:
107	  - If you use `>-`, do not add surrounding quotes inside the block.
108	  - Keep whitespace control (`{{-`, `-}}`) when you must wrap long templated values.
109
110	### Blockinfile with ExecStart
111
112	- **Problem**: YAML `>-` in `blockinfile` content can be included literally in output files, such as systemd service files.
113	- **Check**: Any `blockinfile` task with `block: |` or `block: >-` containing `ExecStart` or other commands.
114	- **Fix**: Use `block: |` and ensure no `>-` appears in the block content itself.
115
116	### YAML Operators Inside `shell:` Blocks
117
118	- **Problem**: YAML block scalar operators like `>-` are only meaningful in YAML. If you put `>-` inside a `shell: |` command block, it is passed to the program as a literal argument.
119	- **Check**:
120	  - Any `shell: |` or `ansible.builtin.shell: |` block that contains `>-` or `|` as command text.
121	  - Shell commands that use `>-` as line continuation, such as `htpasswd -nb >- "{{ user }}" ...`.
122	- **Fix**:
123	  - Use YAML formatting for YAML, not inside shell command text.
124	  - Prefer `ansible.builtin.command` with `argv:` or a dedicated Ansible module.
125	  - If multi-line shell is required, use shell line continuations (`\`) or a heredoc.
126
127	```yaml
128	# BAD - `>-` is a literal shell argument
129	- ansible.builtin.shell: |
130	    htpasswd -nb >-
131	      "{{ user }}" >-
132	      "{{ pass }}" >-
133	      /etc/traefik/auth/dashboard-users
134
135	# GOOD - command argv, output captured and written via copy
136	- ansible.builtin.command:
137	    argv: ["htpasswd", "-nbB", "{{ user }}", "{{ pass }}"]
138	  register: htpasswd_out
139	  changed_when: false
140	  no_log: true
141
142	- ansible.builtin.copy:
143	    dest: /etc/traefik/auth/dashboard-users
144	    content: "{{ htpasswd_out.stdout }}\n"
145	    mode: "0600"
146	  no_log: true
147	```
148
149	### Systemd-networkd Section Merging
150
151	- **Fact**: systemd-networkd does not merge duplicate sections. Only the first `[Section]` is processed.
152	- **Check**: Any `blockinfile` that might create duplicate sections, such as `[DHCPv6]`.
153	- **Fix**: Use `lineinfile` with `regexp` and `insertafter`, or ensure the section does not exist before using `blockinfile`.
154
155	## Variable Safety
156
157	### Undefined Variable References
158
159	- **Problem**: Referencing variables in `set_fact` that are defined in the same task fails because variables are set concurrently.
160	- **Check**: Any `set_fact` task where one variable references another variable defined in the same task.
161	- **Fix**: Split into multiple sequential `set_fact` tasks.
162	- **Common gotcha**: Pipeline facts like `filtered_ipv6` to `container_primary_ip` must be split. Later keys in the same `set_fact` cannot see earlier keys.
163
164	```yaml
165	# BAD - variables set concurrently
166	- set_fact:
167	    var1: "value"
168	    var2: "{{ var1 }}-suffix"
169
170	# GOOD
171	- set_fact:
172	    var1: "value"
173
174	- set_fact:
175	    var2: "{{ var1 }}-suffix"
176	```
177
178	### Jinja2 Filter Safety
179
180	- **Problem**: Using `first` on empty lists causes `No first item, sequence was empty`.
181	- **Check**: Any Jinja2 expression using `first` without checking list length.
182	- **Fix**: Use array indexing with length checks.
183
184	```yaml
185	# BAD - fails on empty list
186	ip: "{{ ip_list | first }}"
187
188	# GOOD
189	ip: "{{ ip_list[0] if (ip_list | length > 0) else '' }}"
190	```
191
192	## KEA DHCP Configuration
193
194	- DHCPv4: `hw-address` and `client-id` are mutually exclusive in reservations.
195	- DHCPv6: `hw-address` and `duid` are mutually exclusive in reservations.
196	- Use only one identifier per reservation. Prefer `hw-address` when MAC is pinned.
197
198	## Linting and Verification
199
200	### Ansible-lint Timing
201
202	- `ansible-lint` is not instant. Wait 2 to 5 seconds after making changes before checking linter output.
203	- The linter needs time to analyze YAML syntax, Jinja2 templates, and module usage.
204	- If linter errors appear immediately after a fix, wait a few seconds and re-check.
205
206	## Pre-commit Checklist
207
208	Before committing Ansible changes, verify:
209
210	1. Line length prefers less than 80, accepts 90, and never exceeds 120 columns unless unavoidable.
211	2. No `url:` fields use `>-` with multi-line URLs unless Jinja2 whitespace control is correct.
212	3. No `url: >-` or `Authorization: >-` values contain surrounding quotes.
213	4. No `shell: |` blocks contain YAML operators like `>-` used as line continuation.
214	5. No `blockinfile` blocks contain literal `>-` in command output.
215	6. No `set_fact` tasks reference variables defined in the same task.
216	7. No `first` filter is used without empty-list checks.
217	8. No KEA reservations use mutually exclusive identifiers.
218	9. No `blockinfile` creates duplicate systemd-networkd sections. Use `lineinfile` instead.
219

2
3	Current state for the OPNsense testbed VM (`opnsense-test`) on suburban. Use

11	## Current state
12
13	- VM `101` (`opnsense-test`) is the suburban OPNsense testbed VM.
14	- The OPNsense VM has one NIC backed by the `vmbrtrunk` VLAN-aware bridge.
15	  FreeBSD names it `vtnet0`.
16	- The MANAGEMENT interface (`opt9` in `config.xml`) carries `10.240.4.1/24` and
17	  `3d06:bad:b01:204::1/64`. Suburban joins the same broadcast domain via a

24	  and TCP port 22 is open there.
25	- The host-side OPNsense gRPC target is
26	  `unix:///var/run/qemu-server/101.mwanrpc`.
27	- The named virtio-console port is `io.goodkind.mwan-opnsense.0`.
28	- The guest-side daemon serial path is `/dev/ttyV0.1` when
29	  `/dev/vtcon/io.goodkind.mwan-opnsense.0` points there.

1	# OPNsense Testbed Config Import
2
3	This runbook is current guidance for importing a production-shaped OPNsense
4	`config.xml` into suburban testbed VM `101` (`opnsense-test`).
5
6	## Core Rules
7
8	Restore each candidate config onto a wiped or freshly restored OPNsense
9	testbed baseline. Do not layer candidate configs on top of an already-mutated
10	router state.
11
12	Do not use MWN1, the OPNsense gRPC helper exposed by `mwan-opnsense`, as the
13	reload mechanism during config-import debugging. Use direct console, QEMU Guest
14	Agent, or SSH for restore and reload. Test MWN1 only after the router is stable
15	again.
16
17	Use the serial console while reloads or reboots are in progress. If SSH drops,
18	continue observing through the console path.
19
20	`revertBackup` swaps the entire `/conf/config.xml`, which includes the `<apikeys>` block. The testbed substitutions transform produces an XML with no API keys at all, so the freshly-imported OPNsense has no API access until you mint one. After every import, mint a fresh root API key via the PHP `OPNsense\Auth\API->createKey('root')` helper and write the resulting key and secret into [ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml).
21
22	## Every Change Gate
23
24	Run this gate for every config change, including small XML edits.
25
26	### 1. Scope Check
27
28	- Confirm the target is suburban OPNsense VM `101` (`opnsense-test`).
29	- Confirm commands do not reference `vault`, production OPNsense, production VM
30	  `113`, or production LXC `116`.
31	- Confirm the intended hypervisor is `suburban`.
32
33	### 2. Baseline Capture
34
35	- Capture Proxmox VM state and QEMU config.
36	- Capture OPNsense `/conf/config.xml` hash and byte size.
37	- Verify QEMU Guest Agent ping and guest hostname.
38	- Verify the serial console path is reachable.
39	- Verify SSH reachability only as a convenience signal, not as recovery proof.
40
41	### 3. Backup Before Mutation
42
43	- Take a Proxmox snapshot without `--vmstate 1`.
44	- Back up the raw `/conf/config.xml`.
45	- Record the pre-change config hash.
46	- Write down the rollback command before applying anything.
47
48	### 4. Apply Method
49
50	- Restore the candidate config onto a wiped or freshly restored OPNsense
51	  baseline.
52	- Do not use MWN1 for reload.
53	- Use direct console, QEMU Guest Agent, or SSH for config restore and reload.
54	- Watch the serial console during reload or reboot.
55
56	### 5. During Reload
57
58	- Watch serial console output.
59	- Tail relevant OPNsense logs, especially `configd` and system logs.
60	- Record the exact command that hangs, exits, or drops connectivity.
61	- Do not call a reload hung without console or log evidence.
62
63	### 6. Post-Change Validation
64
65	- QEMU Guest Agent works.
66	- Serial console is responsive.
67	- SSH is reachable.
68	- Web UI TCP `443` is reachable.
69	- DNS returns `NOERROR`.
70	- Basic `configctl` actions work.
71	- Interface device bindings match the expected testbed topology.
72	- Default routes and gateways are sane.
73	- pf rules load.
74	- NAT sanity checks pass.
75	- FRR/BGP state is sane if FRR is expected.
76	- `mwan opnsense version -target <target>` returns a daemon build banner after
77	  the router is stable.
78
79	### 7. Failure Rule
80
81	- If any baseline check fails, stop.
82	- Roll back immediately.
83	- Re-run the entire baseline after rollback.
84	- Record the failing command, relevant logs, and active config hash.

[tool output]
1	# Testbed DNS and NAT64
2
3	How name resolution works on the suburban testbed, and how to recover it when a
4	rebuilt testbed OPNsense comes up with DNS broken. The testbed is IPv6 primary:
5	its simulated ISPs (LXC 200/201/202) carry IPv4 transit only and no public IPv6,
6	so IPv6-only guests reach the IPv4 internet through NAT64 plus DNS64. Live
7	definitions are owned by [opentofu/suburban/](../../opentofu/suburban/) and the
8	testbed group vars; update this page when they change.
9
10	## Components
11
12	| Piece | Where | Address / prefix | Source of truth |
13	| --- | --- | --- | --- |
14	| Tayga (NAT64 translator) | testbed OPNsense (VM 101/102), `os-tayga` plugin | v6 prefix `3d06:bad:b01:2664::/96`, tun `nat64` at `3d06:bad:b01:264::ffff:1`, v4 pool `10.250.64.0/24` | `<tayga>` block in the imported `config.xml` (prod prefix `3d06:bad:b01:6464::/96` rewritten to `3d06:bad:b01:2664::/96` by the config transform) |
15	| DNS64 resolver (bind9) | LXC 464 `dns64-suburban` | `3d06:bad:b01:204::464`, synthesizes AAAA into `2664::/96` | [dns64_suburban_servers.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/dns64_suburban_servers.yml), deployed by `deploy-dns64.yml --limit dns64_suburban_servers` |
16	| Unbound (LAN resolver) | testbed OPNsense | binds all interfaces, `:53` | imported `config.xml` |
17
18	The DNS64 LXC forwards upstream to `3d06:bad:b01:2664::101:101`, which is
19	`1.1.1.1` expressed in the NAT64 prefix, so its own recursion rides the Tayga
20	path. `dns64_force_synth` is true so dual-stack names also resolve over NAT64
21	(native testbed IPv6 has no public transit).
22
23	## Recovering DNS on a rebuilt testbed OPNsense
24
25	A freshly imported testbed OPNsense (host key changes, so use diagnostics-only
26	relaxed host checking) tends to come up with DNS down for these reasons, in the
27	order you hit them.
28
29	1. **Unbound will not start because the python DNSBL module file is missing.**
30	   The prod config import leaves Unbound configured with `module-config: "python
31	   validator iterator"` and `python-script: unbound-dnsbl/dnsbl_module.py`, but
32	   the rebuilt box has no `dnsbl_module.py`, so Unbound exits at init with
33	   `fatal error: bad config during init for python module`. DNSBL is
34	   `<enabled>0</enabled>` in the config yet the python wrapper still renders on
35	   26.1. Recover by regenerating the module and clearing the stale pid:
36
37	   ```sh
38	   configctl unbound dnsbl       # regenerates /var/unbound/unbound-dnsbl/dnsbl_module.py
39	   service unbound onestop       # clears the stale pidfile from the crashed start
40	   service unbound onestart
41	   ```
42
43	2. **Tayga daemon is down.** The `nat64` tun interface and the `2664::/96` route
44	   can persist while the translator is not running. There is no `rc.d/tayga`
45	   script (the plugin uses `opnsense-tayga` via configd), so start it with:
46
47	   ```sh
48	   configctl tayga start
49	   ```
50
51	   Verify translation from the OPNsense with `ping6 3d06:bad:b01:2664::1.1.1.1`.
52
53	3. **The DNS64 LXC (CT 464) may be stopped.** Check from the suburban hypervisor
54	   (`root@[3d06:bad:b01:200::1]`) with `pct status 464`, start it with
55	   `pct start 464`, and confirm `named` runs inside it.
56
57	Diagnostic note: `sockstat` and `pgrep` need `sudo` on the OPNsense to show the
58	root-owned Unbound and Tayga; without it they falsely report nothing on `:53`.
59
60	## Access paths
61
62	| Target | Path |
63	| --- | --- |
64	| Testbed OPNsense | `ssh -J root@[3d06:bad:b01:200::1] agoodkind@10.250.250.2` (ProxyJump through the suburban hypervisor; relax host-key checking after a rebuild) |
65	| DNS64 LXC (CT 464) | `pct exec 464 ...` from the suburban hypervisor `root@[3d06:bad:b01:200::1]` |
66	| Testbed MWAN VM 950 | `ssh root@3d06:bad:b01:204::950` |
67
68	## How VM 950 reaches DNS
69
70	VM 950 management sits on the `vmbrtrunk` `204::` services LAN, the same segment
71	as the testbed OPNsense MANAGEMENT interface (`opt9`, `3d06:bad:b01:204::1`) and
72	the DNS64 LXC (`3d06:bad:b01:204::464`). This mirrors production, where the MWAN
73	VM `enmgmt0` shares the OPNsense LAN `/64` and reaches DNS on-link.
74	`test_mwan_servers.yml` sets `mwan_dns_servers` to the on-link OPNsense Unbound at
75	`3d06:bad:b01:204::1`, so VM 950 resolves A records there and reaches them over
76	its IPv4 WAN. The OPNsense Unbound does not synthesize DNS64; that path is for the
77	IPv6-only LAN guests that point at the DNS64 LXC instead. The `204::` segment and
78	the resolver are codified in
79	[opentofu/suburban/vms.tf](../../opentofu/suburban/vms.tf) and
80	[test_mwan_servers.yml](../../ansible/inventory/group_vars/test_mwan_servers.yml).
81
82	## Reproducibility gaps
83
84	These still need to move from manual recovery into the deploy path:
85
86	- The config transform
87	  ([testbed/opnsense/substitutions.yaml](../../testbed/opnsense/substitutions.yaml))
88	  should disable the Unbound DNSBL python module for the testbed (it carries no
89	  blocklist data), and `deploy-opnsense.yml` should restart Unbound and Tayga
90	  after the import so they come up without manual `configctl` calls.
91	- The config transform rewrites the prod Unbound forwarder
92	  (`3d06:bad:b01:200::53`) to a public resolver (`2606:4700:4700::1111`). On the
93	  IPv6-only testbed that target is only reachable through NAT64, so forwarding
94	  still depends on the testbed having working upstream transit; a rebuilt
95	  OPNsense that has not converged BGP/DNS yet returns no answers until it does.
96

1	# OPNsense UI testing
2
3	Use this page when a local browser needs to reach an OPNsense UI page through
4	an SSH forward. The forwarding values come from the current testbed inventory
5	and access documentation, so this page does not own hostnames, addresses, or
6	site-specific ports.
7
8	## Sources
9
10	Read the current access path before opening a tunnel:
11
12	- [Suburban testbed](../infra/suburban-testbed.md) defines the testbed host and
13	  virtual machine layout.
14	- [OPNsense testbed baseline](testbed-baseline.md) defines the OPNsense guest
15	  role and management expectations.
16	- [Access](../infra/access.md) defines operator access patterns.
17
18	Use the service repository for service-specific UI paths. For the Cloudflared
19	OPNsense plugin, the settings page path is:
20
21	```text
22	/ui/cloudflared/settings
23	```
24
25	## Inputs
26
27	Set these values from the current inventory or the service under test:
28
29	```sh
30	LOCAL_BIND_HOST='<local browser bind host>'
31	LOCAL_PORT='<unused local port>'
32	JUMP_HOST='<optional ssh jump host>'
33	TARGET_SSH='<ssh target for the OPNsense host>'
34	REMOTE_HOST='<host as seen from TARGET_SSH>'
35	REMOTE_PORT='<OPNsense UI port as seen from TARGET_SSH>'
36	REMOTE_PATH='<OPNsense UI path for the page under test>'
37	```
38
39	Leave `JUMP_HOST` empty when direct SSH access reaches `TARGET_SSH`.
40
41	## Forward
42
43	Run the direct form when the target is reachable without a jump host:
44
45	```sh
46	ssh -N \
47	    -L "${LOCAL_BIND_HOST}:${LOCAL_PORT}:${REMOTE_HOST}:${REMOTE_PORT}" \
48	    "${TARGET_SSH}"
49	```
50
51	Run the jump form when the access documentation requires a jump host:
52
53	```sh
54	ssh -N \
55	    -L "${LOCAL_BIND_HOST}:${LOCAL_PORT}:${REMOTE_HOST}:${REMOTE_PORT}" \
56	    -J "${JUMP_HOST}" \
57	    "${TARGET_SSH}"
58	```
59
60	Keep this terminal open while the browser test runs.
61
62	## View
63
64	Build the local browser URL from the forwarding inputs:
65
66	```sh
67	LOCAL_URL="https://${LOCAL_BIND_HOST}:${LOCAL_PORT}${REMOTE_PATH}"
68	printf '%s\n' "${LOCAL_URL}"
69	```
70
71	For testbed systems that use a self-signed or locally issued certificate,
72	expect browser automation to ignore certificate errors only for this local
73	test run.
74
75	## Capture
76
77	Use headless Chrome when the change needs proof that the actual forwarded page
78	renders:
79
80	```sh
81	CHROME_BIN="${CHROME_BIN:-/Applications/Google Chrome.app/Contents/MacOS/Google Chrome}"
82	SCREENSHOT_PATH="${SCREENSHOT_PATH:-.context/artifacts/opnsense-ui.png}"
83
84	"${CHROME_BIN}" \
85	    --headless=new \
86	    --disable-gpu \
87	    --ignore-certificate-errors \
88	    --screenshot="${SCREENSHOT_PATH}" \
89	    "${LOCAL_URL}"
90	```
91
92	For the Cloudflared OPNsense plugin settings page, set:
93
94	```sh
95	REMOTE_PATH='/ui/cloudflared/settings'
96	SCREENSHOT_PATH='.context/artifacts/cloudflared-settings.png'
97	```
98
99	The screenshot proves that the browser reached the forwarded OPNsense UI page.
100	It does not prove that a plugin change is installed, so pair it with the
101	plugin repository's install, restart, and validation steps.
102
103	## Stop
104
105	Stop the forwarding command with `Control-C` after the browser test finishes.

1	# OPNsense 25.7 config-import flow

3	Target: VM 101 in our suburban testbed, running `OPNsense 25.7 (amd64)` build `25.7-n271606-9af17f0102ca` on `FreeBSD 14.3-RELEASE-p1`. Source citations resolve against `github.com/opnsense/core` tag `25.7` (commit `bbd245bb098cef5a30faa0221238b823c1e49836`, peeled `17d0a22a053233296c5c80d4f8f2e2f349f2ba7d`) and tag `25.7.10` (commit `bb09f97a80aa586de7c8b4b1a069f146a22fa473`, peeled `c2f076f3041d37d59ba219773e5bb34b0a05c7f7`). 4
5	## TL;DR call graph
6
7	```
8	diag_backup.php POST mode=restore
9	    -> Config::restoreBackup(tmpfile)
10	        -> Config::overwrite(tmpfile)        # flock(LOCK_EX) + truncate + write + chmod 0640
11	        -> Config::load()                    # simplexml_load_string, validates only XML well-formedness
12	    -> parse_config()                        # rebuild $config global
13	    -> (only if keepconsole or rrddata) write_config() + convert_config()
14	        -> run_migrations.php                # per-model BaseModel::runMigrations()
15	        -> pluginctl -i                      # register pluggable interfaces
16	        -> firmware/register.php sync        # release-type / plugin sync
17	        -> Config::forceReload(); parse_config()
18	    -> if is_interface_mismatch(false): cancel reboot, route operator to interfaces_assign.php
19	    -> if flush_history: configd_run('system flush config_history')
20	    -> if rebootafterrestore and not mismatched: configd_run('system reboot', true)
21	        -> /usr/local/etc/rc.reboot -> rc.syshook stop -> shutdown -or now
22	            -> reboot -> /usr/local/etc/rc -> /usr/local/etc/rc.bootup
23	                -> convert_config()          # ALWAYS runs on boot
24	                -> system_devd_configure, system_login_configure
25	                -> if is_interface_mismatch(): set_networking_interfaces_ports(true)
26	                                              # interactive console prompt; blocks boot
27	                -> ordered *_configure() chain (interfaces, filter, plugins, dns, dhcp, ...)
28	```
29
30	The parts that look surprising:
31
32	- `restoreBackup()` itself does not migrate the schema. Migration only runs on the `keepconsole` or `rrddata` GUI paths, or via the post-reboot `rc.bootup` call.
33	- The REST API has no upload-and-replace endpoint at all in core 25.7.
34	- A `cp /conf/config.xml + reboot` IS the canonical hot path for "load a foreign XML and bring it up", because `rc.bootup` runs the same migration entry point and the same ordered service-reconfigure chain.
35	- The GUI postpones the reboot if any interface name in the new XML does not exist on the host. On a `cp + reboot`, the same check fires inside `rc.bootup` and drops the boot to an interactive console prompt that reads `php://stdin`.
36
37	## 1. Entry points
38
39	### 1.1 GUI (System -> Configuration -> Backups)
40
41	URL: `https://<host>/diag_backup.php`. Single PHP file at `src/www/diag_backup.php`. Request mode is dispatched by the `restore` POST field (`diag_backup.php:201-202`). Citation: `github.com/opnsense/core` tag `25.7`, file `src/www/diag_backup.php`, lines `200-372`.
42
43	Two restore modes share the same form:
44
45	- **Full restore**: empty `restorearea[]`. Calls `Config::restoreBackup()` with the uploaded tmpfile (`diag_backup.php:317-318`).
46	- **Partial restore**: one or more `restorearea[]` values (e.g. `interfaces`, `bridges`, `vlans`, `gifs`, `laggs`, `ppps`, `wireless`, `rrddata`, plus any sections registered via `plugins_xmlrpc_sync()`). Calls `restore_config_section()` (`diag_backup.php:48-151`) which merges the chosen sections into the in-memory `$config`, calls `write_config()`, then `convert_config()` (line `147`). The GUI hides this with a confirmation dialog warning that section restores can break referential integrity (`diag_backup.php:466-490`).
47
48	Submit-button name is `restore` (`diag_backup.php:605`). The form posts `multipart/form-data` with file field `conffile`, optional `decrypt`/`decrypt_password` for AES-encrypted backups, and check fields `rebootafterrestore`, `keepconsole`, `flush_history`. Reboot-after-restore is the GET-side default (`diag_backup.php:179`).
49
50	ACL coverage: `<page-diagnostics-backup-restore>` matches `diag_backup.php*` (`src/opnsense/mvc/app/models/OPNsense/Core/ACL/ACL.xml`).
51
52	### 1.2 REST API
53
54	ACL pattern `api/core/backup/*` is registered for `<page-diagnostics-configurationhistory>` (`ACL.xml`). The controller is `BackupController` in `src/opnsense/mvc/app/controllers/OPNsense/Core/Api/BackupController.php` (210 lines on tag `25.7`). Public endpoints, derived directly from `public function *Action` methods:
55
56	| Method | Path | Purpose |
57	| --- | --- | --- |
58	| `GET`  | `/api/core/backup/providers`                        | list configured backup providers (`This Firewall`, OPNcentral, etc.) |
59	| `GET`  | `/api/core/backup/backups/{host}`                   | list `config-*.xml` files under the provider directory |
60	| `GET`  | `/api/core/backup/diff/{host}/{backup1}/{backup2}`  | unified diff of two existing local backups |
61	| `POST` | `/api/core/backup/deleteBackup/{backup}`            | unlink one local backup file |
62	| `POST` | `/api/core/backup/revertBackup/{backup}`            | call `Config::restoreBackup()` against an existing local backup file |
63	| `GET`  | `/api/core/backup/download/{host}[/{backup}]`       | download a backup as `application/octet-stream` |
64
65	Citation: `BackupController.php:84-209`. Verified against the live file on VM 101 at `/usr/local/opnsense/mvc/app/controllers/OPNsense/Core/Api/BackupController.php` (210 lines, identical method set).
66
67	**There is no upload-and-replace endpoint in core 25.7**. `revertBackup` only accepts a basename of an existing file under `/conf/backup/config-*.xml`. The REST API cannot receive a foreign XML and apply it. A live grep on VM 101 for `upload`, `restoreXmlConfig`, `restore_xml`, `importXml`, `importConfig` under the Core controllers directory returned no matches.
68
69	### 1.3 configctl
70
71	A live `configctl` enumeration on VM 101 (full output captured in this research) lists no `system restore` or `backup restore` action. The system-related actions are: `remote backup`, `event config_changed`, `flush config_history`, `reboot`, `ha_reconfigure_backup`, `trust configure`, etc. Citation: `/usr/local/opnsense/service/conf/actions.d/actions_system.conf` on VM 101 (full text included in research notes); upstream equivalent at `src/opnsense/service/conf/actions.d/actions_system.conf` tag `25.7`.
72
73	`configctl system reboot` is the post-import reboot trigger that `diag_backup.php` itself uses (`configd_run('system reboot', true)` at `diag_backup.php:685`).
74
75	### 1.4 Direct file replacement plus reboot
76
77	`/conf/config.xml` is the on-disk source of truth. Boot path:
78
79	1. `init` runs `/etc/rc autoboot`, which `exec`s `/usr/local/etc/rc` (header at `/etc/rc:3`).
80	2. `/usr/local/etc/rc` mounts filesystems, recovers users, initializes syshooks and PHP, then `flock`-launches `/usr/local/etc/rc.bootup` (line ~ near the end of `/usr/local/etc/rc`).
81	3. `rc.bootup` is a PHP script. After requiring core includes, **its first stateful action is `convert_config()`** (`src/etc/rc.bootup:24` on tag `25.7`). The author's comment on the `25.7` tag explicitly states this is for the "import or restore or reset" case.
82	4. After migration, `rc.bootup` runs an ordered chain of `*_configure()` calls (lines 26-60), then `exit(0)`.
83
84	So `cp /conf/config.xml + reboot` IS a supported entry point and triggers the same migration step the GUI calls in the keepconsole/rrddata path. It does NOT trigger the GUI's `flush_history` step, and it does NOT preserve console settings the way `keepconsole=1` does.
85
86	## 2. Canonical PHP handler call graph
87
88	For the **full-restore** GUI path used by a production-shaped XML import:
89
90	1. `is_uploaded_file($_FILES['conffile']['tmp_name'])` (`diag_backup.php:260`) and decrypt branch (`:269-275`).
91	2. Save current console fields into `$csettings` (`:303-313`).
92	3. Write decrypted bytes back over the tmpfile (`:316`).
93	4. `Config::getInstance()->restoreBackup($filename)` (`:318`):
94	   - If current config is valid, snapshot the in-memory simplexml + filehandle, then `overwrite($filename)` and `load()`. If `load()` throws, restore the snapshot via `save(null, true)` and return false (`Config.php:653-669`).
95	   - `overwrite()` does `fopen("a+e") + flock(LOCK_EX) + ftruncate(0) + fwrite(file_get_contents($filename))` then `chmod 0640` (`Config.php:632-642`). The new bytes go into `/conf/config.xml` verbatim, with no per-field validation.
96	   - `load()` does `simplexml_load_string(stream_get_contents($fp))`. Validation is XML well-formedness only (`Config.php:375-410, 416-437`).
97	5. `parse_config()` (`diag_backup.php:322`): rebuild the global `$config` array from the new XML. Citation: `parse_config()` lives in `src/etc/inc/config.inc` and is heavily used elsewhere; it does not run migrations.
98	6. If `keepconsole` is set: copy saved console fields back into `$config['system']`, set `$flush = true` (`:323-334`).
99	7. If `$config['rrddata']` exists: import RRDs, unset that node, set `$flush = true` (`:335-340`).
100	8. If `$flush`: `write_config()` plus `convert_config()` (`:341-344`).
101	9. **Migration only runs on the `$flush` branch.** A foreign XML without `keepconsole` and without an `<rrddata>` child does NOT trigger `convert_config()` from this point.
102	10. `is_interface_mismatch(false)` (`:351`). If true, append "Postponing reboot" and clear `$do_reboot` (`:359-362`).
103	11. If `flush_history`: `configd_run('system flush config_history')` and a final `write_config()` (`:368-371`).
104	12. End-of-script: `configd_run('system reboot', true)` (`diag_backup.php:684-685`), which fires `[reboot] -> /usr/local/etc/rc.reboot -> /sbin/shutdown -or now`.
105
106	The implicit "transaction" here is only the `restoreBackup()` rollback on parse failure. After parse succeeds, every later step runs forward and any service-side failure is logged but not reverted.
107
108	## 3. REST API specifics
109
110	`POST /api/core/backup/revertBackup/{backup}`:
111
112	- Path parameter is a basename, e.g. `config-1715000000.1234.xml`. Implementation iterates `glob("/conf/backup/config-*.xml")` and matches by basename (`BackupController.php:172-181`).
113	- Request body: none required. Phalcon's `ApiControllerBase` enforces CSRF / API-key auth at the framework layer. Live behavior on the testbed (untested in this round) is that you can call this with HTTP basic API key + secret.
114	- Response: JSON `{"status":"reverted"}` on success, `{"status":"not_found"}` on miss.
115	- It calls `Config::restoreBackup(filename)` and `Config::save()` synchronously. It does NOT call `parse_config()`, `convert_config()`, or any service-reconfigure. It does NOT trigger a reboot.
116	- Privilege check: `throwReadOnly()` rejects users with `user-config-readonly` ACL (`BackupController.php:169-171, 45-52`).
117
118	This means even the REST entry point that exists is a "swap the on-disk XML, leave the live system stale" operation. It assumes a follow-up reboot (or the operator running `convert_config` and the service-reconfigure chain manually).
119
120	There is no REST endpoint that accepts an uploaded foreign XML.
121
122	## 4. Reboot vs hot-apply
123
124	The GUI default is `rebootafterrestore = true` (`diag_backup.php:179`). That default expectation is intentional: nothing in `restoreBackup()` itself reapplies routing, DHCP, firewall, IPsec, OpenVPN, plugins, or interface assignment. The `flush=true` branch only triggers `convert_config()` (which runs migrations), not service reconfigure. The reboot path does both because `rc.bootup` runs the full ordered chain.
125
126	If the operator unchecks `rebootafterrestore`, the new XML lives on disk but the kernel and services keep running with the old in-memory state until a manual reload or reboot.
127
128	A user-driven hot-apply path would require iterating the same `*_configure()` chain `rc.bootup` runs. There is no single PHP function in `25.7` that does this without a reboot.
129
130	## 5. Schema migration
131
132	`<config><version>` on VM 101 is currently `v9` (live `grep -E '<version>' /conf/config.xml`). This is the legacy top-level version. The 25.x migration model is per-model: every `BaseModel` subclass under `src/opnsense/mvc/app/models/OPNsense/*/Migrations/M*_*_*.php` is run by `run_migrations.php`. Examples present on VM 101: `OPNsense/Dnsmasq/Migrations/M1_0_0.php`, `OPNsense/IPsec/Migrations/M1_0_0..4.php`, `OPNsense/OpenVPN/Migrations/M1_0_0.php`, `OPNsense/Monit/Migrations/M1_0_0..8.php`, `OPNsense/IDS/Migrations/M1_0_0..7.php`, `OPNsense/Syslog/Migrations/M1_0_2.php`. (`find /usr/local/opnsense -path '*Migration*' -type f` on VM 101.)
133
134	`run_migrations.php` (`src/opnsense/mvc/script/run_migrations.php` on tag `25.7`) walks every model, instantiates it, calls `runMigrations()` from `BaseModel`, and reports per-model `Migrated <Class> from <pre> to <post>`. The legacy `<version>` field at the top of `config.xml` is bumped indirectly by `write_config()` writes during migration (the version constant is set in `src/etc/inc/config.lib.inc`'s `latest_config` family of helpers; not inspected here, but visible in older OPNsense source).
135
136	When migration runs:
137
138	- Always on `rc.bootup` (`src/etc/rc.bootup:24`).
139	- During GUI restore only on the `keepconsole` or `rrddata` branch (`diag_backup.php:294, 343`). A plain "upload XML, click Restore, leave keepconsole and rrddata both off" does NOT call `convert_config()` from PHP. Migration would still run on the subsequent reboot.
140	- During `rc.configure_firmware` (`src/etc/rc.configure_firmware:45`).
141	- It does not run on REST `revertBackup`.
142
143	Failure mode: per-model migrations log to the OPNsense system log and print `*** <Class> migration failed from <pre> to <post>, check log for details`. They do not abort the chain.
144
145	## 6. Service-reconfigure ordering
146
147	The order taken from `rc.bootup` lines 24-60 (tag `25.7`) is the canonical post-reboot sequence to verify after import:
148
149	1. `convert_config()` -> `run_migrations.php`, `pluginctl -i`, `firmware/register.php sync`, `Config::forceReload`, `parse_config()`.
150	2. `system_devd_configure(true)`.
151	3. `system_login_configure(true)`.
152	4. **Interface mismatch gate**: `is_interface_mismatch()` -> `set_networking_interfaces_ports(true)` (interactive console reassignment loop). This blocks the boot until the operator reassigns or every required device exists.
153	5. `interfaces_loopback_configure(true)`.
154	6. `system_kernel_configure(true)`.
155	7. `system_sysctl_configure(true)`.
156	8. `system_timezone_configure(true)`.
157	9. `system_firmware_configure(true)`.
158	10. `system_trust_configure(true)`.
159	11. `system_hostname_configure(true)`.
160	12. `system_resolver_configure(true)`.
161	13. `system_syslog_start(true)`.
162	14. `filter_configure_sync(true, false)`  (default policy before interfaces).
163	15. `interfaces_hardware(true)`.
164	16. `interfaces_configure(true)`.
165	17. `system_resolver_configure(true)`  (re-run after interfaces).
166	18. `filter_configure_sync(true)`.
167	19. `plugins_configure('early', true)`.
168	20. `system_routing_configure(true, null, 'ignore')`.
169	21. `plugins_configure('dhcp', true)`.
170	22. `plugins_configure('dns', true)`.
171	23. `filter_configure_sync(true)`  (third pass after DHCP/DNS).
172	24. `plugins_configure('monitor', true)`.
173	25. `plugins_configure('vpn', true)`.
174	26. `plugins_configure('bootup', true)`.
175	27. `system_powerd_configure(true)`.
176
177	That is 27 ordered steps with `filter_configure_sync` repeated three times. The test matrix should at minimum exercise the DHCP, DNS, VPN, monitor, and bootup plugin stages, plus `interfaces_configure` and the routing step.
178
179	## 7. Failure modes
180
181	- **Malformed XML**. `simplexml_load_string` returns false; `loadFromStream` throws `ConfigException("invalid config xml")` (`Config.php:402-406`). `restoreBackup` catches this, restores the previous in-memory simplexml, calls `save(null, true)` to write the original back to `/conf/config.xml`, and returns false (`Config.php:662-668`). The GUI surfaces `gettext("The configuration could not be restored.")` (`diag_backup.php:347`). Result: no change on disk.
182	- **Missing or wrong-shape field**. There is NO field-level validation in `restoreBackup`. The GUI accepts any well-formed XML root. Bad fields surface as runtime errors during the boot-time `*_configure()` chain or during later GUI use.
183	- **Service-reconfigure failure during the GUI flush branch**. `convert_config()` chains use `mwexecf` (non-verbose) which logs but does not abort. The flow continues. There is no rollback at this layer.
184	- **Reboot-time service failure**. `rc.bootup` does not stop on individual `*_configure()` errors. Each function decides its own logging. A service failure leaves the box running with whatever state earlier steps reached, and the boot still completes. This is a known foot-gun.
185	- **Interface name does not exist on host** (e.g. `iavf0` referenced but the box only has `vtnet0`). Two cases:
186	  - Via GUI: `is_interface_mismatch(false)` returns true, GUI cancels the reboot and links to `interfaces_assign.php` (`diag_backup.php:351-363`). The operator can fix it before triggering a reboot manually.
187	  - Via `cp + reboot`: `rc.bootup:29-32` calls `is_interface_mismatch()` and drops to `set_networking_interfaces_ports(true)` which reads `php://stdin`. On a headless or non-interactive console (vsock, Proxmox vnc, blocked serial), this stalls the boot. This is the fail-mode our prod-shaped XML transform was designed to avoid.
188	  - The `<lock>` flag inside an `<interfaces>` entry suppresses the mismatch check for that interface (`is_interface_mismatch` in `console.inc:54-83`). I have not verified whether our prod XML uses `<lock>` anywhere; if it does, that interface will not be guarded.
189
190	## 8. Comparison: `cp /conf/config.xml + reboot` vs the GUI restore path
191
192	| Step | `cp + reboot` | GUI full restore (default) | GUI full restore + `keepconsole=1` |
193	| --- | --- | --- | --- |
194	| XML well-formedness check | yes (rc.bootup load) | yes (`Config::load`) | yes |
195	| Atomic file replace under `flock(LOCK_EX)` | no (plain cp) | yes (`Config::overwrite`) | yes |
196	| `parse_config()` rebuild of `$config` | yes (rc.bootup) | yes (`diag_backup.php:322`) | yes |
197	| Console fields preserved | no | no | yes |
198	| `<rrddata>` import | no | no (unless rrddata sub-tag set) | yes when XML has `<rrddata>` |
199	| `convert_config()` runs in the import process | n/a | NO | yes |
200	| `convert_config()` runs at next boot | yes | yes | yes |
201	| `flush_history` config_history clear | no | optional (`flush_history=1`) | optional |
202	| `is_interface_mismatch` blocks reboot | no (drops to interactive prompt instead) | yes (postpone reboot, route to GUI) | yes (postpone reboot, route to GUI) |
203	| Service-reconfigure chain | yes (rc.bootup) | only on next reboot | only on next reboot |
204	| Audit log entry / revision metadata | no (we did not write through `Config::save`) | yes (Config::save audit) | yes |
205	| Backup history rotation | no | yes (Config::cleanupBackups via save) | yes |
206
207	The functional differences that matter for our case:
208
209	- The GUI atomically replaces the on-disk file under `flock(LOCK_EX)`. A naive `cp` is not atomic relative to a concurrent reader. In practice we do `cp` only when nothing else is writing, but it is a real race window. `install -m 0640 newconfig /conf/config.xml` plus `mv -f` would close it.
210	- The GUI emits an audit log entry through `Config::auditLogChange` and a backup snapshot under `/conf/backup/config-*.xml`. `cp` skips both, so we lose the rollback breadcrumb.
211	- The GUI guards against a missing-interface boot via the `is_interface_mismatch` check before reboot. `cp + reboot` does not, so a bad transform headlessly jams the boot.
212	- The GUI does not do any extra service reload beyond what the next reboot does (assuming `keepconsole` and `rrddata` are off). Our `cp + reboot` is therefore equivalent in service-reconfigure terms.
213	- The GUI does not migrate the schema in-process either (default branch); both paths rely on the next-boot `convert_config()` for that.
214
215	## Practical recommendation for config import
216
217	Use **direct file replacement + reboot** for automated testbed imports, and adopt three of the GUI's safety practices:
218
219	1. **Pre-import interface gate**: before writing the new XML, walk the new `<interfaces>` entries and confirm each `<if>` value resolves to an existing kernel device, treating any mismatch as a hard stop. This replicates the GUI's `is_interface_mismatch` check and prevents the `rc.bootup` interactive-console stall.
220	2. **Atomic write**: replace `cp` with `install -m 0640 -o root -g wheel <new> /conf/config.xml.new && mv -f /conf/config.xml.new /conf/config.xml`. The mv is atomic on UFS/ZFS within the same filesystem.
221	3. **Snapshot before swap**: before the mv, copy the current `/conf/config.xml` to `/conf/backup/config-<epoch>.xml`. This recreates the GUI's automatic snapshot and gives the operator a rollback target via `revertBackup` REST or the GUI history page.
222
223	Why not the GUI: it requires an authenticated CSRF-bound web form, and `multipart/form-data` upload is awkward to script. We already have an `ssh` channel and write access to `/conf/config.xml` via Ansible.
224
225	Why not the REST API: there is no upload-and-replace endpoint in core 25.7, period. `revertBackup` only references a file already under `/conf/backup/`. We could pre-stage our XML there as `config-<epoch>.xml` and call `revertBackup`, but that would skip our own atomic-write guard and still leave us with no service reconfigure (the REST call does not reboot).
226
227	Why not `keepconsole=1` semantics: our build is a virtio guest; we control the console settings via Tofu/cloud-init at boot, so we do not need to preserve the running console fields across import. If we ever switch to a hardware appliance with serial console pinning, we should re-evaluate.
228
229	VM 101 import checks:
230
231	- Capture the `<version>` field before and after import.
232	- Capture per-model migration log lines on first boot, such as `Migrated OPNsense\Foo\Bar from 1.0.0 to 1.0.1`.
233	- Treat the first-boot `set_networking_interfaces_ports` interactive prompt as a failed pre-import interface gate.
234	- Confirm pf rules are stable after the third `filter_configure_sync` pass, which is steps 14, 18, and 23 in the boot sequence above.
235
236	## What rollback design needs to know
237
238	- **Schema version drift is a one-way door under default settings.** After a reboot import, per-model migrations have written into `/conf/config.xml`. Restoring an older XML by file-swap is fine on disk, but the next reboot will run `convert_config()` again and the older models will either (a) be migrated forward again to match this build, or (b) fail to upgrade if a downgrade-migration is missing. Test path: stage current XML, file-swap-import the older XML, reboot, observe whether the older fields parse and which models log re-migration.
239	- **GUI restore writes a backup snapshot; file-swap does not.** If we want symmetry between rollback and forward import, our rollback tool must also write `/conf/backup/config-<epoch>.xml` for every swap. Otherwise an operator looking at the GUI history sees no record of the rollback.
240	- **`flush_history` is destructive.** If the forward-import tool ever sets the equivalent of `flush_history=1`, the operator loses local history and cannot revert via the REST endpoint. Keep `flush_history` off.
241	- **`<lock>` semantics.** If any prod-shaped interface carries `<lock>1</lock>`, both the GUI mismatch check and the boot-time mismatch check skip it. A bad interface name on a locked entry will not block the reboot and will only manifest as a service-reconfigure failure later. Treat any `<lock>` in the XML as "review by hand".
242	- **The reboot-vs-hot-apply asymmetry**. Rollback without reboot must call the same `*_configure()` chain `rc.bootup` runs, in order. There is no single helper for that on `25.7`; expect to call them individually.
243	- **No transaction across services.** Once `interfaces_configure` runs and the new IPs come up, a later `plugins_configure('vpn')` failure does not roll the interfaces back. The rollback tool must be designed around "apply, observe, decide" rather than "all-or-nothing".
244
245	## Sources
246

1	# MWAN email and alert routing
2
3	Forward-looking design doc for MWAN-132. The unified routing described here lands across
4	slices A through F of that ticket. Until those slices merge to `main`, the live code
5	still has three independent email surfaces (slog `email_handler`, ifmgr `AlertManager`,
6	direct `email.Sender.Send` in watchdog) and the `internal/notify` package referenced
7	below may not exist on every branch yet. Where a path is forward-looking, it is called
8	out inline.
9
10	## Why
11
12	Email currently leaks out of three independent surfaces in [mwan/go/](../../mwan/go/). Two of them
13	bypass the per-(kind, key) state-change suppression that the ifmgr `AlertManager`
14	implements. The result on testbed is an every-five-minutes flurry of `vsock unavailable`,
15	`ops transport failed`, and `read deploy file` emails that obscures real signals. The
16	unification gives every email one chokepoint, one dedup policy, one repeat cadence, and
17	one place to migrate when the transport changes. It also unblocks the testbed-to-prod
18	parity work that gates the OPNsense 26.x upgrade (parent MWAN-13).
19
20	## Boundary
21
22	`internal/notify` defines the boundary. Forward-looking; lands in slice A.
23
24	```go
25	package notify
26
27	type Event struct {
28	    Now        time.Time
29	    Level      slog.Level
30	    Kind       string         // required, e.g. "wg-peer-stalled", "bgp-failover", "vsock-unavailable"
31	    Key        string         // optional sub-key, e.g. peer pubkey, vmid, iface
32	    Message    string         // single-line subject-friendly summary
33	    Fields     []slog.Attr    // structured body fields
34	    IsRecovery bool           // true for Resolve, false for Notify
35	}
36
37	type Notifier interface {
38	    Notify(ctx context.Context, ev Event)
39	    Resolve(ctx context.Context, kind, key, msg string, fields ...slog.Attr)
40	    Active(kind, key string) bool
41	}
42	```
43

45
46	- `internal/notify/notify.go`: types, `Notifier` interface, `New(cfg, log, sender)` constructor.
47	- `internal/notify/manager.go`: concrete `Manager` with per-(kind, key) `active`, `lastEmit`, `lastLevel` plus `RepeatResolver`.
48	- `internal/notify/body.go`: `BuildEmailBody`, moved from `internal/logging/body.go`.
49	- `internal/notify/email.go`: `Sink` wrapping `internal/email.Sender` plus subject prefix.
50	- `internal/notify/null.go`: `NullNotifier` for when `[email]` is unconfigured.

73
74	Two TOML blocks govern routing. The non-secret fields live in `/etc/mwan/config.toml`
75	(rendered by Ansible from [mwan/config/config.toml.j2](../../mwan/config/config.toml.j2) or
76	[mwan-failover/config.toml.j2](../../mwan-failover/config.toml.j2)). The SMTP2GO API key is injected at runtime via a
77	systemd `EnvironmentFile`.
78
79	`[email]` block, today and after MWAN-132:
80

82	[email]
83	alert_email    = "alex@goodkind.io"
84	from           = "mwan@goodkind.io"          # testbed: "mwan-testbed@goodkind.io"
85	subject_prefix = "[MWAN-vault]"              # testbed: "[MWAN-suburban]"
86	bind_iface     = "enmbrains0"                # testbed: ""

102	```

104	Env-var injection contract (MWAN-131, first instance in MWAN-132 slice F):
105
106	- Vault stores `vault_smtp2go_api_key`.
107	- Ansible renders `/etc/mwan/secrets.env` with `SMTP2GO_API_KEY=...`, mode 0640 root:root.
108	- Systemd units (`mwan-agent.service`, `mwan-ifmgr.service`, plus the lxc-116 and lxc-100
109	  service files) gain `EnvironmentFile=/etc/mwan/secrets.env`.
110	- `internal/config/config.go:332` already reads `SMTP2GO_API_KEY` from the environment
111	  when the toml field is empty, so no code change is needed for the env-var read path.
112	- Result: lxc-116 and lxc-100 render non-secret email fields from
113	  [mwan-failover/config.toml.j2](../../mwan-failover/config.toml.j2). The secret stays out of the toml.
114
115	## Failure modes
116
117	Sender error (SMTP2GO returns 5xx, network blip, bind_iface gone). The sender returns an
118	error to `notify.Manager`. The manager logs the failure to journald via its embedded
119	`slog.Logger` and leaves the per-(kind, key) `active` flag set so the next state-change
120	emits at all. Repeat-cadence still fires on the next interval; if the transport stays
121	broken, every cadence tick logs a journald error rather than spamming retry email. There
122	is no on-disk retry queue.
123
124	Manager state lost on restart. The state map (`active`, `lastEmit`, `lastLevel`) is
125	in-memory only. After a process restart, the first event of any kind/key pair always
126	emits because the manager has no record of an active alert. That is intentional: it
127	errs toward emitting after a crash rather than silently swallowing a real alert. The
128	trade-off is that planned restarts (Ansible deploy, systemd reload) can produce one
129	extra email per active condition. The journald log records `notify.Manager: starting
130	with empty state` so an operator can correlate.
131
132	Unknown kind. `notify.Notify` accepts any non-empty kind string and treats unseen kinds
133	the same as known ones: per-(kind, key) state-change suppression with the default
134	repeat cadence from `[notify].repeat_every`. There is no allow-list of kinds. The
135	journald log includes the kind on every emit so an operator can spot typos.
136
137	Sender unconfigured. If `[email]` is absent or `alert_email` is empty, `notify.New`
138	returns a `NullNotifier`. Every `Notify` and `Resolve` call is a no-op apart from a
139	journald-level log line at the event's slog level. This is the path lxc-116 and lxc-100
140	ride today (no `[email]` block); slice F adds the block on both, after which they emit
141	through the same path as the rest.
142
143	## Pointers
144
145	- Plan: [docs/MWAN-132-email-unification-plan.md](../MWAN-132-email-unification-plan.md).
146	- Parent ticket: MWAN-132.
147	- Env-var injection standard: MWAN-131.
148	- Existing state-machine source (carved into `notify` in slice A):
149	  [mwan/go/internal/ifmgr/alerts.go](../../mwan/go/internal/ifmgr/alerts.go) and
150	  [mwan/go/internal/ifmgr/alerts_test.go](../../mwan/go/internal/ifmgr/alerts_test.go).
