596	### Task 5: install redactors in main before dispatch (fail-closed)
597
598	**Files:**
599	- Modify: `scripts/cmd/configs/main.go`
600
601	- [ ] **Step 1: Add imports**
602
603	In the import block add `"sync"` and `"goodkind.io/configs/internal/redact"`. `io`, `os`, `fmt`, `errors`, `slog`, and `vault` are already imported.
604
605	- [ ] **Step 2: Replace the run function**
606
607	Order: read and validate the vault first, then install the redactors with the
608	patterns already known, then dispatch. Loading only ever logs a generic decrypt
609	error to the real stderr (never a secret value), so reading before install is
610	leak-safe and avoids a drain-startup deadlock.
611
612	```go
613	func run(args []string) error {
614		if len(args) == 0 {
615			return errors.New("usage: configs <command>")
616		}
617		command := args[0]
618		handler, ok := handlers[command]
619		if !ok {
620			return fmt.Errorf("unknown command: %q", command)
621		}
622
623		patterns, loadErr := loadSecretPatterns()
624		if loadErr != nil {
625			short, isShort := loadErr.(*shortSecretError)
626			switch {
627			case isShort && command == "set-secrets":
628				patterns = nil // set-secrets is exempt; it prints only key names.
629			case isShort:
630				fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, "configs: refusing to run: vault key %q has a value shorter than %d characters; rotate it via 'configs set-secrets'\n", short.key, redact.MinLen)
631				return short
632			default:
633				return loadErr
634			}
635		}
636
637		restore, err := installRedaction(patterns)
638		if err != nil {
639			return err
640		}
641		defer restore()
642
643		return handler(args[1:])
644	}
645	```
646
647	- [ ] **Step 3: Add the helpers at the end of the file**
648
649	```go
650	// shortSecretError marks a fail-closed validation failure. It names the key,
651	// never the value.
652	type shortSecretError struct{ key string }
653
654	func (e *shortSecretError) Error() string {
655		return fmt.Sprintf("vault key %q value shorter than %d chars", e.key, redact.MinLen)
656	}
657
658	// loadSecretPatterns reads the vault and builds redaction patterns. An absent
659	// vault or password file returns no patterns and no error, because nothing
660	// decrypts anywhere in that case. A too-short secret returns *shortSecretError.
661	func loadSecretPatterns() ([]redact.Pattern, error) {
662		passwordFile, err := vaultPassPath()
663		if err != nil {
664			return nil, nil
665		}
666		if _, statErr := os.Stat(defaultVaultFile); statErr != nil {
667			return nil, nil
668		}
669		if _, statErr := os.Stat(passwordFile); statErr != nil {
670			return nil, nil
671		}
672		values, err := vault.Values(defaultVaultFile, passwordFile)
673		if err != nil {
674			slog.Error("vault values load failed", "err", err)
675			return nil, fmt.Errorf("load vault values: %w", err)
676		}
677		patterns := make([]redact.Pattern, 0, len(values))
678		for name, value := range values {
679			if value == "" {
680				continue
681			}
682			patterns = append(patterns, redact.Pattern{Value: []byte(value), Label: name})
683		}
684		if badKey, ok := redact.Validate(patterns); !ok {
685			return nil, &shortSecretError{key: badKey}
686		}
687		return patterns, nil
688	}
689
690	// lockedWriter serializes writes to a shared real descriptor under a mutex, so
691	// the stdout and stderr redactors never interleave a partial write.
692	type lockedWriter struct {
693		mu  *sync.Mutex
694		dst *os.File
695	}
696
697	func (l *lockedWriter) Write(p []byte) (int, error) {
698		l.mu.Lock()
699		defer l.mu.Unlock()
700		return l.dst.Write(p)
701	}
702
703	// installRedaction routes os.Stdout and os.Stderr through redactors that share
704	// one mutex, so writes to the two real streams never interleave mid-write. With
705	// no patterns it is a no-op and leaves the real descriptors in place. It returns
706	// a restore func to call on exit. A pipe-creation failure is fatal: with secrets
707	// present and no way to filter, the tool must not run, so the error propagates
708	// and no command dispatches.
709	func installRedaction(patterns []redact.Pattern) (func(), error) {
710		realStdout, realStderr := os.Stdout, os.Stderr
711		if len(patterns) == 0 {
712			return func() {}, nil
713		}
714		outR, outW, err := os.Pipe()
715		if err != nil {
716			slog.Error("stdout pipe failed", "err", err)
717			return nil, fmt.Errorf("stdout pipe: %w", err)
718		}
719		errR, errW, err := os.Pipe()
720		if err != nil {
721			_ = outR.Close()
722			_ = outW.Close()
723			slog.Error("stderr pipe failed", "err", err)
724			return nil, fmt.Errorf("stderr pipe: %w", err)
725		}
726
727		var mu sync.Mutex
728		var wg sync.WaitGroup
729		drain := func(src *os.File, dst *os.File) {
730			defer wg.Done()
731			w := redact.New(&lockedWriter{mu: &mu, dst: dst}, patterns)
732			_, _ = io.Copy(w, src)
733			_ = w.Close()
734		}
735		wg.Add(2)
736		go drain(outR, realStdout)
737		go drain(errR, realStderr)
738
739		os.Stdout = outW
740		os.Stderr = errW
741
742		restore := func() {
743			os.Stdout = realStdout
744			os.Stderr = realStderr
745			_ = outW.Close()
746			_ = errW.Close()
747			wg.Wait()
748			_ = outR.Close()
749			_ = errR.Close()
750		}
751		return restore, nil
752	}
753	```
754

790		if len(args) != 1 {
791			return errors.New("usage: configs secret <key>")

[tool: Read] {"file_path":"/Users/agoodkind/Sites/configs.wt-ifmgr-scaffold/docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-07-configs-secret-redaction-hardening-design.md"}
[tool output]
1	# Configs secret-redaction hardening
2
3	## Goal
4
5	No `configs` subcommand may print a vault secret to stdout or stderr. A single,
6	generic, fail-closed redaction layer is installed once in `main` and filters all
7	output, so the protection is unbypassable for every current and future command
8	without per-command wiring. The `secret` command stops printing the value to the
9	terminal and instead writes it to a hardened temp file.
10
11	## Non-goals
12
13	- Redacting secrets the tool writes to files it manages on remote hosts (the
14	  rendered `.env`, `s3.json`); those land on the target host by design. This spec
15	  covers the tool's own stdout/stderr only.
16	- Protecting against an operator who deliberately reads the `secret` temp file
17	  and exposes it. The tool hardens perms and warns; downstream handling is the
18	  operator's responsibility.
19	- Changing how ansible logs on the remote host.
20
21	## Definitions
22
23	- "Secret value" is any non-empty value held in the vault file
24	  (`ansible/inventory/group_vars/all/vault.yml`). Detection keys off decrypted
25	  values, not names, so a secret copied into a differently named variable or
26	  embedded in a larger string is still caught.
27	- `MinLen = 16`. A non-empty secret value shorter than this cannot be redacted
28	  safely, so its presence triggers fail-closed.
29	- Placeholder is `<redacted:KEY>`, where `KEY` is the vault key whose value
30	  matched. Key names are not secret. If a value maps to more than one key, the
31	  lexicographically first key is used, deterministically.
32
33	## Architecture
34
35	Three units, each independently testable.
36
37	### 1. `internal/redact` (generic, no vault knowledge)
38
39	A streaming, multi-pattern redactor over an arbitrary `io.Writer`, backed by an
40	Aho-Corasick automaton so finding matches is a single pass independent of how
41	many secrets there are, plus an interval-merge step so overlapping secrets can
42	never leak a fragment.
43
44	- `New(dst io.Writer, patterns []Pattern) *Writer`, where a `Pattern` is a
45	  `{Value []byte, Label string}` pair. The writer replaces every covered region
46	  with `<redacted:Label>`.
47	- Construction builds the Aho-Corasick goto, failure, and output links once from
48	  all pattern values. Writing scans incoming bytes through the automaton, which
49	  reports the end position and length of every pattern occurrence.
50	- Overlap safety by merge: the occurrences are collected as `[start,end)` spans
51	  and merged when they overlap or touch, then each merged span is redacted as one
52	  unit. This is the property a plain longest-match or `bytes.ReplaceAll` lacks:
53	  when secret A's suffix is secret B's prefix and they sit adjacent, neither
54	  byte of either secret survives, because the two spans merge into one redaction.
55	  The label on a merged span is the label of its earliest-starting occurrence
56	  (ties broken by lexicographically first label) so the placeholder is
57	  deterministic.
58	- Streaming-safe: the automaton state persists across `Write` calls, and the
59	  writer holds back the trailing bytes that could still be part of an
60	  in-progress match or an unresolved merge (at most `maxPatternLen-1` bytes)
61	  until a later write or `Close` resolves them, so a secret split across two
62	  writes is still matched.
63	- An empty pattern set is a transparent passthrough.
64	- `Validate(patterns []Pattern) (badKey string, ok bool)` reports the first
65	  pattern whose non-empty value is shorter than `MinLen`, returning its label so
66	  the caller can build an error that names a key, never a value.
67
68	The package depends on nothing in this repo and is fully unit tested without a
69	vault. A test asserts the overlap case (`SECRETab` + `abVALUE` over
70	`xSECRETabVALUEx` yields no surviving `VALUE`), which a non-merging matcher
71	fails.
72
73	### 2. Secret source (vault side)
74
75	- Add `vault.Values(vaultPath, passwordFile string) (map[string]string, error)`
76	  returning the decrypted name -> value map, reusing the existing
77	  `decryptMapping`.
78	- `main` inverts that into redact `Pattern`s (value plus key label), skipping
79	  empty values, and resolves a duplicate value to its lexicographically first
80	  key.
81
82	### 3. The install point (`main.run`): read, then hide, then run
83
84	Order matters for fail-closed: the secret set is read and validated before any
85	subcommand runs, so a too-short secret or an unreadable vault stops every
86	command (including the side-effecting `deploy`) before it does any work. Reading
87	before installing the pipes is leak-safe because the load step only ever logs a
88	generic decrypt error (never a secret value) to the still-real stderr, and it
89	avoids a drain-startup deadlock that an install-first ordering would create when
90	the patterns never arrive on the fail-closed path.
91
92	1. Decrypt the vault, build `Pattern`s, and run `Validate`. This read takes a few
93	   milliseconds.
94	   - On a fail-closed result (a non-empty value shorter than `MinLen`, or an
95	     existing vault that will not decrypt): write the key-named error to stderr
96	     and exit non-zero, before installing anything or dispatching.
97	   - `set-secrets` is exempt: it reads the new value from stdin and prints only
98	     key names, so it cannot leak a value, and it is the path that rotates a
99	     too-short secret. For it, a fail-closed result is downgraded to running with
100	     an empty pattern set instead of aborting.
101	2. Install the redactors with the known patterns: replace `os.Stdout` and
102	   `os.Stderr` with the write ends of two OS pipes, and start two drain
103	   goroutines that stream each pipe through a `redact.Writer` into the saved real
104	   descriptor. The two writers share one mutex so a flush to a real descriptor is
105	   never interleaved mid-write with the other stream, preserving readable
106	   ordering. An empty pattern set is a no-op that leaves the real descriptors in
107	   place. A pipe-creation failure is fatal: with secrets present and no way to
108	   filter, the tool must not run, so the error propagates and no command
109	   dispatches.
110	3. Dispatch the subcommand. `inventory-dump` and `deploy --diff` need no
111	   command-specific code; their output and their child processes' output (via
112	   `cmd.Stdout = os.Stdout`) flow through the pipes.
113	4. On return, close the pipe write ends, wait for the drains to flush their held
114	   bytes, and restore the real descriptors so nothing is dropped or leaked.
115
116	The bespoke `inventory-dump` redaction added earlier is deleted; this layer
117	replaces it, and `InventoryDump` returns to streaming `ansible-inventory` output
118	directly.
119
120	### 4. `secret` command -> hardened temp file
121
122	`runSecret` no longer prints the value. It:
123
124	1. Creates a private temp dir in the host-native temp location
125	   (`os.MkdirTemp(os.TempDir(), "configs-secret-*")`) and chmods it `0700`.
126	2. Writes the value to a file named after the key inside that dir, chmodded
127	   `0600`. Vault keys are `vault_[A-Za-z0-9_]`, so the name is filesystem-safe.
128	3. Prints the file path and a strong, multi-line warning: plaintext on disk; do
129	   not cat, paste, log, or commit it; delete it after use.
130	4. Does not auto-delete; the caller needs to read it.
131
132	The value never reaches stdout, so the global redactor needs no carve-out for
133	`secret`; its path-and-warning output contains no secret and passes through.
134
135	## Fail-closed semantics
136
137	- Vault present and a non-empty value shorter than `MinLen`: validation fails
138	  before dispatch, the tool prints a key-named error to the real stderr and exits
139	  non-zero, for every command except `set-secrets`. Because the check precedes
140	  dispatch, a side-effecting command like `deploy` never starts.
141	- Vault present but undecryptable (wrong or missing password against an existing
142	  vault): same fail-closed path. Printing nothing is safer than risking
143	  unredacted output, and ansible would fail the same way.
144	- Vault and password file both absent: empty pattern set, tool runs normally,
145	  because nothing decrypts anywhere in that case.
146	- Teardown always flushes the redactors before process exit.
147
148	## Error handling
149
150	- New wrapped errors carry context and are logged once at their origin, per the
151	  repo log-and-wrap lint rule.
152	- No error message contains a secret value. A too-short secret is reported by its
153	  key label only.
154
155	## Testing
156
157	- `internal/redact` table-driven unit tests: single match; multi-line value; a
158	  secret split across two `Write` calls (persisted automaton state plus
159	  hold-back); overlapping secrets where one is a substring of another
160	  (leftmost-longest); duplicate value mapping to the first key label; empty
161	  pattern set passthrough; `Validate` accepting `>= MinLen`, rejecting a shorter
162	  non-empty value, and ignoring an empty value.
163	- An ordering test: concurrent stdout and stderr writes are never interleaved
164	  mid-write under the shared mutex.
165	- A fail-closed test: with a too-short secret in the vault, a dispatched command
166	  is never reached (validation returns the key-named error before dispatch).
167	- A `secret` command test: the written file is `0600`, its dir `0700`, the value
168	  is in the file, and the value is absent from stdout.
169
170	## Migration and caller impact
171
172	- No caller captures `configs secret` stdout (verified: zero invocations across
173	  scripts, Makefiles, Rakefile, and tofu), so moving the value to a file breaks
174	  no automation.
175	- `inventory-dump` output keeps its shape; secret values now render as
176	  `<redacted:KEY>` via the shared layer.
177
178	## Resolved decisions
179
180	- Mechanism: global `os.Stdout`/`os.Stderr` wrap installed in `main`.
181	- Detection: value-based, tool-wide, via an Aho-Corasick automaton that finds all
182	  occurrence spans, which are then merged so overlapping secrets cannot leak.
183	- Load timing: synchronously read and validate the vault first, then install the
184	  redactors with the known patterns, then dispatch, so fail-closed precedes any
185	  command's work and the drains never deadlock waiting for patterns.
186	- Streams: stdout and stderr redacted independently, ordering-locked by a shared
187	  mutex.
188	- Placeholder: `<redacted:KEY>`.
189	- `MinLen`: 16.
190	- Short-secret gate: fail-closed, with `set-secrets` exempt.
191	- `secret` output: host-native secure temp dir (`0700`) plus `0600` file, no
192	  auto-delete, printed path and warning.
193

1	# OpenTofu import recipe for suburban resources
2
3	This file documents how an operator brings live suburban resources under
4	OpenTofu control without recreating them. The resources already exist on
5	suburban (`hypervisor.suburban.goodkind.io`); the goal is to attach Tofu
6	state to those running objects.
7
8	The root module keeps the backend and provider configuration. Host-specific
9	resources live under child modules:
10
11	- [suburban/](./suburban/) owns the suburban testbed bridges, VMs, and LXCs.
12	- [vault/](./vault/) owns production vault resources.
13
14	The bpg/proxmox provider import IDs follow these formats:
15
16	- Network interfaces: `<node_name>:<iface>`.
17	- VMs and containers: `<node_name>/<vm_id>`.
18
19	The suburban node name is `hypervisor`.
20
21	## Prerequisites
22
23	1. `terraform.tfvars` is populated with both Proxmox API tokens
24	   (`proxmox_api_token` for vault, `suburban_proxmox_api_token` for

113	## Drift expectations
114
115	- `kvm_arguments` is intentionally absent from VM 950 and VM 101 resources.
116	  Ansible owns the live `args` values because the Proxmox API rejects token
117	  writes to that field.
118	- `initialization.user_account.keys` can change when GitHub public keys rotate.
119	  Resources ignore that field where it would otherwise create noise.
120	- `operating_system.template_file_id` on imported LXCs is informational because
121	  Proxmox does not store the original template name in `pct config`.
122	- `/etc/network/interfaces.d/testbed-masquerade.conf` and the extra routable
123	  `vmbr1` IPv6 address remain Ansible-owned sourced files.
124

[tool: Read] {"file_path":"/Users/agoodkind/Sites/configs.wt-ifmgr-scaffold/pikvm/services/README.md"}
[tool output]
1	# PiKVM systemd units
2
3	Drop-in units for the PiKVM appliance at `10.240.0.57`.
4
5	## Install
6
7	PiKVM's root filesystem is read-only by default. Remount, copy, enable, remount.
8
9	```bash
10	scp pikvm-auto-update.{service,timer} 10.240.0.57:/tmp/
11	ssh 10.240.0.57 'sudo rw \
12	  && sudo install -m 0644 /tmp/pikvm-auto-update.service /etc/systemd/system/ \
13	  && sudo install -m 0644 /tmp/pikvm-auto-update.timer   /etc/systemd/system/ \
14	  && sudo systemctl daemon-reload \
15	  && sudo systemctl enable --now pikvm-auto-update.timer \
16	  && sudo ro'
17	```
18
19	## Units
20
21	- `pikvm-auto-update.timer` fires Sun 04:00 with up to 30m jitter, and `Persistent=true` so a missed run after downtime catches up.
22	- `pikvm-auto-update.service` runs `/usr/bin/pikvm-update`, which reboots when packages require it.
23

Behavior is unchanged; this is a pure refactor that de-duplicates the monitor scaffolding so the upcoming `npt` module (MWAN-207) reuses it instead of copy-pasting.\n\n## Why\n\nThe next ifmgr module (`npt`, for IPv6 NPT) needs the same \"start one panic-guarded monitor goroutine per interface and drain its events into a handler\" pattern that `wan_routes` already has inline. Extracting it into the `ifmgr` package now lets the new subpackage import it. This is the trimmed, low-risk slice of a larger shared-scaffolding refactor; the higher-churn extractions (a `baseModule` embed across all 12 modules, a shared per-WAN identity type, a generic config-build helper) are deferred and tracked as MUST-DO tickets under epic MWAN-2, because they require rewriting every `m.env`/`m.log` reference across all modules (Go does not promote unexported fields across packages).\n\n## Change\n\nNew `ifmgr.StartIfaceMonitors(ctx, log, moduleName, ifaces, handle)` starts a `netif.NewMonitor` per interface, each drained in a panic-guarded goroutine that invokes `handle` per event and exits on ctx-cancel or channel close. `wan_routes` Init now calls it with a small `onMonitorEvent` callback that carries the previous `drainMonitor` filter-and-reconcile logic. The removed inline goroutine, recover block, and `drainMonitor` method are exactly reproduced by the helper plus callback, so the log messages and reconcile path are preserved.\n\nNote: a generic shadow-logging helper was also attempted but dropped, because the repo's `staticcheck-extra` analyzer bans generic `[]T` slice params and a non-generic version could not serve both `wan_routes` and `npt`.\n\n## Testing\n\n`make build-linux` and `make build-mwan-opnsense` pass (lint linux+freebsd, both cross-builds). ### Assistant (2026-07-06 21:13)
Definitive answer: **prod Monkeybrains gets a live DHCPv6-PD, and it uses NPT, not masquerade.** The doc line was stale, exactly as you said. Live evidence from VM 113 (`mwan`, up 18 days) just now:
- **PD delegated:** `find-pd-prefixes.sh enmbrains0` → `2607:f598:d3e8:4500::/56`, confirmed by the `networkctl` DHCPv6 lease (`Prefixes: [2607:f598:d3e8:4500::/56]`).
- **NPT is programmed** (stateless prefix translation), not masquerade:
- `iif enmbrains0 ... daddr 2607:f598:d3e8:4500::/60 dnat prefix to 3d06:bad:b01::/60`
- `oif enmbrains0 ... saddr 3d06:bad:b01::/60 snat prefix to 2607:f598:d3e8:4500::/60`
- plus the `::1` DNAT/SNAT and the `ct status dnat return` guard. No `masquerade` verb anywhere for enmbrains0.
- The PD `::1/128` (`2607:f598:d3e8:4500::1`) is bound on the interface.
Two things this also proves, which kill my earlier npt-plan assumptions:
1. **MB's PD is dynamic and has renumbered.** `mwan.env` still hardcodes `MWAN_PD_MONKEYBRAINS_PREFIX=2607:f598:d3e8:3100::/56` (stale), but the live delegation is `...4500::/56`, and the NPT rules track the **live** value from `find-pd-prefixes.sh`. So the Go `npt` module cannot use a static config prefix; it must track the live PD (the `pd_client` the MWAN-2 epic scopes). My "static-prefix v1" plan is dead.
2. `MWAN_HEALTH_EXCLUDE_WANS="monkeybrains"` — MB is excluded from health checks on prod.
So `docs/infra/mwan-layout.md:120` ("DHCPv6-PD not delegated ... NAT66 masquerade fallback active") is confirmed wrong. Fixing it now with the verified values, on its own small branch (kept off the ifmgr PR).

39	## MWAN WAN Links
40
41	| Interface | Provider | IPv4 | IPv6 | Route metric | Notes |
42	| --------- | -------- | ---- | ---- | ------------ | ----- |
43	| `enwebpass0` | Webpass | `dynamic/CGNAT (not recorded)` | `delegated /64 from provider (not recorded)` | 10 (primary) | Google Fiber. RTT to `2001:4860:4860::8888` ~2.6 ms. |
44	| `enatt0.3242` | AT&T (802.1X) | `dynamic/CGNAT (not recorded)` | Provider-delegated IPv6 from AT&T (not recorded) | 1024 (secondary) | IPv6 gateway pings fine but `ping6 8.8.8.8` is 100% loss. NPT rule or PD routing issue suspected. |
45	| `enatt0` (parent) | AT&T mgmt to ONT | `192.168.1.2/24` (link to ONT) | n/a | n/a | Untagged parent of `enatt0.3242`. Hosts the link to the AT&T ONT at `192.168.1.1`. |
46
47	## AT&T ONT access
48
49	The AT&T ONT is a Realtek-based GPON SFP ("ONT-on-a-stick", firmware
50	`V1.0-220923`) presented to MWAN as a Layer-2 device on the untagged
51	parent `enatt0`. MWAN reaches its management plane at `192.168.1.1` over
52	that link.
53
54	- Credentials: stock vendor defaults for this Humax SFP unit. Not stored in the repo. Operator memory or the Humax operator doc.
55	- SSH: dropbear 0.48, requires legacy KEX, host key, and cipher.
56	- Telnet: also open on port 23.
57
58	SSH command (from MWAN, replace `<user>` and supply the password interactively):
59
60	```bash
61	ssh -o StrictHostKeyChecking=no -o UserKnownHostsFile=/dev/null \
62	  -o KexAlgorithms=+diffie-hellman-group1-sha1 \
63	  -o HostKeyAlgorithms=+ssh-rsa \
64	  -o Ciphers=+3des-cbc \
65	  <user>@192.168.1.1
66	```
67
68	Useful binaries on the ONT: `ShowStatus`, `pondetect`, `checkomci`,
69	`omci_app`, `omcicli`, `oamcli`. Useful `/proc` entries: `/proc/omci`,
70	`/proc/fiber_debug`, `/proc/fiber_mode`, `/proc/internet_flag`. The
71	device has a small connection limit and wedges its SSH/telnet daemons
72	when hit rapidly; keep to one connection at a time and `reboot` over
73	SSH if both daemons stop responding while TCP accepts succeed.
74
75	## AT&T 802.1X chain on MWAN
76
77	The MWAN VM holds AT&T's certificates and runs `wpa_supplicant` directly,
78	with the ONT acting only as a Layer-2 EAPOL forwarder. The bring-up chain:
79
80	1. `wpa_supplicant-mwan.service` runs the supplicant against the parent
81	   `enatt0` interface using certs at
82	   `/etc/wpa_supplicant/{ca_cert,client_cert,private_key}.pem`.
83	2. On reaching the AUTHENTICATED state, `wpa-cli-action.service` writes
84	   `/run/wpa_supplicant-mwan.authenticated`.
85	3. `wpa-authenticated.path` watches that file and starts
86	   `wpa-authenticated.service`, which then starts
87	   `bringup-att-vlan.service`.
88	4. `bringup-att-vlan.sh` polls `wpa_cli status` until AUTHENTICATED, then
89	   runs `networkctl renew enatt0.3242` to trigger DHCPv4 + DHCPv6-PD on
90	   the VLAN sub-interface.
91	5. DHCPv4 yields the AT&T public address. DHCPv6-PD yields the AT&T
92	   delegated `/60` used by `update-npt.sh`.
93
94	Failure modes:
95
96	- **`wpa-authenticated.path` in `failed (unit-start-limit-hit)`**: the
97	  path triggered `bringup-att-vlan` too many times in a row at boot.
98	  Clear with `systemctl reset-failed wpa-authenticated.path` then
99	  `systemctl start wpa-authenticated.path`.
100	- **TLS handshake completes but AT&T returns `EAP-Failure`**: AT&T's
101	  RADIUS rejected our cert identity. The supplicant port may stay
102	  `Authorized` from the initial boot auth, but DHCP gets no replies
103	  because the RADIUS session is invalid. Reboot the ONT
104	  (`reboot` over SSH at `192.168.1.1`) to clear AT&T's session state;
105	  the ONT comes back in ~30s and re-presents EAPOL, triggering a fresh
106	  RADIUS session.
107	- **`Supplicant PAE state=AUTHENTICATING` with `wpa_state=COMPLETED`**:
108	  re-authentication failing in the background. Same recovery as above.
109
110	Diagnostic commands on MWAN:
111
112	```bash
113	ls -la /run/wpa_supplicant-mwan.authenticated
114	ls -la /etc/wpa_supplicant/*.pem
115	sudo wpa_cli -i enatt0 status
116	journalctl -u wpa_supplicant-mwan --no-pager --since "1 hour ago"
117	journalctl -u bringup-att-vlan --no-pager --since "1 hour ago"
118	networkctl status enatt0.3242
119	```

<!-- Generated by dotfiles from corpus. Do not edit this file directly. -->
# Babysit PR
Get this PR to a merge-ready state. Run the verification commands below, fix what is in scope, and loop until every ruleset requirement is satisfied. Babysit alone stops at merge-ready. Merge, terminal cleanup, and unresolved handoff run only when the sections below say to.
## 1. Identify the PR and read merge state
Derive `owner/repo` from `gh repo view --json nameWithOwner` or from the PR JSON.
```bash
gh pr view --json number,headRefName,baseRefName,mergeable,mergeStateStatus,reviewDecision,statusCheckRollup,isDraft
gh pr checks
```
Read `mergeable`, `mergeStateStatus`, `reviewDecision`, and `statusCheckRollup` against the ruleset requirements in step 2.
If `isDraft` is `true`, mark the PR ready for review before doing anything else, since a draft PR cannot be merged:
```bash
gh pr ready
```
A draft also shows `mergeStateStatus` of `DRAFT`, so marking it ready first lets the real merge state surface. Automated reviewers like Copilot and Bugbot do not comment on draft PRs either by default, so marking it ready is what triggers the review comments this loop then triages.
## 2. Read ruleset merge requirements for the base branch
This repo uses GitHub rulesets, not classic branch protection. Read the effective rules for the PR base branch. `gh api` auto-populates `{owner}` and `{repo}` from the current repository, but the base branch is not a `gh api` placeholder, so substitute it from `gh pr view`:
```bash
BASE=$(gh pr view --json baseRefName --jq .baseRefName)
gh api "repos/{owner}/{repo}/rules/branches/$BASE"
```
Or use `gh ruleset check --default` when the PR targets the default branch.
Parse the returned rules:
- `required_status_checks`: lists the checks that must pass before merge.
- `pull_request`: carries `required_approving_review_count`, `require_code_owner_review`, `require_last_push_approval`, and `required_review_thread_resolution`.
Only `active` rules are returned. Rules in `evaluate` or `disabled` enforcement do not gate merge.
## 3. Resolve merge conflicts
Resolve merge conflicts while preserving intent on both the PR branch and the base branch. If intents truly conflict, abort the merge and ask the user for clarification before continuing.
If `mergeStateStatus` is `BEHIND`, update the branch from base before re-checking CI, since another PR may have already fixed a failing check. When babysitting a Graphite stack in a feature worktree, restack via [graphite](../graphite/SKILL.md) (`gt restack` / `gt submit`). Never fast-forward or `git update-ref` local `refs/heads/<trunk>` if trunk is checked out in another worktree.
## 4. Triage inline review comments
Inline diff comments are separate from PR timeline comments.
List inline comments. The PR number is not a `gh api` placeholder, so substitute it from `gh pr view`:
```bash
NUM=$(gh pr view --json number --jq .number)
gh api "repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/$NUM/comments"
```
Read thread resolution state and stable thread IDs with GraphQL:
```graphql
{
repository(owner: "OWNER", name: "REPO") {
pullRequest(number: PR_NUMBER) {
reviewThreads(first: 100) {
nodes {
id
isResolved
isOutdated
path
line
comments(first: 10) {
nodes { body author { login } }
}
}
}
}
}
}
```
Filter to unresolved threads first. Read only each comment body and the minimum location needed to act. Do not dump the full JSON payload.
Automated reviewers (Copilot, Bugbot) re-comment on every push, so thread triage is recurring, not one-time. Each new push can add threads that block merge while `required_review_thread_resolution` is active. Re-read unresolved threads on every babysit loop.
Validate automated review bot comments (for example Bugbot) before acting. Fix valid points. Reply and leave the thread open when you disagree or are unsure.
## 5. Resolve threads once addressed
After a requested change is made and pushed, resolve the thread with GraphQL. REST has no resolve endpoint. Use the `PRRT_...` thread `id` from `reviewThreads`, not a comment ID.
Reply first when a short explanation helps:
```graphql
mutation {
addPullRequestReviewThreadReply(input: {
pullRequestReviewThreadId: "PRRT_..."
body: "Fixed in <commit>."
}) { comment { id } }
}
```
Then resolve:
```graphql
mutation {
resolveReviewThread(input: {threadId: "PRRT_..."}) {
thread { id isResolved }
}
}
```
Resolve only after the change is genuinely addressed. When `required_review_thread_resolution` is active in the ruleset, every required thread must be resolved before merge.
## 6. Fix CI within PR scope
Fix CI failures caused by changes within this PR's scope. Push scoped fixes and re-run `gh pr checks`.
Never edit CI workflows or unrelated code just to make failures pass. Report back when that would be required.
## 7. Loop until merge-ready
After each push, re-run steps 1 through 6 until the PR is merge-ready. Merge-ready means all of the following hold:
- Required status checks are green.
- `reviewDecision` satisfies the ruleset approval count and code-owner requirements.
- Required review threads are resolved when `required_review_thread_resolution` is active (re-check each loop).
- `mergeable` is not blocked by conflicts.
When merge-ready, stop and report that the PR is ready to merge: required checks green, review decision satisfied, and required threads resolved. When not merge-ready yet, report checks, review decision, unresolved threads, and what still blocks merge. Do not arm auto-merge or merge unless the user explicitly asks (see section 8).
When the session is ending and the PR is not merge-ready or terminal, run section 10 before stopping.
## 8. Merge when the user asks
Run this section only when the user explicitly asks to merge (for example "merge", "land", "ship", or "babysit and merge").
**Preconditions:** section 7 requirements are satisfied, or only CI time remains with no real failure and threads resolved.
**Paths:**
- **gt available** (`gt` on PATH and `gt state` output identifies the trunk branch per [graphite](../graphite/SKILL.md), or Graphite MCP loaded): follow [graphite](../graphite/SKILL.md) **Task: Merge a Graphite stack**. Dry-run then `gt merge`, or `gt submit --stack --merge-when-ready --always` when only CI is pending. Never use `gh pr merge --auto`; GitHub native auto-merge conflicts with Graphite.
- **gt unavailable and repo is not Graphite-initialized:** `gh pr merge --merge` or `--squash` per repo policy when fully green; `gh pr merge --auto` only when the sole blocker is CI time.
- **gt unavailable and repo is Graphite-initialized:** do not use `gh pr merge --auto`. Merge manually with `gh pr merge --merge` (or `--squash`) bottom-up one PR at a time after all checks pass.
Loop `gh pr view --json state` until `state` is `MERGED` or superseded `CLOSED` (see section 9). When auto-merge is armed, keep triaging new review threads on each loop.
When merge completes or the PR is superseded, run section 9.
## 9. Clean up after merged, superseded, or when the user asks
Run after section 8 completes, when babysit discovers the PR is already terminal, or when the user explicitly asks to clean up (even if the PR is still open).
**Triggers:**
- `MERGED` (normal land)
- `CLOSED` with no `mergedAt` when the work was **superseded** (another PR landed the same changes, or the user closed it after confirming the branch is obsolete)
- **User explicitly asks** to clean up branches and/or the worktree (for example "clean up", "remove the worktree", "we're done here")
Detect terminal PR state with:
```bash
gh pr view --json state,mergedAt,headRefName,baseRefName
git worktree list
```
**Cleanup sequence** (respect trunk worktree rules from [graphite](../graphite/SKILL.md) section Worktrees and trunk refs):
1. **Record** `headRefName`, feature worktree path (if any), PR `state`, and which checkout owns trunk (`git worktree list`).
2. **Remote branch:** delete only when the PR is `MERGED` or superseded `CLOSED`. When the user asked to clean up while the PR is still `OPEN`, skip remote branch deletion unless the user explicitly confirmed abandoning the PR (deleting the remote branch closes an open PR). Use `git push origin --delete <branch>` or `gh api` delete-ref when deletion is allowed.
3. **Local branch:**
- Graphite-authorized repos: `gt delete <branch>` or scoped `gt sync --no-interactive` when trunk is checked out in the same worktree and no other agents are mid-stack.
- Plain git: `git branch -d <branch>` from a checkout that is not that branch when the PR is terminal or the user confirmed abandoning an open PR (use `-D` only with explicit user approval).
4. **Reconcile trunk worktree:** from the checkout that **owns** trunk (never from a feature worktree):
```bash
git -C <trunk-worktree> fetch origin
git -C <trunk-worktree> merge --ff-only origin/<trunk>
```
Do not `git update-ref refs/heads/<trunk>` when trunk is checked out elsewhere.
5. **Remove feature worktree** when babysitting ran in a dedicated worktree and no open branches still need it:
```bash
git worktree remove <path>
```
Use `--force` only when the tree is dirty and the user approved.
**Graphite stacks:** repeat for every merged or closed branch in the stack (bottom-up order), then one trunk reconcile from the trunk-owning worktree.
Report: PR URL(s), branches deleted (remote/local), trunk commit after reconcile, worktree removed (or skipped and why).
## 10. Session end with no resolution
Run when the babysit session is ending and the PR is **not** terminal: not `MERGED`, not superseded `CLOSED`, and not merge-ready with a clear path forward. Typical signals: context compaction, the user says they are stopping for now, or an agent turn limit is imminent.
**Goal:** preserve recoverable state in git and durable memory, then remove the feature worktree so it does not linger. Do **not** delete the PR branch on remote or local in this path; the work is still in flight.
**Sequence:**
1. **Capture git state** in the feature worktree:
- If the tree is dirty, commit WIP on the PR branch with a message like `babysit handoff WIP` (stage only in-scope files; no `git add .`).
- Create a backup ref under `refs/backup/` only (never `refs/heads/`), matching split-to-prs and graphite conventions:
```bash
git update-ref "refs/backup/babysit-$(git branch --show-current | tr / -)-$(date +%s)" HEAD
```
- Push the PR branch and the backup ref to `origin` when the branch has not been pushed or the backup should survive locally-only loss:
```bash
git push -u origin HEAD
git push origin "refs/backup/babysit-..."
```
2. **Record durable memory** so a future session can resume without relying on the compaction summary. Write one handoff block with: repo, PR number and URL, branch name, worktree path, last known blockers (CI, threads, conflicts), backup ref name, and the next concrete babysit step.
| Host capability | Action |
| --- | --- |
| Cursor (`cursor_dialog` available) | Upsert a user rule titled `Babysit handoff: <owner/repo> PR #<n>` with the handoff block as `content`. List existing rules first; `update` when the title matches, otherwise `add`. |
| Cursor memory unavailable | State once that durable memory could not be saved; point the user at the backup ref and PR URL for manual recovery. |
| Other agents | The pushed branch, backup ref, and clyde transcript (per [reorient](../reorient/SKILL.md)) are the durable record; include the handoff block in the final user-visible report. |
3. **Clean up the feature worktree** only (branches stay):
```bash
git worktree remove <path>
```
Use `--force` only when the tree is dirty after the WIP commit step failed and the user approved.
Report: PR URL, branch name, backup ref, whether memory was saved, worktree path removed, and the single next step for the next babysit session.

<!-- Generated by dotfiles from corpus. Do not edit this file directly. -->

# Writing

Apply the corpus writing rules to the current task.

# Technical documentation writing

Help reviewers find the answer quickly.

## Overview

Good technical documentation feels light, precise, and easy to scan. This rule provides the model for plain language and accessibility and style guide for restrained, polished wording.

A useful document includes only details that help readers understand, verify, or ship safely.

## Write for review

Prose for review should be clear enough for a critical Apple Marketing review.

- The first sentence gives the load-bearing point.
- Each paragraph gives the reviewer one idea to evaluate.
- The prose fits the reviewer's context.
- Accessible writing keeps wording simple and concrete.
- Jargon belongs only when the reviewer needs it.
- The wording stays clear, precise, restrained, and polished.
- Each claim gives the reviewer enough context to verify it.
- Ambiguous claims should become concrete behavior.

## Structure the page

A clear page or pull request (PR) description starts with the result.

- The title names the task, topic, or change.
- The summary sentence states the behavior or qualitative result.
- The `Overview` section gives only the context needed to start.
- Each later section answers one reviewer question.
- Each task heading starts with an action verb.
- Numbered steps describe ordered work.
- Notes appear beside the step they clarify.

## Keep detail load bearing

A detail belongs when it helps the reviewer understand, verify, or ship safely.

- Nonessential context stays out of the document.
- Unasked recommendations stay out of review prose.
- Repeated detail creates drift and should become a link or disappear.
- Adjacent context belongs only when it changes risk or review.
- Implementation detail stays at the system level.
- The prose explains behavior before naming code.
- Prose should not narrate literal code.
- Code anchors appear only when they help the reader orient, not on every statement.
- The code carries line-level detail.

## Order information

The most useful information belongs before supporting detail.

- The first sentence gives the answer.
- Later sentences add limits, examples, and exceptions.
- Everyday product or system nouns introduce a concept before code names.
- Behavioral or qualitative context comes before implementation detail.
- The prose explains why behavior exists when the reason affects review.
- The pattern `This behavior changes X because Y.` keeps cause and effect visible.

## Write plain sentences

Clear sentences can stand alone.

- Each sentence has a concrete subject and a concrete verb.
- Each sentence stays under 20 words when that preserves meaning.
- Separate ideas work better as separate sentences.
- Verbose, inflated, or low-substance prose should become shorter or disappear.
- The [make-readable](../make-readable/SKILL.md) rule helps remove dense or repetitive prose.
- The [plain](../plain/SKILL.md) rule helps define unexplained labels before use.
- The [remove-emdashes](../remove-emdashes/SKILL.md) rule helps split interrupted sentences into separate thoughts.

## Write direct instructions

Direct instructions tell the reader what to do and what will happen.

- Active voice works best for most instructions.
- The word `you` can address the reader directly.
- The word `your` works when the reader owns the object.
- Imperative mood keeps steps direct.
- Irreversible results belong before the action.
- Externally visible results belong before the action.

## Choose precise words

Plain words and specific verbs make instructions easier to follow.

- The word `use` is clearer than `utilize`.
- The word `to` is clearer than `in order to`.
- The word `after` is clearer than `subsequent to`.
- Verbs such as `configure`, `delete`, `export`, and `authenticate` work well when they fit.
- A more specific verb works better than `manage`.
- A more specific verb works better than `process`.

## Preserve exact terms

System names should match the product or code.

- UI element names match the interface exactly.
- Configuration key names match the source exactly.
- Code parameter names match the source exactly.
- Capitalization matches the source exactly.
- Formatting matches the source exactly.
- Acronyms are spelled out on first use unless they are universal.

## Use action language

One interaction type should use one action verb.

- The verb `select` fits menus.
- The verb `click` fits desktop pointers.
- The verb `tap` fits touch screens.
- The verb `run` fits command lines.
- The verb `execute` fits command lines.

## Write helpful errors

Helpful errors explain the cause before the cure.

1. State what went wrong.
2. State how to fix it.

Neutral error text helps the reader recover.

- Error text states system status calmly.
- Error text keeps blame out of the message.
- Error text avoids alarmist language such as `Fatal Error!`.
- Error codes appear with a plain solution.

## Use durable links

Links work best when another local source is the stable home for the detail.

- Link text stays free of backticks.
- Local sources carry load-bearing details when possible.
- Stable local files are better than copied detail.
- Repeated detail creates drift.
- Current behavior matters more than history.
- Historical notes appear only when current work requires them.

## Document architecture as current state

Architecture docs describe the system as it is now, and link to the code or test that holds each detail, so the doc cannot drift from the code.

- One `overview.md` per area lives at `docs/<area>/overview.md`.
- A short entry pointer in `README.md` or `AGENTS.md` links to each area overview.
- Doc path segments are single words. Use paths like `docs/deadcode/overview.md`, and never use paths like `docs/dead-code/overview.md`.
- The overview states what the area does today, in present tense.
- Each statement describes current behavior first, and adds a durable doc or test link only where a reader needs to verify it.
- A behavior doc is not an index of code locations, so do not append a symbol name or file path to every statement.
- Name a code symbol or file path only when it is the shortest way to help a reader orient, never as the default.
- The enforcing test or rule is the source of truth, and the doc never copies the invariant it enforces.
- A copied detail drifts, so link to it instead of restating it.
- The doc describes what is, not how the decision was reached.
- Decision history stays out unless current work needs it.

## Examples

**Bad** (hardcoded symbol and path):

> `anthropicOverloadedClientMessage` in `internal/adapter/anthropic_provider_dispatch.go` and its test hold the enforced wording.

**Good** (behavior and contract):

> The ingress returns every upstream failure as an HTTP 400 with an `invalid_request_error` body, so the real reason reaches the chat.

**Good** (reworded, link only if truly needed):

> The ingress rewords Anthropic capacity sheds into a plain message, and a test locks that wording so it cannot regress.

Related skills: [make-readable](../make-readable/SKILL.md), [plain](../plain/SKILL.md), [remove-emdashes](../remove-emdashes/SKILL.md)

    timeout-minutes: ${{ inputs.timeout_minutes }}
    permissions:
      contents: read
    outputs:
      run: ${{ steps.decide.outputs.run }}
      changed: ${{ steps.detect.outputs.changed }}
      releases: ${{ steps.release-detect.outputs.releases }}
    steps:
      # fetch-depth 0 so the detector can diff against github.event.before on the
      # default branch and compute merge-base against origin/<default> on feature
      # branches.
      - uses: actions/checkout@v7
        with:
          submodules: false
          fetch-depth: 0
      - uses: actions/setup-go@v6
        with:
          go-version-file: ${{ inputs.go_version_file }}
          cache-dependency-path: |
            ${{ inputs.go_version_file }}
            ${{ inputs.working_directory }}/go.sum
            ${{ inputs.working_directory }}/go.work
            ${{ inputs.working_directory }}/go.work.sum
      # make ci-changed runs only the cheap detector path. The engine uses
      # `go list -e` plus declared trigger dirs, writes changed=<bool> to
      # GITHUB_OUTPUT, and any uncertainty fails safe to changed=true.
      - name: Detect Go-relevant changes
        id: detect
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
        env:
          GO_MK_DIFF_BASE: ${{ github.event.before }}
          GO_MK_DIFF_HEAD: ${{ github.sha }}
          GO_MK_DEFAULT_BRANCH: ${{ github.event.repository.default_branch }}
          GO_MK_EVENT_NAME: ${{ github.event_name }}
          GO_MK_REF_NAME: ${{ github.ref_name }}
        run: |
          if ! make ci-changed; then
            echo "ci-changed detector failed; running all gates (fail-safe)" >&2
            echo "changed=true" >> "${GITHUB_OUTPUT}"
          fi
      - name: Decide whether gates run
        id: decide
        env:
          CHANGED: ${{ steps.detect.outputs.changed }}
          SKIP_UNCHANGED: ${{ inputs.skip_unchanged }}
        run: |
          # Only skip when the detector explicitly said changed=false. An empty
          # value (the detector or its GITHUB_OUTPUT write failed) fails safe to
          # running every gate.
          if [ "${SKIP_UNCHANGED}" != "true" ] || [ "${CHANGED}" != "false" ]; then
            echo "run=true" >> "${GITHUB_OUTPUT}"
          else
            echo "run=false" >> "${GITHUB_OUTPUT}"
          fi
      # A repo that releases has a release workflow file, and the build and
      # release gates below key off this output.
      - name: Detect release configuration
        id: release-detect
        run: |
          if [ -f .github/workflows/release.yml ]; then
            echo "releases=true" >> "${GITHUB_OUTPUT}"
          else
            echo "releases=false" >> "${GITHUB_OUTPUT}"
          fi
      # Warm the generated-output cache once here, the single saver, so the
      # quality gates and the compile matrix restore it instead of each
      # regenerating. A repo with no codegen leaves generated_cache_enabled
      # false, so every step below is a no-op and this job stays cheap.
      - name: Inspect go-mk cache manifest
        id: go-mk-cache-prep
        if: steps.decide.outputs.run == 'true'
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
        run: make go-mk-cache-manifest
      - name: Install apt packages
        if: steps.decide.outputs.run == 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache-prep.outputs.generated_cache_enabled == 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux' && inputs.apt_packages != ''
        run: |
          sudo apt-get update
          sudo apt-get install -y ${{ inputs.apt_packages }}
      - name: Install Go tool packages
        if: steps.decide.outputs.run == 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache-prep.outputs.generated_cache_enabled == 'true' && inputs.go_tool_packages != ''
        run: |
          for go_tool_package in ${{ inputs.go_tool_packages }}; do
            go install "${go_tool_package}"
          done
          echo "$(go env GOPATH)/bin" >> "${GITHUB_PATH}"
      - name: Run pre-make commands
        if: steps.decide.outputs.run == 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache-prep.outputs.generated_cache_enabled == 'true' && inputs.pre_make_commands != ''
        run: ${{ inputs.pre_make_commands }}
      - name: Prepare generated submodules
        if: steps.decide.outputs.run == 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache-prep.outputs.generated_cache_requires_submodules == 'true'
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
        run: make go-mk-prepare-submodules
      - name: Build go-mk cache manifest
        id: go-mk-cache
        if: steps.decide.outputs.run == 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache-prep.outputs.generated_cache_enabled == 'true'
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
        run: make go-mk-cache-manifest
      - name: Restore generated outputs
        id: generated-cache-restore
        if: steps.decide.outputs.run == 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_enabled == 'true'
        uses: actions/cache/restore@v6
        with:
          path: ${{ steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_paths }}
          key: go-mk-generated-${{ runner.os }}-${{ runner.arch }}-${{ github.repository_id }}-${{ steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_key }}
      - name: Generate outputs on cache miss
        if: steps.decide.outputs.run == 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_enabled == 'true' && steps.generated-cache-restore.outputs.cache-hit != 'true'
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
        run: make go-mk-generate
      - name: Save generated outputs
        if: steps.decide.outputs.run == 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_enabled == 'true' && steps.generated-cache-restore.outputs.cache-hit != 'true'
        uses: actions/cache/save@v6
        with:
          path: ${{ steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_paths }}
          key: go-mk-generated-${{ runner.os }}-${{ runner.arch }}-${{ github.repository_id }}-${{ steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_key }}

  compile:
    name: Compile
    # The per-platform compile matrix. It produces this run's build artifacts,
    # which the release gate consumes. It runs once per push with the shared
    # build component. Fork pull requests are skipped because fork tokens carry
    # no secrets or id-token. The nesting depth is consumer ci.yml, then _ci.yml,
    # then _build.yml, which is three levels inside GitHub's cap.
    needs: prepare
    if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases == 'true' && (github.event_name != 'pull_request' || github.event.pull_request.head.repo.fork == false)
    uses: agoodkind/go-makefile/.github/workflows/_build.yml@main
    secrets: inherit
    with:
      cgo: true
      apt_packages: ${{ inputs.apt_packages }}
      submodules: ${{ inputs.submodules }}
      platforms: ${{ inputs.release_platforms }}
      darwin_runner: ${{ inputs.darwin_runner }}

  build:
    name: Build
    # The required build gate. On a releasing repo it rolls up the compile
    # matrix so the single go / Build check reflects compilation with one
    # uniform name across every consumer platform set; its first step fails when
    # the compile matrix did. On a repo without a release configuration it runs
    # the host make build instead. This job always runs so its named Build check
    # reports, and a skipped compile matrix (an irrelevant push or a fork pull
    # request) keeps this check green because nothing was supposed to build.
    needs: [prepare, compile]
    if: ${{ !cancelled() }}
    runs-on: ${{ inputs.runs_on }}
    timeout-minutes: ${{ inputs.timeout_minutes }}
    permissions:
      contents: read
      id-token: write
    steps:
      # A prepare failure leaves run empty, which would skip every gated step
      # below and report this required check green. Fail loudly instead so a
      # broken setup blocks merge.
      - name: Require prepare success
        if: needs.prepare.result != 'success'
        run: |
          echo "Prepare did not succeed (result: ${{ needs.prepare.result }})." >&2
          exit 1
      - name: Require compile success
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases == 'true' && (needs.compile.result == 'failure' || needs.compile.result == 'cancelled')
        run: |
          echo "Compile matrix did not succeed (result: ${{ needs.compile.result }})." >&2
          exit 1
      - if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true'
        uses: actions/checkout@v7
        with:
          submodules: ${{ inputs.submodules }}
      - name: Install apt packages
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux' && inputs.apt_packages != ''
        run: |
          sudo apt-get update
          sudo apt-get install -y ${{ inputs.apt_packages }}
      - if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true'
        uses: actions/setup-go@v6
        with:
          go-version-file: ${{ inputs.go_version_file }}
          cache-dependency-path: |
            ${{ inputs.go_version_file }}
            ${{ inputs.working_directory }}/go.sum
            ${{ inputs.working_directory }}/go.work
            ${{ inputs.working_directory }}/go.work.sum
      - name: Install ccache
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux' && inputs.apt_packages != ''
        run: |
          sudo apt-get update
          sudo apt-get install -y ccache
      - name: Restore ccache
        id: ccache-restore
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux' && inputs.apt_packages != ''
        uses: actions/cache/restore@v6
        with:
          path: ~/.ccache
          key: ccache-${{ runner.os }}-${{ runner.arch }}-${{ inputs.working_directory }}-${{ hashFiles(inputs.go_version_file, format('{0}/go.sum', inputs.working_directory), format('{0}/go.work', inputs.working_directory), format('{0}/go.work.sum', inputs.working_directory)) }}
          restore-keys: |
            ccache-${{ runner.os }}-${{ runner.arch }}-${{ inputs.working_directory }}-
      - name: Configure ccache
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux' && inputs.apt_packages != ''
        run: |
          {
            echo "CCACHE_DIR=${HOME}/.ccache"
            echo "CCACHE_BASEDIR=${GITHUB_WORKSPACE}"
            echo "CCACHE_COMPILERCHECK=content"
            echo "CCACHE_NOHASHDIR=true"
            echo "CC=ccache gcc"
            echo "CXX=ccache g++"
          } >> "${GITHUB_ENV}"
      - name: Inspect go-mk cache manifest
        id: go-mk-cache-prep
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true'
        run: make go-mk-cache-manifest
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
      - name: Prepare generated submodules
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache-prep.outputs.generated_cache_requires_submodules == 'true'
        run: make go-mk-prepare-submodules
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
      - name: Build go-mk cache manifest
        id: go-mk-cache
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache-prep.outputs.generated_cache_enabled == 'true'
        run: make go-mk-cache-manifest
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
      - name: Restore generated outputs
        id: generated-cache-restore
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_enabled == 'true'
        uses: actions/cache/restore@v6
        with:
          path: ${{ steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_paths }}
          key: go-mk-generated-${{ runner.os }}-${{ runner.arch }}-${{ github.repository_id }}-${{ steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_key }}
      - name: Install Go tool packages
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true' && inputs.go_tool_packages != ''
        run: |
          for go_tool_package in ${{ inputs.go_tool_packages }}; do
            go install "${go_tool_package}"
          done
          echo "$(go env GOPATH)/bin" >> "${GITHUB_PATH}"
      - name: Run pre-make commands
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true' && inputs.pre_make_commands != ''
        run: ${{ inputs.pre_make_commands }}
      - if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true'
        run: make build
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
      - name: Show ccache stats
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux' && inputs.apt_packages != ''
        run: ccache --show-stats || true
      - name: Save generated outputs
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_enabled == 'true' && steps.generated-cache-restore.outputs.cache-hit != 'true'
        uses: actions/cache/save@v6
        with:
          path: ${{ steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_paths }}
          key: go-mk-generated-${{ runner.os }}-${{ runner.arch }}-${{ github.repository_id }}-${{ steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_key }}
      - name: Save ccache
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases != 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux' && inputs.apt_packages != '' && steps.ccache-restore.outputs.cache-hit != 'true'
        uses: actions/cache/save@v6
        with:
          path: ~/.ccache
          key: ccache-${{ runner.os }}-${{ runner.arch }}-${{ inputs.working_directory }}-${{ hashFiles(inputs.go_version_file, format('{0}/go.sum', inputs.working_directory), format('{0}/go.work', inputs.working_directory), format('{0}/go.work.sum', inputs.working_directory)) }}

  release-package:
    name: Package
    # The per-platform package matrix. It consumes the compile artifacts and
    # signs, notarizes, archives, and attests them, throwing the archives away on
    # a dry run. Its legs roll up into the required Release (dry run) gate.
    needs: [prepare, compile]
    if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases == 'true' && (github.event_name != 'pull_request' || github.event.pull_request.head.repo.fork == false)
    permissions:
      contents: read
      id-token: write
      attestations: write
    uses: agoodkind/go-makefile/.github/workflows/_package.yml@main
    secrets: inherit
    with:
      submodules: ${{ inputs.submodules }}
      platforms: ${{ inputs.release_platforms }}

  release:
    name: Release (dry run)
    # The release dry run rolls up the package matrix and exercises the full
    # package path (sign, notarize, archive, attest) without tag or publish, so
    # a release-path regression blocks merge before it reaches the real release.
    # It is required across consumers under this one uniform name. On a repo
    # without a release configuration it does nothing and stays green.
    needs: [prepare, release-package]
    if: ${{ !cancelled() }}
    runs-on: ${{ inputs.runs_on }}
    timeout-minutes: ${{ inputs.timeout_minutes }}
    permissions:
      contents: read
    steps:
      # A prepare failure would otherwise skip the gated steps and report this
      # check green, so fail loudly on it.
      - name: Require prepare success
        if: needs.prepare.result != 'success'
        run: |
          echo "Prepare did not succeed (result: ${{ needs.prepare.result }})." >&2
          exit 1
      - name: Require release package success
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases == 'true' && (needs.release-package.result == 'failure' || needs.release-package.result == 'cancelled')
        run: |
          echo "Release package matrix did not succeed (result: ${{ needs.release-package.result }})." >&2
          exit 1
      - name: Report dry run
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && needs.prepare.outputs.releases == 'true' && needs.release-package.result == 'success'
        run: |
          echo "Release dry run succeeded: compiled, signed, archived, and attested without publishing." >> "${GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY}"

  quality:
    name: Quality / ${{ matrix.name }}
    # Gates run in parallel with the compile matrix and the release dry run,
    # depending on neither. They restore the generated cache the prepare job
    # warmed. A gate failure blocks merge independently of the build and release
    # results.
    needs: [prepare]
    if: ${{ !cancelled() }}
    runs-on: ${{ inputs.runs_on }}
    timeout-minutes: ${{ inputs.timeout_minutes }}
    permissions:
      contents: read
    strategy:
      fail-fast: false
      matrix:
        include:
          - name: Vet
            command: make vet
            install_golangci_lint: false
          - name: Test
            command: make test
            install_golangci_lint: false
          - name: Golangci Lint
            command: make lint-golangci
            install_golangci_lint: true
          - name: Format
            command: make lint-format
            install_golangci_lint: true
          - name: Gocyclo
            command: make lint-gocyclo
            install_golangci_lint: false
          - name: Deadcode
            command: make lint-deadcode
            install_golangci_lint: false
          - name: Staticcheck Extra
            command: make staticcheck-extra
            install_golangci_lint: false
          - name: Govulncheck
            command: make govulncheck
            install_golangci_lint: false
          - name: Go Version
            command: make go-version-check
            install_golangci_lint: false
    steps:
      # A prepare failure would otherwise skip every gated gate step and report
      # these required checks green, so fail loudly on it.
      - name: Require prepare success
        if: needs.prepare.result != 'success'
        run: |
          echo "Prepare did not succeed (result: ${{ needs.prepare.result }})." >&2
          exit 1
      - if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true'
        uses: actions/checkout@v7
        with:
          submodules: ${{ inputs.submodules }}
      - name: Install apt packages
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux' && inputs.apt_packages != ''
        run: |
          sudo apt-get update
          sudo apt-get install -y ${{ inputs.apt_packages }}
      - if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true'
        uses: actions/setup-go@v6
        with:
          go-version-file: ${{ inputs.go_version_file }}
          cache-dependency-path: |
            ${{ inputs.go_version_file }}
            ${{ inputs.working_directory }}/go.sum
            ${{ inputs.working_directory }}/go.work
            ${{ inputs.working_directory }}/go.work.sum
      - name: Install ccache
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux' && inputs.apt_packages != ''
        run: |
          sudo apt-get update
          sudo apt-get install -y ccache
      - name: Restore ccache
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux' && inputs.apt_packages != ''
        uses: actions/cache/restore@v6
        with:
          path: ~/.ccache
          key: ccache-${{ runner.os }}-${{ runner.arch }}-${{ inputs.working_directory }}-${{ hashFiles(inputs.go_version_file, format('{0}/go.sum', inputs.working_directory), format('{0}/go.work', inputs.working_directory), format('{0}/go.work.sum', inputs.working_directory)) }}
          restore-keys: |
            ccache-${{ runner.os }}-${{ runner.arch }}-${{ inputs.working_directory }}-
      - name: Configure ccache
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux' && inputs.apt_packages != ''
        run: |
          {
            echo "CCACHE_DIR=${HOME}/.ccache"
            echo "CCACHE_BASEDIR=${GITHUB_WORKSPACE}"
            echo "CCACHE_COMPILERCHECK=content"
            echo "CCACHE_NOHASHDIR=true"
            echo "CC=ccache gcc"
            echo "CXX=ccache g++"
          } >> "${GITHUB_ENV}"
      - name: Inspect go-mk cache manifest
        id: go-mk-cache-prep
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true'
        run: make go-mk-cache-manifest
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
      - name: Prepare generated submodules
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache-prep.outputs.generated_cache_requires_submodules == 'true'
        run: make go-mk-prepare-submodules
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
      - name: Build go-mk cache manifest
        id: go-mk-cache
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache-prep.outputs.generated_cache_enabled == 'true'
        run: make go-mk-cache-manifest
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
      - name: Restore generated outputs
        id: generated-cache-restore
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_enabled == 'true'
        uses: actions/cache/restore@v6
        with:
          path: ${{ steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_paths }}
          key: go-mk-generated-${{ runner.os }}-${{ runner.arch }}-${{ github.repository_id }}-${{ steps.go-mk-cache.outputs.generated_cache_key }}
      - name: Install Go tool packages
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && inputs.go_tool_packages != ''
        run: |
          for go_tool_package in ${{ inputs.go_tool_packages }}; do
            go install "${go_tool_package}"
          done
          echo "$(go env GOPATH)/bin" >> "${GITHUB_PATH}"
      - name: Run pre-make commands
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && inputs.pre_make_commands != ''
        run: ${{ inputs.pre_make_commands }}
      - name: Install golangci-lint
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && matrix.install_golangci_lint
        uses: golangci/golangci-lint-action@v9
        with:
          version: ${{ inputs.golangci_lint_version }}
          install-only: true
      - if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true'
        run: ${{ matrix.command }}
        working-directory: ${{ inputs.working_directory }}
      - name: Show ccache stats
        if: needs.prepare.outputs.run == 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux' && inputs.apt_packages != ''
        run: ccache --show-stats || true
